601 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bogan


No. 4-88-0926


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


185 Ill. App. 3d 129; 540 N.E.2d 1135; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 973; 133 Ill. Dec. 269



June 28, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Harold L. Jensen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which sentenced him to imprisonment with no credit for time served on probation subsequent to his guilty plea on a charge of burglary, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-1 (1987).


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the terms of a plea agreement, defendant pled guilty to one count of burglary, a class two felony. The State dismissed the theft count, a class A misdemeanor. The lower court sentenced defendant to 24 months' intensive probation supervision. After the probation was subsequently revoked, defendant was sentenced to four years' imprisonment. The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court. The Illinois Supreme Court had already concluded that the burglary statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. cha. 38, para. 19-1 (1987), was not unconstitutionally broad. It allowed prosecutors the discretion to choose whether to charge a defendant with burglary, theft, or retail theft. Defendant had no constitutional right to compel his prosecution for the lesser, rather than the greater, offense. The lower court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant to four years' imprisonment. Defendant had been afforded opportunities for rehabilitation in the past, but failed to comply with even the simplest requirements of probation. Also, under Ill. Rev. Stat. Ch. 38, para. 1005-6-4(h) gave the lower court broad discretion in refusing to refuse credit for time served on probation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which revoked defendant's probation and sentenced him to four years' imprisonment with no credit for any time served on probation.

 

602 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Wenger v. Finley


No. 1-88-3778


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


185 Ill. App. 3d 907; 541 N.E.2d 1220; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 968; 133 Ill. Dec. 782



June 27, 1989  
June 27, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 23, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff litigants sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant court administrators, upon their challenge of the Illinois Not-for-Profit Dispute Resolution Center Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 851 - 856 (1987), where they argued that it violated Ill. Const. art. I § 12, art II § 1, and art. IV § 13 as well as due process and equal protection clauses.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that an alternate dispute program was not provided for nor part of the judicial system in the Illinois Constitution and that the cases a neighborhood dispute resolution center (DRC) would hear were typically not justiciable in the law courts; therefore, DRCs were not related to the judicial system. Plaintiffs also challenged the trial court's reliance on the legislature's finding that a filing fee was directly related to the justice system. Defendants argued that DRCs would reduce the number of cases pending in the courts, thus shortening the amount of time it takes to reach a resolution for both those cases going to DRCs and those remaining in the court system. The court held that the trial court properly deferred to the legislature and found that DRCs were related to the operation and maintenance of the courts and that the fee was imposed for a court-related purpose, and that there was a reasonable, nonarbitrary relationship between the purpose of the Act, which is to improve the efficient administration of the court system, and the means adopted, imposing a $ 1 fee on the party "initiating the litigation."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court in favor of defendants.

 

603 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Klawitter v. Crawford


No. 1-86-3490


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


185 Ill. App. 3d 778; 541 N.E.2d 1159; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 960; 133 Ill. Dec. 721



June 26, 1989  
June 26, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 28, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. D. Adolphus Rivers, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his petition to establish paternity and visitation rights pursuant to the Illinois Parentage Act of 1984, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, paras. 2501-2526 (1984), and the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 601 et seq. (1985). The circuit court granted defendant mother's motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The father alleged he was the father of the mother's child and filed a petition to establish paternity and visitation rights pursuant to the Illinois Parentage Act of 1984 (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, paras. 2501-2526 (1984), and the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 601 et seq. (1985). The mother filed a motion to dismiss, claiming the petition was barred by the two-year statute of limitations, and the circuit court granted the motion. The father appealed, challenging the retroactive application and constitutionality of the statute of limitations, and the court affirmed, holding that the action was not filed by or on behalf of the child and as it was filed more than two years after the child's birth, it was barred pursuant to the Act's statute of limitations. The court found that the time period for putative fathers to file an action was rationally related to a government purpose and did not violate equal protection, and that although the statute was applied retroactively to bar the claim, the father did not file his petition within a reasonable amount of time after the Act went into effect, and thus dismissal was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's dismissal of the father's petition to establish paternity and visitation rights, based on the mother's motion to dismiss the petition as time barred by the two-year statute of limitations.

People v. Rodarte


No. 1-86-3167


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


190 Ill. App. 3d 992; 547 N.E.2d 1256; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 958; 138 Ill. Dec. 635



June 26, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing December 4, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Jack G. Stein, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted and sentenced him for four counts of aggravated criminal assault and one count of aggravated battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of his conviction and sentencing for four counts of aggravated sexual assault under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14 (1985), and one count of aggravated battery under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-4 (1985). The court affirmed the convictions because 1) testimony by the complainant was sufficient to support the convictions; 2) defendant's conduct satisfied the statutory requirements for each offense; 3) an instruction on a lower offense was unnecessary; 4) multiple acts of equal value could have been prosecuted; 5) and a general verdict was presumed valid. However, the court modified the sentencing by stipulation of the parties for conformity with sentencing guidelines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but modified the sentencing by stipulation of the parties to conform to sentencing guidelines.

 

605 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Medina v. Taylor


Nos. 1-88-1366, 1-88-1430 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


185 Ill. App. 3d 808; 542 N.E.2d 33; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 964; 134 Ill. Dec. 33



June 26, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John P. Tully, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff drivers appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County's (Illinois) dismissal of their separate negligence actions against defendant bus drivers employed by the Chicago Transit Authority (CTA) for failure to give notice and file suit within the statutory limitations prescribed under the Metropolitan Transit Authority Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 301 et seq. (1985).


OVERVIEW: After one driver's vehicle was struck from behind by a CTA bus, she filed a notice of claim with the CTA and a civil action against the bus driver. The second driver filed suit against the bus driver who hit him after his vehicle was also struck from behind by a CTA bus. However, the second driver did not notify the CTA of his claim. The bus drivers filed motions to dismiss pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-619(a)(5) (1985) based on the drivers' failure to comply with the statutory limitations under § 41 of the Metropolitan Transit Authority Act, which required notice to be given to the CTA within six months and suit to be filed within one year from the date of injury. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the Act's limitations provisions extended to employees of the CTA. In response to the bus drivers' motion to dismiss, the drivers did not submit affidavits or any other evidence contradicting the bus drivers' assertion of the respondeat superior doctrine in their motion to dismiss. Due to the CTA's size and the threat of blind claims a rational basis existed for specialized notice and civil action limitations periods.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of the negligence actions.

 

606 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Washington


No. 2-87-1039


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


184 Ill. App. 3d 703; 540 N.E.2d 1014; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 900; 133 Ill. Dec. 148



June 21, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. Joseph M. McCarthy, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction of the offense of possession of a stolen or converted motor vehicle in violation of § 4-103(a)(1) of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-103(a)(1) (1985), rendered by a jury in the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: In view of a recent Illinois Supreme Court ruling, the court rejected defendant's contention that § 4-103(a)(1) of the Illinois Vehicle Code was unconstitutional. The failure to instruct the jury that theft required intent to permanently deprive was not error as defendant was not charged with theft, but with knowing possession of a stolen or converted motor vehicle. Whether defendant intended to permanently deprive the car's owner of its use or benefit had no bearing on the car's character as stolen property as the car was already stolen at the time he obtained possession. The trial judge did not erroneously instruct the jury on the definition of "converted" by using a legal dictionary definition as it was not substantially different from Ill. Pattern Jury Instructions, Crim. No. 23.15A (Supp. 1989). As defendant's allegations were on their face insufficient to show possible neglect of defendant's case but rather showed decisions by counsel well within the bounds of proper trial strategy, remanding for a new post-trial hearing with new counsel to investigate his ineffective assistance of counsel claim was not warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which had convicted defendant of possession of a stolen or converted motor vehicle.

 

607 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hannan


No. 1-87-2545


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


184 Ill. App. 3d 937; 540 N.E.2d 1064; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 932; 133 Ill. Dec. 198



June 21, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James M. Bailey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his petition for discharge from the custody of the department of corrections pursuant to § 9 of An Act in Relation to Sexually Dangerous Persons, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 105-9 (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted to raping two women and was charged with rape, attempt to rape, and home invasion. Defendant petitioned for commitment under the Act in Relation to Sexually Dangerous Persons and was found to be a sexually dangerous person. Defendant filed a petition seeking his discharge from prison pursuant to § 9 of the Act. The circuit court denied defendant's petition until a better release plan could be formulated. The court affirmed the denial, holding that defendant could only be released if he appeared no longer to be dangerous and only if adequate facilities were available to provide such supervision as was necessary to protect the public. Because defendant did not have a satisfactory release plan, it was appropriate for the circuit court to deny his release even though he no longer appeared to be dangerous. The court held that it was reasonable to require defendant to show by a preponderance of the evidence that the public would not be endangered during his conditional release.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's denial of defendant's petition for discharge pursuant to An Act in Relation to Sexually Dangerous Persons.

 

608 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Belton


Nos. 1-86-0757, 1-86-0758 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


184 Ill. App. 3d 1001; 540 N.E.2d 990; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 906; 133 Ill. Dec. 124



June 20, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert J. Sulski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted them of residential burglary and sentenced them to consecutive sentences for the burglary and for possession of a stolen motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of residential burglary, and before sentencing, both defendants pled guilty to an earlier charge of possession of a stolen motor vehicle. The terms of defendants' imprisonment for the burglary were set to run consecutively with their sentence for the possession charge. On appeal, defendants alleged that § 5- 8- 4(h) of the Unified Code of Corrections (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4(h) (1985)) violated due process and the doctrine of separation of powers, and that their sentences violated the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws. The court affirmed, holding that there was substantial evidence of defendants' guilt, and that defendants were adequately informed with respect to sentencing. It was stated that § 5-8-4(h) did not violate due process or the doctrine of separation of powers because it applied to defendants only after they committed the burglary, which was after the statute became effective. The court refused to consider the claim that the circuit court failed to determine the voluntariness of defendants' guilty pleas because defendants failed to file a motion to withdraw the pleas as required by Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court that convicted defendants of residential burglary and sentenced them to consecutive sentences for the burglary and for possession of a stolen motor vehicle.

 

609 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dace


No. 3-88-0575


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


184 Ill. App. 3d 1082; 540 N.E.2d 926; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 886; 133 Ill. Dec. 60



June 16, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. William R. Penn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted him of felony murder and sentenced him to natural life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The victim was shot and killed after she caught defendant stealing from her work, so defendant was ultimately convicted of felony murder. Defendant was sentenced to natural life imprisonment. On appeal, defendant alleged that because the State had appealed the reversal of his first conviction by the court, the trial court lacked jurisdiction to issue a search warrant for the seizure of impressions of defendant's teeth. But the court held that the issuance of the warrant was collateral to the issues that were pending in the State's appeal. The court further held that the trial court properly limited defense counsel's cross-examination of a State's witness because the elicited impeachment testimony was likely to confuse the jury. The court also held that the trial court properly sentenced defendant to natural life imprisonment in light of his subsequent criminal charges. Finally, the court held that the mittimus needed to be corrected to reflect that defendant had been convicted of felony murder as opposed to both murder and felony murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order from the trial court, which convicted defendant of felony murder and sentenced him to natural life imprisonment. The court remanded the case to amend the mittimus to indicate that defendant was sentenced to natural life for only the felony murder charge.

 

610 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Covelli


Nos. 2-87-0459, 2-87-0545 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


184 Ill. App. 3d 114; 540 N.E.2d 569; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 868; 132 Ill. Dec. 829



June 15, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 11, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Edward W. Kowal, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) with six counts of murder and one count of armed robbery and also in federal court on charges that arose out of the same incident. Defendant was granted his motion to dismiss the armed robbery count. The state sought review of the grant of the motion, and defendant sought review of the denial of the motion to dismiss the remaining counts.


OVERVIEW: The court first held that defendant's motion to dismiss was timely filed. The court held the trial court had the discretion to extend the time for filing in light of the facts that defendant had three different attorneys and was in the process of obtaining transcripts from the federal proceedings. The court next concluded that the trial court's grant of defendant's motion to dismiss the armed robbery count was not erroneous because the prosecution did not commence within the applicable the three-year statute of limitations under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 3--5(b)(1987). The court held that the federal prosecution did not toll the running of the limitations period on the state charges. The court then held that count IV of armed robbery charge was not barred on statutory double jeopardy grounds because defendant was convicted in federal court of a violation of the Hobbs Act, which included robbery. The court held to have a valid double jeopardy claim based on constitutional or statutory grounds defendant had to be charged with the same offense. The court held that the state and federal charges for armed robbery were not the same charges and affirmed the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the armed robbery count and affirmed the denial of the dismissal of the remaining counts against defendant.

 

611 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Peeples


No. 4-88-0679


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


184 Ill. App. 3d 206; 539 N.E.2d 1376; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 866; 132 Ill. Dec. 570



June 15, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Donald R. Parkinson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which dismissed his request for post-conviction relief, upon the motion of the state. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of § 5 -- 5 -- 3.2(b)(2) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005 -- 5 -- 3.2(b)(2) (1987), under which he was given an extended-term sentence for murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for sexually assaulting and murdering a teacher. The sentencing court imposed an extended-term sentence under para. 1005 -- 5 -- 3.2(b)(2) because the crime was accompanied by exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty. After exhausting his direct appeals and federal habeas corpus proceedings, defendant filed the instant challenge to the statute, alleging that it was vague and that it violated the Eighth Amendment. The court affirmed the dismissal of his petition, holding that the doctrine of res judicata applied because defendant had unsuccessfully raised the argument in prior proceedings. The court found that the exception to res judicata, the doctrine of fundamental fairness, did not apply in this case. It applied only where the right in question had been recognized for the first time after the direct appeal. The court held that the issue had been raised in other cases, rejecting defendant's claim that the cases only considered vagueness claims under the Fourteenth Amendment and did not address the merit of his Eighth amendment claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence upon his conviction for murder.

 

612 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Suhadolnik v. Springfield


Nos. 4-88-0836, 4-88-0860, 4-88-0879 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


184 Ill. App. 3d 155; 540 N.E.2d 895; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 870; 133 Ill. Dec. 29



June 15, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 14, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in 4-88-0860 and 4-88-0879; reversed and remanded in 4-88-0836 with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) order granting summary judgment to plaintiff landowner in an action contesting the constitutionality of a zoning ordinance. It alleged that the trial court erred in invalidating the ordinance and that its order was overly broad. Plaintiff appealed orders, dismissing counts based on an improper taking, U.S. Const. amend. V, and on defamation for failure to state a claim.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landowner filed an action against defendant city seeking to invalidate a zoning ordinance as unconstitutional and to recover damages for defamation. The trial court dismissed the counts alleging an illegal taking of property and defamation for failure to state a claim. It granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgment, ruling the ordinance invalid. Both sides appealed. The court affirmed the summary judgment for plaintiff, but reversed to the extent that the order was overly broad. It held that after applying the appropriate factors, the trial court correctly determined the zoning classification of the property was arbitrary and unreasonable if it failed to permit plaintiff's proposed use as a day care facility. However, upon invalidating the zoning ordinance as applied to the subject property, the trial court erred in reclassifying the zoning, rather than permitting plaintiff to develop the property as proposed. It properly dismissed the count alleging an improper taking of property under U.S. Const. amend. V because plaintiff was not deprived of all use of the land. The defamation count was correctly dismissed because the complaint lacked the requisite specificity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to plaintiff landowner in an action against defendant city to invalidate a zoning ordinance. The trial court correctly found that the ordinance, as applied to plaintiff, was arbitrary, but the order was reversed as overly broad to the extent that it rezoned the property. The court affirmed the dismissal of claims alleging an unconstitutional taking of property and for defamation.

DeLuna v. St. Elizabeth's Hosp.


Nos. 1-86-2995, 1-87-0831 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


184 Ill. App. 3d 802; 540 N.E.2d 847; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 858; 132 Ill. Dec. 925



June 13, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended September 21, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Willard J. Lassers and the Hon. Thomas R. Rakowski, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the administrator of the estate of a deceased patient (the administrator), sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his medical malpractice suit against defendants, a hospital and a doctor.


OVERVIEW: After the patient's death, the administrator filed a medical malpractice suit against defendants. However, the circuit court dismissed the suit because the administrator failed to file a report of a medical professional pursuant to Ill. Code Civ. P., 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2 -- 622, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2 -- 622 (1985). On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the circuit court's order holding that § 622 was unconstitutional because it allowed the health professional to assess the merits of the claim. The court further held that § 622 unconstitutionally delegated judicial authority to lay persons and improperly denied the administrator the right to pursue his claim against defendants. Finally, the court held that although the circuit court had dismissed the suit without prejudice to refile, the actual dismissal was prejudicial to the administrator, so the dismissal was a final and appealable order of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded an order of the circuit court, which dismissed the administrator's medical malpractice suit against defendants.

 

614 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Franzen


No. 2-87-0182


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


183 Ill. App. 3d 1051; 540 N.E.2d 548; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 841; 132 Ill. Dec. 808



June 9, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John J. Bowman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault, aggravated kidnapping, kidnapping, unlawful restraint, and aggravated battery. Defendant was sentenced to natural-life imprisonment for aggravated criminal sexual assault, as a habitual criminal offender, and received concurrent sentences of 30 and 10 years for aggravated kidnapping and aggravated battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault, aggravated kidnapping, kidnapping, unlawful restraint, and aggravated battery. Defendant was sentenced to natural-life imprisonment, without parole, for aggravated criminal sexual assault, as a habitual criminal offender and also received concurrent extended-term sentences of 30 and 10 years for the offenses of aggravated kidnapping and aggravated battery. The court affirmed the conviction, modifying the sentence for aggravated battery. The court found that the trial judge's refusal to grant a continuance when defendant retained a new attorney was proper because nothing in the record suggested that defendant was prejudiced in any manner by the refusal although he employed new counsel shortly before trial. The court held that defendant's sentence was proper. Where a defendant received a sentence of natural life, an indeterminate sentence, the trial court could also impose an extended-term sentence upon conviction of a lesser felony for which a determinant sentence was imposed where the lesser felony was accompanied by exceptionally brutal behavior indicative of wanton cruelty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for aggravated criminal sexual assault, aggravated kidnapping, kidnapping, unlawful restraint, and aggravated battery with the sentence for aggravated battery modified to a five-year concurrent term.

 

615 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gryczkowski


No. 2-88-0674


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


183 Ill. App. 3d 1064; 539 N.E.2d 1360; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 851; 132 Ill. Dec. 554



June 9, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Richard A. Lucas and the Hon. Harold D. Nagel, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which denied his petition for rescission of the summary suspension of his driving privileges, pursuant to § 2 -- 118.1 of the Illinois Vehicle Code (Code), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 2 -- 118.1 (1987). Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in failing to consider evidence that his blood-alcohol content was not 10 percent at the time he was arrested.


OVERVIEW: Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in finding that he was not entitled to rescission because the arresting officer's testimony failed to confirm the validity of the breathalyzer certification, and failed to establish the police department's compliance with testing procedures. On appeal, the court disagreed and held that the petition was properly denied. Evidence of defendant's blood-alcohol content at the time of his arrest was not required by the statutory language of the summary suspension provision contained in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11--501.1, or by the summary suspension hearing provision of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 2--118.1. Rather, the relevant time of blood-alcohol content was the time at which defendant was tested. As a result, the trial court did not err in rejecting defendant's offer of proof on that issue. Defendant also failed to meet his burden of proving a prima facie case for rescission because he offered no evidence that his breathalyzer test was improperly administered, that the machine malfunctioned, or that the results were inaccurate. Thus, the summary suspension was not against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying defendant's petition for rescission of the summary suspension of his driving privileges.

 

616 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mounson


No. 3-87-0639


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


185 Ill. App. 3d 31; 540 N.E.2d 834; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 845; 132 Ill. Dec. 912



June 9, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 13, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. John F. Michela, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant was convicted of felony murder and aggravated battery that arose out of an altercation in jail that resulted in the death of a correctional officer, defendant appealed the judgment and sentence for felony murder entered on a jury verdict by the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois), which sentenced defendant to serve concurrent terms of 35 and 5 years, respectively, in prison.


OVERVIEW: When defendant resisted correctional officers attempting to physically force him into his cell, he kicked on of the officers in the chest and he died. Defendant was convicted of felony murder and aggravated battery. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for felony murder and held that the enhanced mental state of knowingly or intentionally committing a battery of a correctional institution employee known to be engaging in his official duties, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12 -- 4(b)(6) (1985), was not less culpable than consciously disregarding a substantial risk that one's acts would result in death or great bodily harm. The court held that the restoration hearing to determine defendant's fitness to stand trial did not offend minimal due process guarantees because the trial court accepted the stipulation to the psychiatrist's report and not merely his conclusion, weighing in-court observations and the report. The court ruled that the record was based on credible and substantial evidence and the jury was entitled to accept the state's expert testimony over defendant's expert witness regarding the correctional officer's cause of death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for felony murder.

 

617 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re T.L.B.


No. 4-88-0302


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


184 Ill. App. 3d 213; 539 N.E.2d 1340; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 833; 132 Ill. Dec. 534



June 8, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Robert J. Steigmann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent minor sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which ordered the minor committed to the juvenile division of the department of corrections after the minor stipulated to having committed criminal damage to property having a value in excess of $ 300 in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 21-1(a) (1987).


OVERVIEW: The minor damaged a car by walking on the roof. Because he had had prior difficulties, the trial court committed the minor to the juvenile division of department of corrections (DOC). On appeal, the minor contended that the trial court had abused its discretion when it sentenced him to an indeterminate term because he only had two misdemeanor thefts on his record and the trial court had not considered alternatives. The minor also argued that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 805 33(2) (1987), which prohibited a trial court from imposing a determinate-term sentence to DOC upon a minor violated the equal-protection clauses of the United States and Illinois Constitutions because the it permitted the commitment of minors for a longer period of time than similarly situated adults and was not precisely tailored to serve a compelling governmental interest. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the trial court had not abused its discretion in making the commitment in light of the minor's behavioral history. Additionally, the court held that there was no equal protection violation because the law was open ended in its application and applied to all juveniles evenly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court, which committed the minor to a juvenile detention facility for an indeterminate term or until he reached 21 after the minor stipulated to having committed criminal damage to property.

 

618 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Velasco


No. 1-86-0918


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


184 Ill. App. 3d 618; 540 N.E.2d 521; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 842; 132 Ill. Dec. 781



June 8, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 13, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas J. Maloney, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed conviction for two counts of attempted murder from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), contending that he was improperly tried in absentia, plain error occurred when the jury was incorrectly instructed on the mental state necessary to commit attempted murder, he did not receive effective assistance of counsel, and improper remarks by the trial judge constituted reversible error.


OVERVIEW: Although he appeared for arraignment and was instructed to appear at trial, defendant failed to appear. The trial court granted the state's motion for bond forfeiture, issued an arrest warrant, and continued the case for two days. When defendant did not appear, trial was held in absentia and he was found guilty of the attempted murders. The trial court denied defense counsel's post trial motion, and this appeal followed. On review, the court held that as defendant was personally present in an open court when the specific trial date was set and was apprised of his rights and the consequences of failure to appear, additional notice by certified mail was not required by 38 Ill. Comp. Stat. 115/4. Continuation of the trial was merely an additional safeguard. As to jury instructions, the court held that the jury could not reasonably have acquitted defendant of one attempted murder even if properly instructed on the issue of intent. Yet, with regard to the other attempted murder, it concluded that the evidence was not so clear as to defendant's intent to kill. Thus, it did not overcome the damage of the erroneous instructions, which constituted plain error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for one attempted murder. However, it reversed the conviction for the other attempted murder and remanded this case for a new trial on that charge.

 

619 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sledge


No. 2-87-0940


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


183 Ill. App. 3d 1035; 539 N.E.2d 1312; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 814; 132 Ill. Dec. 506



June 6, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John J. Nelligan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which arose out of the kidnapping and molestation of a six-year-old girl. He was found guilty of aggravated kidnapping, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-1(a)(2) (1985), aggravated criminal sexual abuse, para 12-16(c)(1), unlawful restraint, para. 10-3(a), and residential burglary, para. 19-3(a).


OVERVIEW: The court considered defendant's arguments on appeal and ruled as follows: 1) Although defendant waived his objection to the jury venire by not raising a written objection pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 114-3(b), he still failed to prove that the jury selection process violated his Sixth or Fourteenth Amendment rights because he failed to show that the representation of the venire group was not reasonable in relation to the number of persons in the community. 2) Defendant was not prejudiced by a witness referring to his photograph in a lineup as a "booking photo" because the trial court admonished the jury to disregard the reference and no further references were made. 3) The trial court did not err in refusing to suppress defendant's oral and written statements of confession because it had the discretion to give the testimony of the interrogating officers more credibility and the officers' testimony supported the conclusion that defendant's statements were voluntary. 4) The six-year-old victim was shown to be sufficiently competent to testify to defendant's identity. 5) The state proved the elements to convict defendant of residential burglary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants convictions for aggravated kidnapping, aggravated criminal sexual abuse, unlawful restraint, and residential burglary.

 

620 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Mutual Life Ins. Co. v. Washburn


No. 4-88-0816


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


183 Ill. App. 3d 978; 539 N.E.2d 1278; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 793; 132 Ill. Dec. 472



June 1, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. C. Joseph Cavanagh, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff foreign insurer sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which denied its motion to vacate an order granting summary judgment to defendants, insurance department and state treasurer. The insurer sought a refund of retaliatory taxes paid under protest, claiming that defendants had not shown that taxes in its home state were generally more onerous than Illinois taxes on foreign insurers.


OVERVIEW: The insurance department assessed a retaliatory tax against the foreign insurer under the Illinois Insurance Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, para 1056 (1987), which the foreign insurer paid under protest. The foreign insurer claimed that the tax was improper unless Illinois domiciled insurers were more heavily burdened by the tax formula of its domiciliary state than under Illinois law. The trial court disagreed, finding that the Illinois tax law was less burdensome on some foreign insurers than the law of the foreign insurer's domiciliary state. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, finding that it was unclear whether the foreign state's tax laws were invariably or generally more onerous than Illinois taxes on foreign insurers since taxes in the foreign state were calculated under various formulas, which resulted in retaliatory taxes being assessed at rates both higher and lower rates than those imposed by Illinois. The court held that the mere possibility of a higher tax under a foreign statute that was not actually applied to Illinois insurers was not a basis for assessing a retaliatory tax.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that denied the foreign insurer's motion to vacate an order that granted the insurance director and state treasurer's motion for summary judgment in the foreign insurer's action for a refund of retaliatory taxes paid under protest. The court remanded the case for entry of a judgment in favor of the foreign insurer.

People ex rel. Kelly v. Pasko


No. 1-88-350


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


184 Ill. App. 3d 528; 540 N.E.2d 462; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 785; 132 Ill. Dec. 722



May 30, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Ellis E. Reid, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which determined that he was the father of appellee mother's child.


OVERVIEW: The mother, who was unmarried, filed a paternity complaint against the father. The trial court entered a judgment finding paternity. The trial court denied the father's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict and ordered the father to pay child support. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the mother's paternity complaint was not barred by the statute of limitations because the extended limitation period provided for in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2508 (1985) applied. The court concluded that even though the statute was enacted only after the action was filed, the limitations provided for in the statute effectuated the clearly expressed intent of the legislature to provide children born of unwed parents up to 20 years in which to enforce their right to support in a paternity action. The court also concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support a finding of paternity because even though neither the mother nor the father's testimony was corroborated, the jury observed the witnesses and chose to believe the mother. Finally, the court determined that the trial court properly allowed expert testimony as to the statistical results of the blood tests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the adjudication of paternity.

People v. Nash


No. 4-88-0291


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District

May 25, 1989, Filed

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) for indecent solicitation of a child in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-6 (1987). Additionally, defendant appealed the circuit court's order to pay restitution to the victim and the circuit court's order that he reimburse the county for the cost of his appointed defense attorney.


OVERVIEW: The parties stipulated that defendant, who was a custodian in an elementary school, wrote a note to a child asking to see her naked. The lower court convicted defendant of indecent solicitation of a child and ordered defendant to pay restitution to the victim and to pay a certain amount for the cost of his court appointed attorney. The court ruled that § 11-6 was not unconstitutionally vague because, in context, it was clear that the statute prohibited adults from soliciting children to engage in sexual practices which victimized the children. The court ruled that because the lower court reviewed defendant's affidavit and gave him the opportunity to explain his financial circumstances, the order requiring defendant to pay the county's attorney fees was valid under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 113-3.1 (1987)


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's conviction of defendant for indecent solicitation of a child, the lower court's order that defendant pay restitution to the victim, and the lower court's order that defendant reimburse the county for the cost of his appointed defense attorney.

People v. Hattery


No. 1-87-1252


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


183 Ill. App. 3d 785; 539 N.E.2d 368; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 750; 132 Ill. Dec. 58



May 19, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert V. Boharic, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's conviction for murder and armed violence was reversed and his death sentence vacated. On remand, defendant's substitution of judge motion was denied but later granted upon the issuance of a supervisory order, and another judge was assigned. Defendant appealed the denial of his motion for transfer of the case by random computer assignment and his murder conviction and sentence by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for three counts of murder and sentence of three consecutive natural life terms. The court held that: (1) the trial court properly denied the computer assignment motion because Ill. Rev. The court found that the consecutive life sentences were proper because defendant did not receive the death penalty when convicted of two or more counts of murder, his behavior was exceptionally brutal or heinous, and the public needed protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and consecutive life sentences.

People v. Melody E. (In re Marcus E.)


Nos. 1-85-2134, 1-86-2836 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


183 Ill. App. 3d 693; 539 N.E.2d 344; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 733; 132 Ill. Dec. 34



May 18, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended September 18, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Nello Gamberdino, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent parents appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, which denied the mother's motion for a new trial in petitioner State's case for wardship of the parties' children. The parents challenged the nature and extent of the evidence and the constitutionality of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, paras. 702-4(2), 705-1, 705-7 (1983), the provisions of the Juvenile Court Act upon which the removal of the children was based.


OVERVIEW: The Illinois Department of Children and Family Services, after notification of an initial complaint of possible sexual abuse, filed a petition for wardship of the parents' two children, and placed the children in foster care. The trial court entered a finding of abuse as to each child and found a substantial risk of physical injury. The parents contended the statements that the State's witnesses attributed to the children constituted uncorroborated hearsay that violated their rights to due process of law. The court found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37 para. 704-6(4)(c) (1983) did not deprive the parents of constitutional rights or violate due process. The court found the statements that the witnesses attributed to one of the children were corroborated by the child's trial testimony in chambers. The court found that, overall, the parents received a fair trial. The court found the standard of proof required only that it appear more likely than not that abuse occurred. The court held that it was satisfied that it did, that the father and mother were unable to provide a safe environment for the children, and that the trial court's findings and disposition were appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the findings of the trial court as to the father's abuse of the children, reversed the finding that the mother abused or knowingly allowed the abuse to occur, and affirmed the dispositional ruling that placed the children in foster care. The court found that the parents' rights were not terminated and one or both could regain custody at a later date.

People v. Douglas


No. 4-88-0482


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


183 Ill. App. 3d 241; 538 N.E.2d 1335; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 730; 131 Ill. Dec. 779



May 17, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing June 14, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Adams County; the Hon. Dennis K. Cashman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois), which, upon a jury verdict, convicted him of two counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault and one count of unlawful restraint, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 12-14, 10-3, respectively. Defendant also appealed his concurrent sentences of 15 years in prison on each sexual assault conviction, and three years on the unlawful restraint conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant met the victim in a bar, and later raped her in her car and in his cousin's apartment. On appeal from his convictions and sentences for aggravated criminal sexual assault and unlawful restraint, defendant raised numerous points of error. The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for several reasons. First, the victim's testimony was clear and convincing. While she was feeling the effects of the alcohol, she was not so drunk as to not be aware of what was happening. Second, defendant's threats to kill the victim and throw her body in a river, plus the injuries, including the marks to her throat, were sufficient to establish that he acted in such a manner as to threaten or endanger her life. Third, the testimony about the rape trauma syndrome and whether the victim's conduct was consistent with that of someone suffering from it would be helpful to the fact finder on the question of consent, thus, there was no error in its admission. Fourth, the tape recording of the victim's initial telephone call to the police was properly admitted as a spontaneous declaration. Finally, the trial court did not consider good-time credit as a sentencing factor.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences for aggravated criminal sexual assault and unlawful restraint were affirmed.

People v. Wendt


No. 2-87-1203


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


183 Ill. App. 3d 389; 539 N.E.2d 768; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 706; 132 Ill. Dec. 205



May 15, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County; the Hon. David A. Englund, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Boone County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of willfully failing to file an income tax return for the taxable year 1984 in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 13-1301 (1985).


OVERVIEW: The court held that the evidence was sufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant willfully failed to file a 1984 income tax return. According to the court, the evidence established that defendant was consciously aware that a failure to file his income tax return was practically certain to be caused by his conduct. The court also held that the jury was properly instructed. According to the court, all of defendant's tendered instructions were properly refused. The court determined that the jury was properly instructed as to the correct principles of law applicable to the evidence submitted to it. The court found that the information was sufficient because the information properly appraised defendant of the precise offense charged with sufficient specificity to prepare his defense and allow pleading a resulting conviction as a bar to future prosecution arising out of the same conduct. The court also held that the prosecution did not made any prejudicial comments. Finally, the court held that even if the 16th Amendment was improperly ratified, it did not affect the propriety of the tax, and the income tax on defendant's wages would pass constitutional muster.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which convicted defendant of willfully failing to file an income tax return for the taxable year of 1984.

Chambers v. Board of Election Comm'rs


No. 1-87-0992


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


183 Ill. App. 3d 567; 539 N.E.2d 267; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 704; 131 Ill. Dec. 914

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant voters sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted appellee board of election commissioners' motion to dismiss their petition contesting the results of an election.


OVERVIEW: The voters filed a petition to contest the results of an election passing an option to permit the sale of liquor by retail liquor licensees within the precinct. The board of election commissioners filed a motion to dismiss which was granted by the trial court. On appeal, the court affirmed finding that the complaint lacked sufficient specificity. The court found that the voters alleged that the entire conduct of the election was fraudulent, but failed to include the specificity required to support an election contest claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

628 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Bender v. Board of Fire & Police Comm'rs


No. 1-87-3262


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


183 Ill. App. 3d 562; 539 N.E.2d 234; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 650; 131 Ill. Dec. 881



May 10, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 21, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. George M. Marovich, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer sought review of the decision of defendant board of police commissioners to discharge him on grounds he violated Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 14 -- 2 (1985), which prohibited eavesdropping, by recording his conversation with a superior and that he disobeyed a lawful order to surrender the tape. The officer appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the board's decision.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the trial court's decision. No eavesdropping occurred where an individual to whom statements were made or directed recorded them, even without the knowledge or consent of the person making the statements, because the declarant did not intend to keep his statements private vis-a-vis that individual. In this case, the officer did not commit eavesdropping in recording his conversation with his superior because the superior was speaking to the officer. Thus, there was no lawful order to surrender the tape and no grounds for the officer's discharge. The court rejected the board's argument that, even if the officer did not commit eavesdropping, he nonetheless violated his superior's reasonable expectation of privacy in their conversation. The officer had been charged with committing the criminal offense of eavesdropping and not merely with violating or breaching a superior's reasonable expectation of privacy in confidential communications.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and entered judgment for the officer.

People v. Heim


No. 2-88-0859


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


182 Ill. App. 3d 1075; 538 N.E.2d 1259; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 644; 131 Ill. Dec. 703



May 9, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jo Daviess County; the Hon. Eric S. DeMar, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a denial of its petition for revocation of a recognizance bond from the Circuit Court of Jo Daviess County (Illinois) in a case against defendant for attempted burglary.


OVERVIEW: Prior to hearing the state's interlocutory appeal, the state filed a notice of mootness. The court agreed to pass on the constitutional issue presented pursuant to the public interest exception to the mootness doctrine. The court ruled that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 110-6(f), 110-2 (1987), which provided for appeals by the state from circuit court bail orders, unduly infringed upon a fundamental prerogative of the courts, that of regulating appeals. The court ruled that to the extent the statutes were inconsistent with the supreme court rule they were declared void.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the state's appeal, which was based on a void statute.

McCarthy v. Streit


Nos. 1-89-0127, 1-89-0705, 1-89-0706 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


182 Ill. App. 3d 1026; 538 N.E.2d 873; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 656; 131 Ill. Dec. 498



May 8, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Curtis Heaston, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed in 1 -- 89 -- 0127; judgment affirmed in 1 -- 89 -- 0706; reversed and remanded in 1 -- 89 -- 0705.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff township party candidates sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found in favor of defendant Republican Party candidates in three consolidated actions concerning the township's elections.


OVERVIEW: The Republican nominees were ordered to be placed on the ballot as the Republican candidates. The effect of that order was to deny a place on the ballot for former Republican candidates who then formed a new political party and became the township candidates. Objections were filed to their candidacies on the basis that they had participated in the Republican caucus and were therefore statutorily precluded from third party candidacy. The trial court ordered most of the township candidates removed from the ballot. On review, the court held that the trial court correctly determined that vacancies existed in the nominations for the Republican Party and that the vacancies could be filled by resolution of the Republican committeeman pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 10 -- 11, 7 -- 61 (1987). However, the trial court erred in removing the township candidates from the ballot. The court was not persuaded that the nonaction of failing to have their names withdrawn from nomination constituted "participation" under the statute and excluded the candidates from the ballot.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed as moot one of the appeals, affirmed another, and reversed and remanded the third appeal. The court held that the Republican candidates could remain on the ballot, but some of the township candidates had to be returned to the ballot.

People v. Volkmar


No. 5-87-0282


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


183 Ill. App. 3d 149; 538 N.E.2d 1255; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 677; 131 Ill. Dec. 699



May 8, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County; the Hon. Mark M. Joy, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Marion County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(2) (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder. He did not pull the trigger, but he obtained the gun and actively participated in planning the murder. The victim, suspected of being an informant by defendant and his fellow thugs, was shot in the head two or three times while facedown on the ground. Several days after the murder, defendant and the others burned the body. Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to 60 years. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. During trial, defendant's lawyer claimed he had a lawyer-client relationship with the State's witness and a social relationship with the parents of the witness and argued that the relationships would make difficult cross-examination of the witness. The court affirmed the decision of the lower court, which found that the motion was not timely, the attorney was not representing the witness in any matter at the time, the attorney did not claim a problem with confidentiality, and no actual conflict was shown. Therefore, the court stated that there was no need to attack the believability of the witness in cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the murder conviction.

 

632 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Hahnenkamp v. Madison County


No. 5-87-0606


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


183 Ill. App. 3d 76; 538 N.E.2d 1204; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 639; 131 Ill. Dec. 648



May 2, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. Michael J. Meehan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners challenged the judgment and order of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which, in their declaratory judgment action against defendants, a county, the county board's chairman, and the chairman of the county zoning board of appeals, granted plaintiffs' request for a special use permit but imposed restrictions on the use of the property, and which found the county zoning ordinance constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought a declaratory judgment action against defendants after defendants denied their application for a special use permit to open a restaurant on their property. The trial court found the county zoning ordinance constitutional, granted plaintiffs a special use permit, and imposed a restriction on the permit that at least 80 per cent of the restaurant's business had to be food service. Plaintiffs argued that the ordinance as applied to them was unconstitutionally vague and that the restrictions imposed by the trial court did not bear a real and substantial relationship to the public health, safety, morals, or general welfare and were against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in part and reversed it in part. The ordinance was constitutional. While it did not define the words "restaurant," "bar," and "nightclub," plaintiffs could read the ordinance and realize that they needed a special use permit for the establishment they envisioned. The 80 per cent food service restriction was against the manifest weight of the evidence and bore no real and substantial relation to the public health, safety, morals, or general welfare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the county zoning ordinance was constitutional and further affirmed the trial court's judgment as to the issuance of a special use permit to plaintiffs. The court reversed as to the restrictions placed on plaintiffs' special use permit.

Ross v. Kozubowski


No. 1-87-1764


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


182 Ill. App. 3d 687; 538 N.E.2d 623; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 506; 131 Ill. Dec. 248



April 20, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Eugene L. Wachowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensee appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the licensee's petition to void a local referendum regarding prohibition of retail sales of alcohol and which denied the licensee's motion for leave to file an amended petition against defendants, city clerk and others.


OVERVIEW: The licensee operated the only retail liquor business in his precinct. After a petition was circulated, notice of the election was made by publication, and the electorate voted to prohibit the retail sale of liquor in the licensee's precinct. The licensee filed a petition against the city clerk and others to void the referendum, alleging that the petition contained misrepresentations, that proponents of the proposition had engaged in fraud and electioneering, and claiming that due process required actual notice of the election. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss, and denied the licensee's motions for reconsideration and for leave to amend. The court affirmed, holding that the counts of misrepresentation were not timely filed under § 9-4 of the Liquor Control Act of 1934 and held that the lack of actual notice did not constitute a denial of due process. The court held that the licensee had failed to file a legally sufficient petition within the 30 days prescribed by § 23-24 of the Election Code, and consequently, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the licensee's motion to amend.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the licensee's petition to void a local referendum regarding prohibition of retail sales of alcohol and denying the licensee's motion for leave to file an amended petition.

 

634 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Myers


No. 4-88-0713


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


181 Ill. App. 3d 769; 537 N.E.2d 1089; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 508; 130 Ill. Dec. 760



April 20, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. Keith E. Campbell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 12--14, 12--16 (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse for having sexual intercourse, having oral sex, and fondling with his nine-year-old ex-stepdaughter. The court affirmed the convictions, and held that defendant had no standing to challenge the constitutionality of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-13, because § 12-13 was not involved with his charge of violating Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14. The court found that defendant could not challenge § 12-14 as being overbroad on the grounds that the statute, in another situation not before the trial court, could be applied unconstitutionally to another party. The court held that the mental states of intent, knowledge, or recklessness would be implied in § 12-14. The court found no authority for defendant's position that an offense titled as "aggravated" must include all the elements of the titled underlying offense, or it would run afoul of the Due Process Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse.

 

635 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Roberts


No. 1-87-2188


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


182 Ill. App. 3d 313; 537 N.E.2d 1080; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 501; 130 Ill. Dec. 751



April 19, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Christy S. Berkos, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault and criminal sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed. On review, the court affirmed. Defendant claimed that the jury instructions were inadequate because they required defendant to prove consent beyond a reasonable doubt. However, the State's evidence sufficiently established "non-consent" beyond a reasonable doubt because, where the State proved defendant used force, it necessarily proved the victim did not consent. Moreover, even if it were error to omit the consent instruction, it was harmless error beyond a reasonable doubt. The trial court instructed the jury on the elements of aggravated criminal sexual assault and on the defense of consent, the presumption of innocence, and the State's burden. Overall, the instructions fully and fairly defined the applicable law. Defendant was eligible for an extended-term sentence because he previously was convicted of rape and aggravated kidnapping. There was no double enhancement where "bodily harm" was an element of the offense because the aggravating factor for sentencing purposes required "serious harm" under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 1005 -- 5 -- 3.2(a)(1) (1987).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault and criminal sexual assault.

 

636 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Easa v. Group III Promotions


No. 1-88-1399


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


182 Ill. App. 3d 297; 537 N.E.2d 1063; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 493; 130 Ill. Dec. 734



April 18, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas E. Hoffman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed with prejudice plaintiff's complaint that sought damages for personal injuries against defendant driver. Plaintiff asserted that the trial court erred in considering her activities prior to the running of the statute of limitations in ruling on defendant's motion to dismiss under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 103(b), 107 Ill. 2d R. 103(b).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was injured in a car accident on March 2, 1985 and filed suit on July 31, 1985. The statute of limitations ran on March 2, 1987. Plaintiff's action was dismissed for want of prosecution, but, for reasons unknown, the trial court permitted plaintiff to nonsuit the action. Plaintiff immediately refiled the action. The summons was issued more than 24 months after plaintiff filed the original complaint and 6 months after the statute of limitations ran. The trial court granted the driver's motion to vacate for failure to use reasonable diligence to effectuate service. Plaintiff appealed, and the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that Rule 103(b), which provided that failure to exercise reasonable diligence to obtain service after the expiration of the applicable statute of limitations resulted in dismissal with prejudice, would not be disturbed on appeal absent a showing of abuse of discretion and that plaintiff failed to make such a showing. The court held that due diligence in serving process was essential to the administration of justice and that plaintiff's prompt refiling did not benefit the driver because the driver was not put on notice of the suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff's personal injury action against the driver.

 

637 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brown


No. 1-87-0108


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


184 Ill. App. 3d 277; 540 N.E.2d 782; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 416; 132 Ill. Dec. 860



March 31, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified Opinion Filed June 30, 1989. Rehearing Denied July 3, 1989 defendant's conviction for possession of a stolen motor vehicle even though there were a number of alibi witnesses, since the trial judge concluded that the testifying officer was a credible witness, and the officer was no more than 15 feet from the defendant and looked him in the eye for several seconds, under light from a nearby streetlamp, when he initially saw him at the scene of the crime.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert V. Boharic, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him under the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, par. 4 -- 103(a)(1) (1985), of possession of a stolen motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed and claimed that a tire and hubcap emblems were not "essential parts" of a vehicle, so he could not be guilty of possession of a stolen motor vehicle. On review, the court affirmed. The court found that a person exercising exclusive unexplained possession over a stolen vehicle or an essential part of a stolen vehicle had knowledge that such vehicle or essential part was stolen. Possession of the tire and hubcaps was possession of "essential parts." Moreover, where the identification of defendant was at issue, the testimony of a single witness, a police officer, was sufficient to support defendant's conviction even in the presence of alibi testimony because the witness was credible and had viewed defendant under circumstances that would permit positive identification. The test for a positive identification was whether the witness was close enough to defendant for a sufficient length of time, under circumstances that provided adequate opportunity for observation. In the instant matter, the officer was no more than 15 feet from defendant, and he looked him in the eye for several seconds, under light from a nearby street lamp.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of a stolen motor vehicle.

 

638 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Heard


No. 1-86-3007


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


181 Ill. App. 3d 943; 537 N.E.2d 883; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 419; 130 Ill. Dec. 554



March 30, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur J. Cieslik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a dismissal of an amended post-conviction petition of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied a motion for reconsideration of the amended petition, alleging that defendant was denied effective assistance of counsel because his trial attorney failed to file a motion to quash arrest and suppress statements, and that his appellate attorney failed to raise any meaningful issue on appeal of his murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction of murder and sentence to 68 years in prison was affirmed, then defendant filed a pro se petition for post-conviction relief that was denied. A private attorney filed a motion for reconsideration. The appellate court remanded the cause back to the trial court to hear the motion, which was dismissed. The court affirmed the trial court's order denying defendant's motion to reconsider the dismissal of his petition. The court held that (1) defendant failed to raise and waived the issue of trial counsel's incompetence because he had different counsel on appeal; (2) ineffective assistance of counsel was not established; (3) appellate counsel was not incompetent for raising only one issue because an attorney was not required to raise unmeritorious issues; (4) there was no conflict between the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-2.1 (1985), and Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c), 107 Ill. 2d R. 651(c) regarding an indigent's appointment of counsel; and (5) a mandatory 30-day period for dismissing a post-conviction petition did not apply to a motion for reconsideration and written findings of fact and conclusions of law were also not required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying defendant's motion to reconsider the dismissal of his amended post-conviction petition from a murder conviction and prison sentence.
