American Nat'l Bank & Trust Co. v. Skokie


No. 1-87-2532


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


181 Ill. App. 3d 189; 536 N.E.2d 926; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 372; 129 Ill. Dec. 876



March 23, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant national bank and trust company sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found that appellee municipality had complied with the standards set forth in its zoning ordinance, Village of Skokie Official Zoning Ordinance § 10.5 et seq. (1981) and that the municipality's Board of Trustees had the authority to grant appellee developer's petition for a site plan approval.


OVERVIEW: A bank and trust company filed suit against the municipality contending that the Board of Trustees had erred in overruling the Plan Commission and in granting a developer a special use permit to build a five-story office building located in the municipality's office research district, a zoning district created under the zoning ordinance. The bank and trust company contended that, under the special use provisions of the zoning ordinance, the Board was prohibited from granting site plan approval after the Commission's negative recommendation. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment for the municipality and concluded that provisions of the zoning ordinance demonstrated that the Board was the body that determined whether to grant or deny a site plan approval. The recommendations by the Commission were only advisory, and the final approval authority was vested in the Board. The court held that proper procedures were following in granting modifications to the requisites of the office research district and concluded that the bank and trust company had failed to establish that the site plan approval did not comply with the requirements of the zoning district.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment for the municipality and the conclusion that the municipality had complied with the standards set forth in its zoning ordinance when it granted a site plan approval to a developer.

 

640 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lawler


No. 4-88-0268


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


181 Ill. App. 3d 464; 536 N.E.2d 1283; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 345; 130 Ill. Dec. 72



March 23, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. Rodney A. Scott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentenced him to 15 years imprisonment, as well as an order that assessed the costs of a transcript on appeal against his bond proceeds.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the trial judge abused his discretion in finding the complaining witness competent to testify. Defendant also challenged the trial court's order assessing costs of a transcript on appeal against his bond proceeds. Upon review, the court held that the trial court improperly assessed defendant for the cost of the transcript. Because the controlling factor was the degree of intelligence, not the child's chronological age, it was irrelevant that the victim did not possess the intelligence of an average 13-year-old. The proper inquiry was what intelligence she did possess and whether she met the criteria for determining competency of a witness. Considering the totality of the complaining witness' testimony and the trend to allow testimony, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the testimony to stand. Even if the complaining witness had not testified, the overwhelming weight of the remaining evidence would have supported the verdict. Because the trial court lacked authority to seize the bond proceeds to pay for the transcript, defendant did not waive that issue by failing to object at trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for aggravated criminal sexual assault, reversed the order to pay the costs of the transcript from defendant's bond proceeds, and remanded the matter to the trial court with instructions to refund to defendant the sum of $ 48.

Herbes v. Graham


No. 2-88-0332


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


180 Ill. App. 3d 692; 536 N.E.2d 164; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 306; 129 Ill. Dec. 480



March 16, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Stephen E. Walter, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of orders from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) which disqualified their attorney and dismissed their suit against defendants, township and supervisor, for injunctive relief to restrain township officials from exercising powers and disbursing public funds to execute an open-space program on the ground the Township Open Space Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 139, para. 321 et seq. (1985) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs contended, in part, that the trial court erred in disqualifying their attorney in their case against defendants, township and supervisor, which challenged the constitutionality of Township Open Space Act (Act) Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 139, par. 321 et seq. (1985). Though plaintiffs' attorney did not provide legal services or advice to defendant township, the court found that an attorney-client relationship had formed between defendant township and the plaintiffs' attorney during an initial interview which concerned the possibility of the attorney's representation of defendant township in its open-space acquisition program. The relationship was sufficient to justify defendants' invocation of Ill. Code of Prof'l Resp. (Code) Canons 4 and 9, which required a lawyer to preserve the confidences of a client and cautioned against even the appearance of professional impropriety. As the court found that an attorney-client relationship existed, it next considered whether disqualification was required. The court found that disqualification was proper under both the Code, as well as federal cases, on the ground that the subject matter of both representations was essentially the same.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the trial court which disqualified plaintiffs' attorney and dismissed their constitutional challenge to a township open-space statute. Plaintiffs' attorney had been properly dismissed because a previous attorney-client relationship between the attorney and defendant township had been established and the subject matter of both representations had been essentially the same.

People v. White

Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert V. Boharic, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that found defendant guilty of unlawful use of weapons on school grounds and sentenced him to two years adult probation.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred in rejecting his necessity defense. Upon review of defendant's testimony, the court held that it failed to provide the defense of necessity. The court found that necessity involved the choice between two admitted evils where other optional courses of action are unavailable. Common sense precluded the conclusion that defendant's choice of action was the sole reasonable alternative available to him. Moreover, the record indicated that the trial judge was appropriately sensitive to defendant's youth in his sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawful use of weapons on school grounds and his sentence to two years adult probation.

Margolis v. Director of Dep't of Revenue


No. 1-88-1413


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


180 Ill. App. 3d 1084; 536 N.E.2d 827; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 292; 129 Ill. Dec. 777



March 15, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Roger J. Kiley, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant director challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgement in its action to have the director disclose certain information under § 2a of the Retailers' Occupation Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1987, ch. 120, par. 441a.


OVERVIEW: The director refused plaintiff's request for the information on the ground that it was exempt from disclosure under § 7(b)(iv) of the Freedom of Information Act (Illinois FOIA), Ill. Rev. Stat. 1987, ch. 116, par. 206. The trial court determined that the requested information did not fall within the exemptions under the Illinois FOIA and granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgement. Upon review, the court held that the trial court erred because it did not determine whether disclosure would have resulted in a clearly unwarranted invasion of personal privacy by balancing the appropriate factors. In making such a determination under § 7 of the Illinois FOIA, a court must balance (1) the plaintiff's interest in disclosure; (2) the public interest in disclosure; (3) the degree of the invasion of personal privacy; and (4) the availability of alternative means of obtaining the requested information. Because the trial court failed to make such a determination, the court remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to plaintiff and remanded for further proceedings.

Capodagli v. Wilson


No. 1-86-2491


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


180 Ill. App. 3d 456; 536 N.E.2d 135; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 280; 129 Ill. Dec. 451



March 10, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Charles J. Durham, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother, as administratrix of her son's estate, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered a judgment notwithstanding the verdict in favor of appellee city police chief in the mother's § 1983 action based on her son's suicide in the city jail. The mother alleged that the police chief's policies were inherently deficient procedures for detaining prisoners.


OVERVIEW: After her son's suicide in jail, the mother filed a § 1983 action alleging that the police chief's policies were deficient in allowing intoxicated prisoners to be jailed without a medical exam and without being observed at periodic intervals. After a jury found for the mother, the trial court entered a judgment notwithstanding the verdict. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the evidence so overwhelmingly favored the police chief that the verdict for the mother could not stand. The court ruled that, although he acted under color of state law, the mother failed to demonstrate that any of the police chief's policies violated the son's 14th amendment right not to be deprived of his life without due process. The court ruled that the police chief's knowledge that the son was violent, intoxicated, and disorderly was not a reason to know or suspect that his violence might become self-directed. The court found that the failure to obtain a medical exam, despite the son's intoxication, and violation of procedures to check the cells every half hour were perhaps negligent, but were not a deliberate disregard for the son's well being or safety so as to violate his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the police chief notwithstanding the verdict for the mother.

Oak Park Trust & Sav. Bank v. Mt. Prospect


No. 1-88-0565


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


181 Ill. App. 3d 10; 536 N.E.2d 763; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 254; 129 Ill. Dec. 713



March 7, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 1, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Harold A. Siegan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlords sued defendant village in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), challenging the validity and constitutionality of certain sections of the village's landlord-tenant ordinance. The trial court held the ordinance unconstitutional and invalid. The village appealed.


OVERVIEW: The village passed Mount Prospect, Ill., Ordinance 3366, § 23.1801 (1983) which regulated relations between landlords and tenants and included provisions that allowed tenants to withhold rents for building violations, charged a licensing fee, and required landlords to be licensed. The landlords sued the village, contending that the ordinance was unconstitutional, that the regulation was not a valid exercise of the village's police power, and that the license fee charged was unreasonable. The village filed an answer to the complaint and also filed a counterclaim seeking a declaratory judgment that the Ordinance was valid. The trial court held that the ordinance was unconstitutional, and thus, invalid. On appeal, the court held that the ordinance was a valid regulation and was within the ordinance's stated purpose to protect and promote the public health, safety, and welfare of its citizens. The court further found that the ordinance contained genuine regulatory provisions, the fee was valid unless unreasonable, and there had been no such showing by the landlords particularly as the fee did not even cover all the costs of regulation.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment holding the ordinance to be unconstitutional was reversed.

OVERVIEW: The court convicted defendant of criminal sexual assault. The court affirmed that conviction on appeal. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for criminal sexual assault.

650 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Lockwood v. McDaniel


No. 4-88-0353


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


180 Ill. App. 3d 13; 536 N.E.2d 80; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 425; 129 Ill. Dec. 396



February 23, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Donald R. Parkinson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which found that he was the father of appellee mother's child in a paternity action. The individual contended that the trial court erred in striking his request for a jury trial because he failed to pay a jury fee.


OVERVIEW: The individual was found indigent by the trial court and was appointed counsel pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 5--105 (1987). He requested a jury trial, but his request was stricken when he failed to pay the jury fee. The individual contended that he was not required to pay the fee pursuant to § 5--105 and that he had a guaranteed right to a trial by jury in the paternity action under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2513(b) (1987). Upon review, the court found that the individual had no constitutional right to a trial by jury in a civil proceeding to determine paternity. Further, requiring him to pay the jury fee did not result in an unconstitutional denial of due process or equal protection because no fundamental interest of the individual was gained or lost depending on the availability of a jury trial. The court found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 5--105 (1987) was only intended to provide equal access to the courts, which the individual had. It did not provide that no expenses would be borne by an indigent individual.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that found the individual was the father of the child in a paternity action.

People v. McBounds

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a decision of Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which convicted them of murder and sentenced them to incarceration for terms of 38 years and 28 years respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendants asserted that a statute authorizing the use of prior inconsistent statements was unconstitutional and that the prosecutor's closing argument was improper. The court rejected defendants' contentions, finding that the admission of prior inconsistent statements was proper because the legislature was empowered to alter rules of evidence. The court ruled that the confrontation clause was not violated by the use of prior inconsistent statements of witnesses because the witnesses testified at trial and were subject to cross-examination by defendants. The court held that defendants were not denied a fair trial as a result of the prosecutor's comments because there was evidence to support the prosecutor's contention concerning when defendants became suspects. The court noted that the trial court's finding of guilt would have been the same absent the prosecutor's remarks.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that the admission of the prior inconsistent statements of witnesses was proper because there was evidence to support the trial court's finding that the statements were not coerced and were voluntary.

 

652 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brooks


No. 4-88-0118


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


179 Ill. App. 3d 767; 534 N.E.2d 1063; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 176; 128 Ill. Dec. 618



February 16, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Robert J. Steigmann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which convicted him of violating Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(b)(2) (1987) by selling 6.9 grams of a substance containing cocaine. The trial court sentenced him to five years' imprisonment. Defendant argued that § 5-5-3(c)(2)(D) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3(c)(2)(D), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after selling cocaine to an undercover police officer. On appeal, defendant contended that there was no rational reason for punishing a person convicted of delivering over five grams of cocaine more severely than persons convicted of delivering other substances such as heroin, morphine, barbiturates, or amphetamines. He therefore argued that his punishment violated equal protection. The court disagreed and affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court noted that the legislature had wide discretion in classifying offenses and providing penalties for them. The court determined that absent a fundamental right or a suspect classification, the legislature could treat similarly situated persons differently if a rational reason existed for doing so. The court found that the legislative history of § 5-5-3(c)(2)(D) of the Code clearly established that the legislature was particularly concerned with the easy availability of cocaine. The court concluded that § 5-5-3(c)(2)(D) was constitutional. The court also found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant to five years' imprisonment rather than the minimum term of four years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction.

People v. Clemons


No. 2-87-0428


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


179 Ill. App. 3d 667; 534 N.E.2d 676; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 153; 128 Ill. Dec. 494



February 10, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. William D. Block, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Lake County (Illinois), finding him guilty but mentally ill of murder and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty but mentally ill of murder and armed robbery. Defendant appealed, arguing that placing the burden on him to prove his insanity by a preponderance of the evidence unconstitutionally shifted the burden of proof to him. The court ruled that it was constitutionally permissible to place the burden of proof on defendant to prove insanity by a preponderance of the evidence. The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant and modified the sentence, concluding that placing the burden of proving insanity on defendant and requiring that the jury be instructed to first determine whether the state met its burden of proving defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt before considering whether defendant sustained his burden of proving insanity was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant was affirmed and the sentence was modified.

People v. Casey


No. 4-88-0174


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


179 Ill. App. 3d 737; 534 N.E.2d 1036; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 146; 128 Ill. Dec. 591



February 9, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. Luther H. Dearborn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) that convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court committed reversible error by refusing his instruction on battery; and that he was denied a fair trial by the failure of the trial court to sua sponte instruct the jury that the State had the burden of proving defendant acted intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly in committing the acts alleged. Upon review, the court found that an instruction on battery was not required. There was no requirement for the State to prove specific intent under the aggravated criminal sexual assault statute and specific intent was a necessary element of battery. There is no error if a court refuses to instruct on a specific mental state even though a specific mental state is alleged in the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault.

Hansen v. Illinois Racing Bd.


No. 88-1094


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


179 Ill. App. 3d 353; 534 N.E.2d 658; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 123; 128 Ill. Dec. 476



February 8, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas R. Rakowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant racing board sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which declared Illinois Racing Board Rule 25.19, Ill. Admin. Code tit. 11, § 1325.190 (1985), unconstitutional on its face and reversed its decision suspending the occupation license of plaintiff horse trainer for refusing to consent to a search of a truck allegedly within his control at a race track.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the racing board contended that the trial court erred in finding Illinois Racing Board Rule 25.19, Ill. Admin. Code tit. 11, § 1325.190 (1985) unconstitutional on its face. In the alternative, the racing board argued that if the trial court was correct in finding the rule unconstitutional, it erred in awarding the horse trainer attorney fees and costs under § 14.1(b) of the Illinois Administrative Procedure Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 1014.1(b) (1987). Upon review, the court affirmed trial court's judgment. Ill. Admin. Code tit. 11, § 1325.190 (1985) was unconstitutional because it did not properly limit the discretion of the inspecting officers. The rule failed to set forth appropriate times for inspections or the frequency of inspections, or the proper method for choosing who is subject to a search at a given time. Another cases' holding did not indicate that the court in that case found § 1325.190 invalid or unconstitutional on its face. Therefore, the holding in that case did not preclude an award of attorney fees and costs under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 1014.1(b) (1987) in the instant case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and held that the applicable rule was unconstitutional because it did not properly limit the discretion of the inspecting officers.

Lake Forest Chateau, Inc. v. Lake Forest


No. 2-87-1176


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


178 Ill. App. 3d 917; 533 N.E.2d 1186; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 121; 128 Ill. Dec. 98



February 7, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 1, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Charles F. Scott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developer appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which granted judgment on the pleadings to defendant city in the developer's declaratory judgment action seeking a determination that certain increased building permit fees and other new fees and costs were not applicable to a townhouse development. The trial court also denied the developer's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Some property owners entered into a contract to sell land to the developer's predecessor. The contract was contingent upon the owners securing rezoning to permit a townhouse development. The city denied the owners' petition for rezoning, but the court rendered an opinion in favor of the owners that allowed the proposed use. The city adopted certain ordinances after the court's opinion but before the trial court's judgment order. The ordinances substantially increased building permit fees and imposed new fees applicable to townhouse developments. The city refused to issue a building permit to the developer until the new fees were paid. The developer brought an action against the city to recover the increase in the fees, and the trial court denied the developer's motion for summary judgment and granted the city's motion for judgment on the pleadings. The court reversed the trial court's decision with regard to the motion for judgment on the pleadings. The court held that the city improperly sought to control or affect the result of the underlying litigation after it was adjudicated by the courts, and that the developer was subject to the fees as of the time of the court's mandate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the developer's motion for summary judgment but reversed the trial court's decision that granted the city's motion for judgment on the pleadings in the declaratory judgment action.

People v. Montgomery


No. 86-2007


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


179 Ill. App. 3d 330; 534 N.E.2d 651; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 122; 128 Ill. Dec. 469



February 7, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John J. McDonnell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of mob action under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 25-1(a)(2) (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with mob action and the trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss. Defendant was convicted and challenged that conviction, alleging that the state failed to demonstrate beyond a reasonable doubt that she assembled with another in front of the restaurant to knowingly, intentionally or recklessly interfere with an arrest and that she encouraged others to do so as well. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court found that the judge, who was the trier of fact in the case, could reasonably have concluded that a crowd formed in response to defendant's shouting and joined her in yelling, "don't let him or them take that man away." He could further have inferred that defendant intended or at least knew that her exhortation to the crowd was likely to result in the interference of an arrest. The trial judge heard testimony describing the circumstances surrounding the incident and could reasonably have found that the police had not yet arrested the individual when defendant began shouting, and that the disturbance she caused did result in interference with this arrest.


OUTCOME: An order of the lower court convicting defendant for mob action was affirmed.

 

658 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Coleman


No. 83-1569


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


179 Ill. App. 3d 410; 534 N.E.2d 583; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 116; 128 Ill. Dec. 401



February 3, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 2, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Romie Palmer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted them of armed robbery and murder and sentenced them to 30 years for the armed robbery, and life for the murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of armed robbery and murder. The trial court sentenced them to 30 years for the armed robbery and life for the murder. Defendants sought review. The court held that, pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. VI, the requirement of presence of counsel at a lineup extended to any adversary judicial criminal proceedings, whether by way of formal charge, preliminary hearing, indictment, information, or arraignment. The court held that, for there to have been a valid waiver of counsel, there must have first been a complete admonition to defendants of their right to counsel and the consequences of asserting or relinquishing such right and then there must have been a knowledgeable and voluntary waiver of such right. The court held that defendants had knowingly and voluntarily waived such rights. The court held that defendants had the right to waive the jury for the separate sentencing proceeding. The court held that the trial court had not abused its discretion in failing to comply with the jury's request during deliberations for a transcript of a witness' testimony. The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendants of armed robbery and murder and sentenced them to 30 years for the robbery and life for the murder. The court held that defendants had voluntarily and knowingly waived their Sixth Amendment right to counsel and that defendants had waived the jury for the separate sentencing proceeding.

People v. Ziomek


No. 87-504


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


179 Ill. App. 3d 303; 534 N.E.2d 538; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 96; 128 Ill. Dec. 356



February 1, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Eugene E. Campion, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion for the return of illegally seized weapons and directed that the property be returned outside the borders of the City of Chicago.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested, charged with unlawful use of weapons, and charged under a city ordinance with failure to register a deadly weapon and unlawful possession of fireworks. The trial court suppressed the evidence on constitutional grounds and quashed the arrest. The trial court ruled that defendant had a property right in the guns, but that he could not lawfully possess them within the city under the city ordinance. Therefore, the trial court ordered the weapons returned to defendant outside the city. The state appealed, contending that the property was contraband per se because at the time of the seizure mere possession by defendant constituted a violation of the city ordinances. Defendant countered that a gun alone was not contraband per se. The court reversed, remanded with directions to confiscate the weapons, and held that the trial court erred in ordering the return of the weapons outside the city because the weapons constituted contraband per se. An illegally possessed weapon violating registration requirements resembles other contraband per se items such as counterfeit money and illegal narcotics.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision granting defendant's motion for return of illegally seized weapons and remanded the case with directions to the trial court to order the confiscation of the weapons and disposal of the property under the relevant local ordinance.

People v. Williams


Nos. 1-87-0060, 1-87-0187 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


182 Ill. App. 3d 598; 538 N.E.2d 564; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 79; 131 Ill. Dec. 189



January 27, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 13, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur J. Cieslik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and codefendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted the defendant of rape and the codefendant of indecent liberties with a child. Both defendants asserted that their joint representation was improper, that their counsel was incompetent, and that improper hearsay evidence was admitted at trial.


OVERVIEW: Both defendant and codefendant gave inculpatory statements to the police but, at trial, defendant claimed that his statement was not intelligently made or true while the codefendant denied making any incriminating statement. As a result, the court noted that neither could cross-examine the other about their respective states and, accordingly, there was no conflict of interest in their joint representation by one attorney. The court also noted that trial counsel's decision not to seek a severance or to file a motion to suppress either statement related to trial strategy and that such decisions did not establish ineffective assistance of counsel. With regard to the admission of a letter written by the victim, the court found that the letter's admission into evidence was not prejudicial when it was cumulative to the victim's testimony at trial and when that testimony was corroborated by the oral admissions of both defendant and codefendant.


OUTCOME: The judgments of conviction entered by the circuit court were affirmed.

In re N.F.


No. 2-87-0819


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


178 Ill. App. 3d 662; 533 N.E.2d 952; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 22; 127 Ill. Dec. 870



January 13, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of De Kalb County; the Hon. Richard D. Larson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of De Kalb County (Illinois) finding her unfit pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1501(D)(p)(1985), terminating her parental rights, and granting the Department of Children and Family Services the power to consent to the adoption of her natural child.


OVERVIEW: The mother gave birth while a resident of a mental health center where she was being treated for a mental disorder. Because of the mother's illness, the baby was taken from her at birth. Then, the baby was adjudicated a neglected and dependent minor. Later, the State filed a petition to terminate the mother's parental rights. The trial court found the mother unfit in that she failed to make reasonable progress toward the baby's return within 12 months after baby's adjudication, and in that the mother was unable to discharge her parental responsibilities due to mental illness. The court concluded that the trial court did not err in terminating the mother's parental rights due to unfitness resulting from mental illness. The court deemed the mother's arguments regarding the adoption statute's constitutionality waived, as it was not raised in the trial court.

People v. Hendrickson


No. 4-88-0487


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


178 Ill. App. 3d 152; 532 N.E.2d 1075; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1821; 127 Ill. Dec. 246



December 30, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Moultrie County; the Hon. Joseph C. Munch, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Circuit Court of Moultrie County (Illinois) on the State's charge of unlawful possession of cannabis in violation of § 4(e) of the Cannabis Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 704(e) (1985). Defendant also sought review of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of cannabis in violation of § 4(e) of the Cannabis Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 704(e) (1985). His sentence included a fine in the amount of $ 2,594.50 pursuant to § 5-9-1.1 of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-9-1.1 (1985). Defendant sought review of his conviction and sentence. The court affirmed. The court noted that § 5-9-1.1 provided for the imposition of a "street value" penalty on persons found guilty of drug-related offenses. At sentencing, the State argued that this section mandated the imposition of a fine against defendant for the full street value. Defendant maintained that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 710.1 (1985) applied instead. That section granted the trial court the discretion to set the amount of the fine, the court noted. The court approved of the trial court's adoption of the State's argument. The court held that the legislative history of ch. 56 1/2, para. 710.1 showed that the General Assembly had no intention of supplementing the mandatory requirement of § 5-9-1.1. The court also found that no double enhancement could have occurred here.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence on the State's charge of unlawful possession of cannabis.

People v. Kimbrough


No. 86-2416


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


178 Ill. App. 3d 445; 533 N.E.2d 439; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1830; 127 Ill. Dec. 567



December 30, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Philip Carey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief pursuant to the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-2.1 (1985), as unmeritorious.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of various crimes and was sentenced to prison. Petitioner filed a petition for post-conviction relief based on errors at trial. The trial court dismissed the petition as unmeritorious. On appeal, petitioner claimed that reversal was required because the trial court failed to enter the order of dismissal within 30 days of the petition's filing and docketing, thus the trial court could no longer dismiss the petition as frivolous under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-2.1 (1985). The court agreed and reversed. Filing of the order by the trial court within 30 days of the petition's filing and docketing was mandatory. Remand was required. The court rejected petitioner's claim that he was entitled to have his petition heard by the same trial judge who presided at his trial. The court held that the petition was subject to dismissal regardless of whether petitioner was represented by counsel because the petition was found to be unmeritorious.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of a petition for post-conviction relief filed by the petitioner as unmeritorious and remanded.

People v. Paine


No. 1-86-1231


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


182 Ill. App. 3d 812; 539 N.E.2d 731; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1774; 132 Ill. Dec. 168



December 27, 1988, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert L. Sklodowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's accomplice named him as a participant in a robbery after one of the victims stated that the person previously identified by the accomplice as a participant was not a participant. The accomplice gave police an address on Christiana street as defendant's address. Defendant was arrested and the victim identified him in a lineup, even though he was unable to identify him from a police photo book. The trial court denied defendant's motion to quash his arrest and evidence and found him guilty of robbery. The court affirmed. Moreover, prior to his arrest, defendant gave police his name and address, which corresponded with the name and address of the person that the accomplice alleged was a participant in the armed robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for armed robbery.

People v. Hester


No. 85-2222


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


178 Ill. App. 3d 360; 532 N.E.2d 1344; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1788; 127 Ill. Dec. 335



December 23, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified Opinion Filed January 27, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Howard Fink, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged her conviction for reckless homicide and driving a vehicle while under the influence of alcohol in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on the ground that the trial court erroneously instructed the jury that it could presume that defendant was under the influence of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving when she struck and killed a pedestrian. Defendant was found guilty of reckless homicide and driving under the influence of alcohol. On appeal, defendant claimed that the instruction given under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 1-501.2(b)(3) (1987) authorized the presumption of a necessary element of the state's case without advising the jury on the required degree of proof of the fact upon which the presumption was predicated and that the presumption instruction erroneously reduced the state's burden of proof from beyond a reasonable doubt. The court agreed. The court held that the jury was not instructed that it had to find beyond a reasonable doubt that the amount of alcohol in defendant's blood was .10 percent or more before it could presume that defendant was under the influence of alcohol. That fact was the factual predicate for the presumption of intoxication. The mandatory presumption was improper. The trial court erred when it did not instruct the jury that it had to find that the factual predicate had been proven beyond a reasonable doubt for it to presume that defendant was under the influence of alcohol. Defendant was entitled to a new trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for reckless homicide and driving a vehicle while under the influence of alcohol was reversed. The court remanded for a new trial.

Stanton v. Chicago


No. 88-1161


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


177 Ill. App. 3d 519; 532 N.E.2d 464; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1742; 126 Ill. Dec. 779



December 19, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. George M. Marovich, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff policeman filed an action against defendant city to enjoin the city form enforcing an amended retirement ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 25 - 37 (1988), that would have required his retirement and the termination of his disability status. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the policeman a temporary restraining order and the city filed an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: The city maintained that the order was actually a preliminary injunction, which should have required an evidentiary hearing to determine whether the standards for granting a preliminary were satisfied. The court affirmed the order and held that no preliminary injunction was issued. The trial court set a fixed date in the near future to have a hearing on a preliminary injunction, thus the order was not of unlimited duration. In addition, the city had yet to file an answer to the complaint so that it was impossible to adequately review the city's arguments. Because the order was only a temporary restraining order the policeman was only required to make a summary showing that the order was necessary to prevent immediate and irreparable harm and that there was no adequate remedy at law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the issuance of the temporary restraining order against the city.

 

669 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Embry


No. 4-88-0230


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


177 Ill. App. 3d 96; 531 N.E.2d 1130; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1720; 126 Ill. Dec. 503



December 15, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of De Witt County; the Hon. Stephen H. Peters, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of De Witt County (Illinois), which convicted him of child abduction, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-5(b)(10) (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of child abduction. Defendant appealed contending the child abduction statute created an impermissible mandatory rebuttable presumption with respect to an element of the offense, namely intent, which required reversal of his conviction. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and found that defendant had not established any constitutional infirmity in his conviction. There was nothing of record which supported a claim that the inference permitted by the statute was applied to defendant by the trial judge. The matter of presumptions and prima facie case were never mentioned during the bench trial, in closing arguments, or by the judge in reciting his findings of fact. To the contrary, the trial court relied on the specific content of defendant's statements to the girls in determining the State proved the requisite unlawful intent. Under the circumstances, defendant's claim that evidence of a prior incident was improperly admitted and proof of his purpose was speculative was merit.


OUTCOME: An order of the lower court convicting defendant of child abduction was affirmed.

 

670 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Goetten v. Heitzig


No. 4-88-0255


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


177 Ill. App. 3d 89; 531 N.E.2d 1126; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1723; 126 Ill. Dec. 499



December 15, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jersey County; the Hon. Claude J. Davis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant taxpayers appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Jersey County (Illinois), which refused to order any refund of real estate taxes paid under protest and assessed by plaintiff County Treasurer and Collector of Taxes.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought refund of real estate taxes paid under protest for one year's taxes. After the filing of tax objections and a hearing on the People of Illinois's application for judgment, the circuit court entered judgment against all of the taxpayers, refusing to order any refunds. The taxpayers appealed objecting to the constitutionality of Public Act 82-121, 1981 Ill. Laws 853. The taxpayers contended that they were deprived of due process, that a portion of Public Act 82-121 was unconstitutional, and that they were entitled to a complete refund of the taxes paid under protest together with interest at 5 percent per annum. The court found that the taxpayers' complaint stemmed from changed assessments. The court concluded that the administrative procedure regulating assessment challenges required a written complaint to the board of review. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 589(4) (1981). The court found that the taxpayers' objections failed to note a written complaint, stating instead their contact with the supervisor of assessments resulted in being told there was nothing local assessing officers could do regarding the assessment changes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's refusal to order a refund of real estate taxes to the taxpayers.

 

671 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Katz v. Chicago


No. 87-3425


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


177 Ill. App. 3d 305; 532 N.E.2d 322; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1695; 126 Ill. Dec. 637



December 7, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Irwin Cohen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owners of laundromats located in the City of Chicago (laudromat owners), sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), granting the motion to dismiss of defendant City of Chicago (city), in the laundromat owner's action against the city seeking a declaration that the Chicago Transaction Tax Ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 200.1 et seq. (1974), was unconstitutional as applied to them.


OVERVIEW: The laundromat owners brought an action against the city seeking a declaration that the Chicago Transaction Tax Ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 200.1 et seq. (1974), which imposed a tax on all leases of personal property, was unconstitutional as applied to them. A subsequent revenue ruling provided that use of a clothes washing machine, where the possession of the machine did not transfer, but where a charge was made for the period of use of the machine by the user, was taxable under § 200.1-2. The laundromat owners alleged that the ordinance constituted an unconstitutional service tax. The trial court granted the city's motion to dismiss and the laundromat owners appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the ordinance as applied to the laundromat owners constituted a valid tax on the rental of personal property. Because the washing machines were not merely incidental to the laundromat service, the tax was not an unconstitutional service tax. The court also found that the city was not estopped from enforcing the ordinance against the laundromat owners, and that § 200.1-2 did not limit the taxation of leased time transactions solely to leases of office-type equipment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting the city's motion to dismiss in the laundromat owner's action against the city seeking a declaration that the Chicago Transaction Tax Ordinance was unconstitutional as applied to them.

 

672 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Stark v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 88-0213


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


177 Ill. App. 3d 293; 532 N.E.2d 309; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1886; 126 Ill. Dec. 624



December 6, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 27, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for review of order of Pollution Control Board.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizen sought review of an order of respondent Illinois Pollution Control Board (IPCB), which dismissed his petition for review of the Cook County Zoning Board's decision to grant approval for a balefill proposed by respondents, county and municipalities. The IPCB relied on § 39.2(h) of the Illinois Environmental Protection Act (Act) in its dismissal of the petition.


OVERVIEW: The Board granted approval for a proposed balefill. The IPCB dismissed the citizen's petition for review of the Board's decision. On appeal, the court affirmed the IPCB's decision, holding that the citizen failed to overcome the presumption of validity of § 39.2(h). The court found that the citizen did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of the procedural designations created by the Act under the special legislation clause of the Illinois Constitution. He was not directly materially affected by the provision and was not in immediate danger of sustaining a direct injury as a result of the enforcement of the Act. The court addressed the constitutional question because the issue could recur in other actions brought by residents of the county. The court held that the distinction in § 39.2(h) for cities and counties of a certain size was not special legislation because it was rational to conclude that the environmental problems of the county and municipalities were different from those in other cities and counties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the IPCB, which dismissed the citizen's petition for review of the Board's decision to grant approval for a proposed balefill.

 

673 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hermann


No. 1-86-1437


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


180 Ill. App. 3d 939; 536 N.E.2d 706; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1688; 129 Ill. Dec. 656



December 5, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 23, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Richard Kavitt, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of two counts of delivery of 30 grams or more of a controlled substance containing cocaine in violation of § 401(a)(2) of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 401(a)(2) (1981).


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold cocaine to an undercover agent on two separate occasions. He delivered the cocaine in white envelopes. The agent initialed, dated, and sealed the white envelopes, put them in evidence envelopes, and delivered them to the crime lab analyst. The samples tested positive for cocaine. Defendant was convicted of delivery of cocaine. The court affirmed, finding that a sufficient chain of custody was established. There was no suggestion that the seals on the evidence envelopes had been tampered with before the analyst received them, the samples remained under the agent's control until he personally handed them to the analyst, and the seals were intact on both evidence envelopes when received by the analyst. In addition, there was a reasonable probability that the evidence had not been altered or contaminated in any way, even though the agent could not recall exactly where the evidence was at all times. The court also found that defendant's hypothetical questions regarding whether moisture would affect cocaine were properly restricted, as the theory was merely speculative, was beyond the scope of cross-examination, and there was no basis for his hypothetical questions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for delivery of 30 grams or more of a controlled substance containing cocaine.

People v. Hominick


No. 2-87-1065


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


177 Ill. App. 3d 18; 531 N.E.2d 1049; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1672; 126 Ill. Dec. 422



December 1, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 11, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County; the Hon. Roland A. Herrmann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence from the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) for delivery of a controlled substance, specifically cocaine, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(c) (1985) and narcotics racketeering in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1654(a) (1985). Defendant raised several issues on appeal, including, whether the chain of custody of the cocaine was sufficiently established.


OVERVIEW: After selling small amounts of cocaine to undercover police officers on several different occasions, defendant was convicted of delivery of a controlled substance and narcotics racketeering. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that (1) the state sufficiently established the chain of custody by showing that, after the cocaine was purchased from defendant, it was put in a sealed envelope, stored in either a locked file cabinet or a briefcase that only the undercover officers had access to, and then secured in an evidence locker; (2) any alleged deficiencies in the chain of custody went to the weight and not the admissibility of the evidence; (3) defendant waived any argument as to whether the trial court improperly denied defendant's motion for a directed verdict by failing to renew the motion at the close of all the evidence; (4) defendant waived any challenges to the constitutionality of the Narcotics Profit Forfeiture Act, specifically, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1652 (1985), by failing to raise the issue before the trial court; and (5) the trial court did not abuse its discretion and properly considered defendant's lack of remorse in imposing defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for delivery of a controlled substance, specifically cocaine, and narcotics racketeering.

People v. Terry


No. 85-2927


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


176 Ill. App. 3d 947; 531 N.E.2d 999; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1660; 126 Ill. Dec. 372



November 30, 1988, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested in front of the apartment building where he lived after a police officer spotted a weapon on his person. He was charged with and later convicted of unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon. On appeal, defendant claimed that the unlawful possession of firearms by felons statute was unconstitutional, but the court disagreed and upheld the statute. The court further held that defendant's prosecution under the statute did not violate his equal protection and due process rights. The court also rejected defendant's contention that the prosecutor's comments on his failure to testify required reversal because the prosecutor's statements were invited by defense counsel's remarks to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order from the trial court, which convicted defendant of unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon.

 

676 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Maller v. Cohen


Nos. 87-2199, 87-2492 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


176 Ill. App. 3d 987; 531 N.E.2d 1029; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1656; 126 Ill. Dec. 402



November 30, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Dennis Berkbigler, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a child and the Illinois Department of Public Aid (Department) sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their action to establish that appellee individual was the child's biological father.


OVERVIEW: When the child was six, her mother filed an action to establish that the individual was the child's father. Because the Illinois Paternity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, paras. 1351 through 1368 (1981), required the filing of such actions within two years of the child's birth, the mother's suit was dismissed. Subsequently, the Illinois Paternity Act was held unconstitutional. On appeal, the child and the Department argued that the trial court erred in dismissing their action. Upon review, the court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment. The mother was not acting in the child's best interest when she filed the paternity action four years late. There was no privity between the mother and the child when the mother filed the action. The child did not have a cause of action under the Illinois Paternity Act and could not have maintained an action against the individual under that Act. Therefore, § 25 of the Illinois Parentage Act could not have barred the child's action. The Department was not furnishing financial assistance to either the child or her mother in 1981. Therefore the Department had no claim against the individual and no interest in the mother's suit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court, and held that the child and the Department had the right to litigate the child's parentage, which was not barred by the prior dismissal of the mother's action.

Knapp v. Palos Community Hosp.


Nos. 84-3004, 85-0218, 85-0917 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


176 Ill. App. 3d 1012; 531 N.E.2d 989; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1666; 126 Ill. Dec. 362



November 30, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 6, 1989. As Amended April 4, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Warren D. Wolfson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Several parties sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), in a dispute involving hospital privileges. The trial court directed a verdict against plaintiff physicians and denied the physicians a permanent injunction. The trial court also entered a judgment in favor of one physician based upon a jury verdict but entered an award to defendant hospital for damages resulting from a wrongful preliminary injunction.


OVERVIEW: Certain physicians brought suit against a hospital to challenge its decision to revoke their privileges at the hospital. A preliminary injunction was issued but was reversed by the trial court and all the physicians but one had directed verdicts issued against them. A jury verdict was entered as to that one physician. The court held that the trial court erred in entertaining the causes of action pleaded seeking equitable and legal relief. The court found that the trial court erred in entertaining the physicians' claims and requests for relief and in so doing, it violated the rule of limited judicial review of hospital medical staffing decisions established by caselaw and reaffirmed by relevant statutory law. The court ruled that the trial court was required to decline to exercise subject matter jurisdiction over the physicians' causes of action and requests for relief based thereon. The court affirmed the directed verdicts against certain physicians and the denial to all the physicians of permanent injunctive relief, and reversed the judgment and award of damages for the one physician. The court also affirmed the damages award as a result of the wrongful preliminary injunction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision in part and reversed it in part. The court held that the trial court erred in hearing the case against the hospital in relation to the issue of privileges because caselaw and statutory law dictated that a rule of limited judicial review of such decisions. The court affirmed the finding against the physicians and reversed the verdict in favor of one physician and affirmed a damage award in favor of the hospital.

Davis v. Chicago Housing Authority


No. 87-1008


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


176 Ill. App. 3d 976; 531 N.E.2d 1018; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1667; 126 Ill. Dec. 391



November 30, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Myron T. Gomberg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Chicago Housing Authority (housing authority) appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which vacated the dismissal of plaintiff resident's second amended complaint and granted the resident leave to file a third amended complaint. The housing authority claimed that the Illinois Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 3-106 (1985), applied.


OVERVIEW: The resident was a child who lived in a public housing project and was injured while playing at a public playground provided by the housing authority. The resident filed an action against the housing authority alleging that his injuries were caused by unsafe conditions at the playground, of which the housing authority was aware. The resident was granted leave to file a third-amended complaint. The housing authority appealed and claimed that it was immune from suit under the § 3-106, because the resident failed to allege willful and wanton conduct on the part of the housing authority. The court held that the Act applied. The housing authority, by providing the playground, was performing a governmental function, and not a proprietary function. The power of the housing authority to plan and maintain playgrounds for their residents was within the spirit and meaning of the Housing Authorities Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 67 1/2, para. 8.2 (1985), even though not specifically mentioned therein.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that vacated the dismissal of the second-amended complaint and granted leave to file a third-amended complaint. The court dismissed the resident's action for injuries sustained at a public playground, but denied the housing authority's motion for attorney fees and costs.

Le Blanc v. G.D. Searle & Co.


No. 87-3415


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


178 Ill. App. 3d 236; 533 N.E.2d 41; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1618; 127 Ill. Dec. 423



November 18, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Willard J. Lassers, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, sought review of the decision by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their strict liability complaint brought against defendant manufacturer.


OVERVIEW: The wife alleged that she suffered kidney failure as a result of her use of a birth control pill made by the manufacturer, and the husband claimed loss of consortium. The trial court's dismissal was based on the borrowing statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13 (1985). The trial court reasoned that because the husband and the wife were residents of Louisiana, their claim was barred by Louisiana's one-year statute of limitations. The husband and the wife argued that the manufacturer's principle place of business was in Illinois and that application of the borrowing statute was improper. The court disagreed and found that based on Illinois law, the state of incorporation established the residency of the manufacturer. As a result, Delaware was the residence of the manufacturer and application of the borrowing statute was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's application of the borrowing statute and dismissed the husband and the wife's claim.

 

680 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Price


No. 86-2039


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


176 Ill. App. 3d 831; 531 N.E.2d 901; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1599; 126 Ill. Dec. 274



November 16, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Will E. Gierach, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of six counts of murder and three counts of aggravated arson.


OVERVIEW: After arguing with his family members, defendant spread gasoline on the floor of their house. The gasoline caught fire, resulting in the death of six of the family members. He was convicted of murder and aggravated arson. The court affirmed the murder conviction, finding that defendant's conduct before and after the fire negated his statements that he did not intend to harm the children or damage the house, as he told his wife that he was going to burn the house down and that he was going to burn up the family members, he borrowed a gasoline can and purchased gasoline, and he deliberately poured gasoline throughout the house. Further, defendant was not entitled to an instruction on involuntary manslaughter, as the evidence did not support the contention that defendant acted recklessly in performing the actions that caused the deaths. The aggravated arson conviction was vacated, however, as the statute under which defendant was convicted was unconstitutional. The legislature intended that the statute provide for an aggravated form of arson and that the factors would enhance the offense from simple arson to aggravated arson; however, it failed to define an underlying offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder convictions, but vacated his convictions for aggravated arson.

In re Marriage of Ingram


No. 5-87-0738


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


176 Ill. App. 3d 413; 531 N.E.2d 97; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1615; 125 Ill. Dec. 918



November 15, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Effingham County; the Hon. E. C. Eberspacher, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent wife sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Effingham County (Illinois), which awarded custody of the parties' minor child to petitioner husband.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner husband filed for dissolution of marriage and custody of the parties' minor child. Respondent wife alleged that petitioner was not the child's natural father. The circuit court awarded custody to petitioner. Respondent contended that, because she was asserting the nonparentage of petitioner as a defense to petitioner's attempt to gain custody, § 8 of the Parentage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2508 (1985), allowed her to place nonparentage in issue. The court disagreed because petitioner did not bring an action to declare the existence of the parent and child relationship, but an action to gain permanent custody. Petitioner did not necessarily need to be, nor establish that he was, the natural father in order to obtain legal custody.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment awarding custody of the parties' minor child to the husband.

People v. Green


No. 86-1019


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


179 Ill. App. 3d 1; 535 N.E.2d 413; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1601; 128 Ill. Dec. 902



November 14, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 10, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Romie Palmer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found him guilty of four counts of murder, aggravated arson, residential burglary, home invasion, armed robbery, and four counts of armed violence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, 16 years old, agreed with friends to break into a home. While at the home, defendant's friends murdered the occupants and set fire to the residence. The court found that (1) the trial court had jurisdiction to try defendant as an adult where Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, par. 702-7(6)(a) did not provide juvenile jurisdiction and it was irrelevant that defendant was charged under an accountability theory, (2) there was probable cause to arrest defendant, regardless of whether defendant consented to the entry of police into his apartment, (3) defendant did not establish that he was illegally restrained, (4) defendant was not in custody and was not subject to juvenile rules regarding custody where he was subject to adult jurisdiction, (5) defendant did not establish that his statements to the grand jury were involuntary, (6) there was sufficient evidence that defendant participated in the criminal enterprise, and (7) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the admission of hearsay evidence where the declarants were unavailable and the statements were not reliable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, as defendant was not subject to juvenile rules where he was subject to adult jurisdiction.

Meyer v. Caterpillar Tractor Co.


No. 86-0625


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


179 Ill. App. 3d 268; 533 N.E.2d 386; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1590; 127 Ill. Dec. 514



November 14, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 5, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James A. Geroulis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, premises owner, contractor, and employer, challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment on the jury's verdicts returned in favor of plaintiff worker in the worker's action that alleged a violation of the Structural Work Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 60 (1985).


OVERVIEW: The worker brought an action to recover damages for an injury suffered while working for his employer that had been hired by the contractor to build and install a storage rack system for the premises owner. The premises owner and contractor sought indemnity from the employer. The jury returned verdicts in favor of the worker, and denied recovery to the premises owner and contractor on their indemnity claims. Defendants appealed, and the court reversed in part. The worker claimed that he was injured because defendants failed to provide a safe, suitable, and proper support for a bundle of storage racks which tipped over onto the worker, causing severe and permanent injury to his left knee. The court held that the Act was intended to cover and applied to construction site support devices whether used to support material or workmen. The court ruled that defendants were entitled to a new trial because of the worker's improper introduction of an expert's inadmissible opinion testimony that the unbundling procedure was unsafe, that the amount of the verdict was not unreasonable, and that the indemnity claims were properly denied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that entered judgment in favor of the injured worker and against the contractor and the premises owner, and ordered a new trial. The court affirmed the judgment that denied indemnity to the premises owner and contractor from the employer.
