Snuggery Pub, Inc. v. Mt. Prospect


No. 87-2163


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


176 Ill. App. 3d 119; 530 N.E.2d 1097; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1542; 125 Ill. Dec. 688



November 3, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended April 4, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. George M. Marovich, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff business owner sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion for summary judgment filed by defendants, Village of Mount Prospect, a mayor, trustees, a village manager and a village clerk. The trial court also determined that the annexation amendment to § 7-1-13 of the Illinois Municipal Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 7-1-13 (1985), was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants amended the annexation statute to permit the annexation of unincorporated territories of less than 60 acres located within counties having a population of more than 400,000 and bounded by a creek. The owner brought an action, seeking injunctive and declaratory relief and challenging the constitutionality of the amendment. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment, and the trial court granted defendants' motion. On appeal, the court held that the annexation amendment did not constitute special legislation pursuant to Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13. The court found that the owner failed to satisfy his burden of showing that the placing of counties with a larger population into a separate class was unreasonable and arbitrary. There was no evidence that it was more difficult for lesser-populated counties to obtain a majority vote for voluntary annexation. Moreover, the court found that the population classification bore a reasonable relationship to the amendment's purpose of allowing involuntary annexation. The court also rejected the owner's contention that the amendment's use of a creek as a boundary was vague, finding that the creek's description was sufficient notice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendants.

 

685 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Halcomb


No. 87-1542


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


176 Ill. App. 3d 100; 530 N.E.2d 1074; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1526; 125 Ill. Dec. 665



November 2, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. William Cousins, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14(a)(2) (1985). Defendant challenged his conviction by alleging, inter alia, that the trial court improperly excluded evidence pursuant to the Illinois rape shield statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-7 (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought to introduce evidence that the complainant told him during an intimate conversation prior to the sexual acts that she had recently had an abortion. The trial court excluded the evidence pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-7 (1985). Reversing the conviction on appeal, the court held that the evidence was not rendered inadmissible by the rape-shield statute because it was not offered to prove the complainant's prior sexual activities. Rather, the proffered evidence would have corroborated defendant's claim that the complaint consented. The court also held that the prosecutor's accusation that defendant was discharged from the Navy for larceny presented another ground for reversal. The court held that defendant's being charged with larceny was not the equivalent of a criminal conviction. Thus, it was not admissible against defendant. Moreover, if defendant had been convicted, the prosecution could not cross-examine defendant about the crime. The court rejected defendant's contention that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14(a)(2) (1985), was unconstitutional, finding that defendant was not treated differently from those committing crimes of a similar quality.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault. The court remanded the action to the trial court.

 

686 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Patzner v. Baise


No. 2-88-0174


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


175 Ill. App. 3d 818; 530 N.E.2d 588; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1525; 125 Ill. Dec. 430



November 1, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County; the Hon. F. Lawrence Lenz, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents Secretary of the Department of Transportation of the State of Illinois (secretary) and the Department of Transportation of the State of Illinois (department) appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois), which issued a writ of mandamus directing the secretary to institute condemnation proceedings against property owned by petitioner landowner. At issue was whether the trial court had jurisdiction to issue the writ.


OVERVIEW: The landowner alleged that the department, in constructing an overpass directly above that portion of the highway which used to front his property, (1) trespassed by parking construction vehicles on his property; (2) eliminated the air, light, and view serving his property; and (3) eliminated the practical access from his property to the highway. On the landowner's amended petition, the trial court issued a writ of mandamus compelling the secretary to institute eminent domain proceedings to compensate the landowner for the taking and damaging of his property. The secretary and department appealed. The court reversed, holding that the trial court did not have jurisdiction to issue the writ because the land had been damaged but not "taken" within the meaning of Ill. Const. art, I, § 15. The landowner's sole remedy against the state, the court concluded, was to bring an action for damages in the court of claims pursuant to its exclusive jurisdiction under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, par. 439.8(a) (1985).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting the landowner's petition for a writ of mandamus to compel the secretary to institute eminent domain proceedings.

 

687 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Mettawa v. Carruthers


No. 2-88-0092


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


175 Ill. App. 3d 772; 530 N.E.2d 537; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1507; 125 Ill. Dec. 379



October 26, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Stephen Walter, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owner sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which determined that the property owner violated the zoning ordinance, Mettawa, Ill., Ordinance 76-0-3 (1976), of plaintiff Village of Mettawa by keeping more than the permissible number of horses on her property. The property owner challenged the zoning ordinance's validity under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 3-11-17 (1975).


OVERVIEW: The Village brought an action for injunctive relief, alleging that the property owner violated the zoning ordinance in not obtaining a special use permit and in keeping 33 horses on the property. The trial court found that the Village complied with the procedural requirements in enacting the zoning ordinance. The trial court enjoined the property owner from operating the stable until she obtained a special use permit. On appeal, after deciding that the issue of the zoning ordinance's validity was properly before it, the court held that Mettawa, Ill., Ordinance 76-0-3 (1976) was void and unenforceable because the Village did not comply with the requirements set forth in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 3-11-17 (1975). The court found that for the zoning ordinance to be valid, the record had to show that the roll call vote was taken and the vote of each trustee. The court found that the minutes from the meeting at which the zoning ordinance was enacted did not show the vote of each trustee or that the roll call vote was taken. The court also found that the affidavit supporting the record was insufficient because it was prepared almost 11 years after the zoning ordinance was enacted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's finding that the property owner violated the zoning ordinance.

 

688 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Majidi v. Palmer


No. 2-88-0025


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


175 Ill. App. 3d 679; 530 N.E.2d 66; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1493; 125 Ill. Dec. 148



October 20, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of De Kalb County; the Hon. Douglas Engel, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of De Kalb County (Illinois), which dismissed the father's complaint against respondent mother for declaratory judgment of parentage because it was filed after the applicable limitations period, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2508 (1987), had expired.


OVERVIEW: The father filed a declaratory judgment action against the mother, seeking to establish himself as the father of the parties' minor child, to obtain custody of the child, and to obtain visitation if custody to him was not granted. The trial court dismissed the father's complaint because it was filed after expiration of the applicable limitations period, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2508 (1987). The father appealed, contending that: the statute of limitations was unconstitutional, that the trial court improperly applied the statute of limitations retroactively, and that a guardian ad litem should have been appointed to represent the minor child. On appeal, the court affirmed, remanded for appointment of a guardian ad litem, and held that the retroactive application of the statute of limitations did not result in a harsh and oppressive result and, therefore, did not deny the father due process because he had a reasonable time period in which to file his claim, that the statutory classification in para. 2508 was rationally related to a legitimate governmental purpose and therefore did not violate equal protection, and that the trial court had an obligation to appoint a guardian.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the father's action for declaratory judgment of parentage against the mother and remanded the case with directions for appointment of a guardian ad litem for the parties' minor child.

 

689 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. McDarrah


No. 2-87-0041


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


175 Ill. App. 3d 284; 529 N.E.2d 808; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1456; 124 Ill. Dec. 827



October 6, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Robert A. Nolan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part, and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted him on two counts of home invasion, and on one count each of aggravated criminal sexual assault, aggravated kidnapping, kidnapping, and aggravated battery, and sentenced him to imprisonment on all convictions except for the kidnapping conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged, convicted, and sentenced on two counts of home invasion, and one count each of aggravated criminal sexual assault, aggravated kidnapping, kidnapping, and aggravated battery. The court rejected defendant's argument that the trial court erroneously refused to allow a psychologist to give an opinion as an expert or lay witness in support of defendant's insanity defense. The witness proffered by defendant was not qualified to give an expert opinion. Given the witness' relationship to defendant, the duration of her interview with him, and the remoteness of time between the offenses and interview, the trial court's refusal to allow her to give a lay opinion was not an abuse of discretion. The statute placing the burden of proof of insanity on defendant and specifying the instruction to be given the jury on that defense was not unconstitutional, and there was no basis for instructing the jury on guilty but mentally ill. It was improper to convict defendant of two aggravated felonies where the two underlying felonies were committed at the same time and each served to enhance the other.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed except for the conviction for aggravated kidnapping and on one count for home invasion, which were vacated. The case was remanded for the purpose of imposing sentence for the kidnapping conviction.

Castaneda v. Human Rights Com.


No. 87-2722


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


175 Ill. App. 3d 1085; 530 N.E.2d 1005; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1429; 125 Ill. Dec. 596



September 30, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for review of order of Human Rights Commission.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former employee sought review of an order and decision, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 3-101 et seq. (1987), and the Illinois Human Rights Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 8-111 (1987), of the Illinois Human Rights Commission (commission), which dismissed with prejudice his complaint of discrimination against respondent former employer.


OVERVIEW: The former employee, a native of Mexico, had been employed as a senior vice president by the former employer, who was an insurance broker. When he was terminated, he filed a charge of discrimination with the commission, which dismissed his complaint with prejudice. The former employee contended that a default judgment should have been entered against his former employer for violating various discovery orders and that the decision was against the manifest weight of the evidence. On appeal, the court dismissed the former employee's appeal, holding that he failed to exhaust his administrative remedies. The court concluded that after a three-member panel of the commission entered an order and decision adopting the administrative law judge's recommendations, the former employee should have sought a rehearing before the entire commission, so dismissal of his appeal was appropriate because the exhaustion of remedies rule precluded the court's review.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the former employee's appeal from an order and decision of the commission, which dismissed his complaint of discrimination against his former employer with prejudice.

 

691 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Scholten


No. 2-87-1018


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


175 Ill. App. 3d 214; 529 N.E.2d 796; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1422; 124 Ill. Dec. 815



September 29, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Edward W. Kowal, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), granting defendants' pretrial motion to suppress evidence. Defendants were charged in a three-count indictment with the offenses of gambling, keeping a gambling place, and conspiracy to commit the offense of gambling.


OVERVIEW: Defendants alleged that evidence was obtained in a warrantless search in violation of their Fourth Amendment rights. Defendants had rented a separate area contained within a country club for a private party. The city police received information that gambling was occurring in the club. They made a liquor check and observed certain items, which they seized and the State intended to introduce into evidence. The trial court found that the entry was warrantless and that the officers entered, not to inspect for a liquor violation, but to determine if gambling occurred on the premises. The State contended that because the country club was licensed by the State and by the City to sell alcoholic beverages, it was subject to inspection and search without a warrant. The court held that: (1) the undisputed evidence showed that the purpose of the search was solely to look for gambling activities on the premises, not to further any purpose under § 10--8 of the Liquor Control Act of 1934, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 190 (1987), or City of Wood Dale, Ill., Municipal Code ch. 3, § 3--201, which regulated alcohol licensees; and (2) thus, the trial court properly suppressed the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court.

 

692 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gonzalez


No. 86-1176


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


175 Ill. App. 3d 466; 529 N.E.2d 1027; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1416; 124 Ill. Dec. 910



September 27, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 31, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Strayhorn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated in part, and reversed in part and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder and armed violence and sentenced him to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for murder by shooting and for armed violence based on the shooting. The trial court denied defendant's motion for a severance. The court vacated in part and reversed in part the trial court's decision. Defendant's conviction was largely based on the testimony of his co-defendant's sister. The court determined that the mandatory life provisions was not unconstitutional. It was error for the trial court to restrict defendant's attorney's cross-examination of a witness because the principal issue concerned the identification of defendant and his attorney would have been given wide latitude on cross-examination. The trial court improperly accepted the State's offer of proof and defendant did not take a position that constituted a knowing waiver of the right to bar certain evidence by making his own offer of proof. Because it was a denial of due process for the trier of fact to consider evidence untested by cross-examination or contrary to the rules of evidence, reversible error occurred. Defendant's rights in a bench trial were the same as they would have been in a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court vacated in part, and reversed in part and remanded for new trial the trial court's decision convicting him of murder and sentencing him to life in prison.

 

693 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Poliny v. Soto


No. 87-1322


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


178 Ill. App. 3d 203; 533 N.E.2d 15; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1390; 127 Ill. Dec. 397



September 23, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Myron T. Gomberg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff complainant appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his complaint for failure to state a cause of action against defendants, city and its police officers, charging them with negligence in leaving him at an arrest scene where he was subsequently attacked by a friend of the arrestee.


OVERVIEW: The complainant charged defendants with negligence in leaving him at an arrest scene where he was subsequently attacked by a friend of the arrestee. The trial court dismissed the complaint for failure to state a cause of action. On appeal, the complainant argued that the judicially created "special duty" exception to the tort immunity of police officers was improperly formulated, against public policy, and against the Tort Immunity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 9-103 (1985). The court affirmed the trial court, finding that defendants owed no special duty to the complainant. The control element of the special duty exception to the tort immunity of police officers outweighed the public noninvolvement consideration advanced by the complainant. While the court agreed with the complainant's position as an ideal one in fostering the assistance of the public citizenry in apprehending criminals, it appeared to be an impossible one in light of the burden that would have been imposed on the police to accomplish the ideal relationship. The court found without merit the complainant's allegation of an unconstitutional classification in violation of Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, (1970).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which dismissed the negligence complaint for failure to state a cause of action against defendants.

People v. Webster


No. 86-105


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


175 Ill. App. 3d 119; 529 N.E.2d 741; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1369; 124 Ill. Dec. 760



September 20, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 12, 1988. As Amended March 3, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Christy Berkos, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which a jury trial convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault and attempt. The circuit court sentenced him to 60 years' imprisonment for aggravated criminal sexual assault, ruling that the other charge had merged.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction. On appeal, the court vacated defendant's conviction of attempt and affirmed the other conviction and sentence. The court found defendant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault must be affirmed because the decision whether to file a pretrial motion was one of strategy which had no bearing on the competency of counsel and had not demonstrated ineffective assistance of counsel. The court held that his conviction for attempt was vacated because of the incomplete judgment entered by the trial court. The court found that the jury was adequately apprised of the elements of the offense of aggravated criminal sexual assault, since the state needed not prove the type of sexual penetration as an element of the offense. The court held that the trial judge's questions that regarded defendant's past and his employment were proper because the questions related to defendant's potential for rehabilitation. Finally, the court held that defendant was eligible for an extended-term sentence because of his felony conviction within 10 years of this conviction.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction of attempt and affirmed defendant's conviction of aggravated criminal sexual assault and affirmed defendant's sentence.

People v. Vought


No. 2-87-0015


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


174 Ill. App. 3d 563; 528 N.E.2d 1095; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1352; 124 Ill. Dec. 204



September 15, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 14, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Edward W. Kowal, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction and sentence in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), for unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence obtained following a warrantees entry into his hotel room by a police officer.


OVERVIEW: Acting on information from hotel personnel, a police officer entered a hotel room to check on a suitcase containing what was thought to be cocaine. The officer was told that the occupant of the room, the defendant, had checked out. The defendant appeared at the room and consented to the officer's search of the suitcase, claiming that the suitcase was not his. Finding that the suitcase contained contraband, later discovered to be cocaine, the officer arrested the defendant. The defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. On appeal, the court found that the warrantless search of the defendant's hotel room was not justified by exigent circumstances or by the hotel supervisor's authority to allow the officer into the room because she believed the room to be vacant. The court rejected the state's argument that the presence of cocaine in the room posed a danger to hotel employees. Holding the search unlawful, the court also examined inculpatory statements made by the defendant at the time of his arrest. The court held that these statements should have been suppressed because they were not made voluntarily.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

696 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


DOT ex rel. People v. Amoco Oil Co.


No. 2-87-0727


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


174 Ill. App. 3d 479; 528 N.E.2d 1018; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1480; 124 Ill. Dec. 127



September 12, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. William E. Black, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) entered a judgment, after a jury verdict, in favor of defendant oil company and against plaintiff Illinois Department of Transportation (Department) in its action to condemn a portion of the oil company's property. The Department appealed the adverse judgment.


OVERVIEW: The Department issued the oil company a permit to build a service station on the oil company's property, which abutted a freeway. The permit was conditioned on the oil company's agreement that it would not seek additional compensation from the Department in the event a portion of the property was condemned for use of the freeway. The Department condemned a portion of the property, closed the oil company's driveways, and sought to enforce the agreement. The trial court denied enforcing it. In affirming the denial, the court held that the agreement was void and unenforceable. The court found that the purpose of the condition was solely to depress the property value in anticipation of future acquisition. The court stated that the statute that allowed the Department to prohibit abutting property owners from constructing access driveways to a freeway was intended to promote the safety and convenience of highway traffic and eliminate the danger of accidents. Conditions proscribing surfacing, dimensions, and illumination might serve such a purpose; however, it was clearly not served by a condition that solely sought to depress the value of condemned property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that was entered in favor of the oil company and against the Department.

People v. Bostic

County of Lake v. Zenko


No. 2-87-0841


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


174 Ill. App. 3d 54; 528 N.E.2d 414; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1479; 123 Ill. Dec. 869



August 30, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Stephen E. Walter, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county, citing Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 34, para. 3151 (1987), sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which entered a directed finding in favor of defendant landowner, in the county's action to enjoin the landowner's operation of a junkyard in violation of its zoning ordinance and the landowner's counterclaim for a declaratory judgment that the zoning ordinance and its application to him were invalid.


OVERVIEW: The county contended on appeal that its definition of "junk yard" in the zoning ordinance was reasonable and therefore valid. The court reversed and remanded. The court noted that the county's power to enact a zoning ordinance was provided in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 34, para. 3151 (1987), and that an express legislative grant of power or authority included the grant of power to do all that was reasonably necessary to execute that power or authority. The court found nothing unreasonable, arbitrary, or capricious about the county zoning ordinance's definition of the term "junk yard." The court stated that the fact that the used cars and parts on the landowner's lot had commercial value did not serve to remove it from the definition of "junk yard." The court concluded that the county's definition of the term "junk yard" was neither unauthorized by law nor arbitrary, unreasonable, discriminatory, or confiscatory.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting the landowner's motion for a directed verdict in the county's action to enjoin his operation of a junkyard and his counterclaim for a declaratory judgment, and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

699 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Dawson v. St. Francis Hosp.


No. 87-0923


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


174 Ill. App. 3d 351; 528 N.E.2d 362; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1273; 123 Ill. Dec. 817



August 25, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas R. Rakowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed her medical malpractice complaint against defendant doctors pursuant to Sup. Ct. R. 103(b), 107 Ill. 2d R. 103(b), for lack of diligent service, and granted summary judgment in favor of defendant hospital.


OVERVIEW: Doctors performed back surgery on the patient. She filed a malpractice claim against them and the hospital in 1983. The doctors were not served until 1985. After several continuances, the trial court granted the doctor's motion to dismiss for lack of due diligence in effecting service and it granted the hospital's motion for summary judgment, finding it demonstrated adequacy of medical care and that the patient had not taken steps toward acquiring discovery from the hospital or obtaining an expert. The trial court denied the patient's motions to vacate the orders. Thus, she appealed. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion nor did it deprive her of due process by denying further continuances because the patient's attorney agreed to a final date for the hearing and did not comply. Further, the doctors' motions were properly granted based on the doctors' proof of an obvious place of business and the patient presented no basis for the delay in service. Also, the hospital showed that the patient had not taken steps to proceed in the case. The court further concluded that it was highly doubtful that any amendment would have aided her on the diligence issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

700 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Triple A Servs. v. Rice


No. 86-1274


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


174 Ill. App. 3d 654; 528 N.E.2d 267; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1247; 123 Ill. Dec. 722



August 19, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Charles Freeman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mobile food vendors appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), in favor of defendant City of Chicago and related personnel, which upheld Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 27-269.1, which prohibited all mobile food vendor traffic in the Medical Center District (District) at all times.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that the trial evidence established that the city council passed the ordinance without any meaningful deliberation and without being informed that the means employed by the ordinance would accomplish the ordinance's stated purpose, or what effect the ordinance would have on the licensed mobile food vendors. The effect of the ordinance was not to further the purpose of the District but instead was to summarily revoke the mobile food vendor licenses, without notice and a hearing as required under the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 (1982), and the Municipal Code of Chicago. No evidence was presented to establish that mobile food vendor vehicles had any impact upon the District's performance of its purposes to provide care for the sick and injured and for the study of diseases. The substance of the defense testimony was that the mobile food vendor vehicles' presence in the District was cosmetically offensive. Thus, the ordinance constituted arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable municipal action, there was no permissible interpretation which justified its adoption and it was not directly related to the stated purposes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision below that upheld the ordinance and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

701 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Rawles v. Hartman


No. 2-87-1125


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


172 Ill. App. 3d 931; 527 N.E.2d 680; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1193; 123 Ill. Dec. 217



August 5, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Barbara Gilleran-Johnson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which declined to apply § 513 of the Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 513 (1985), to provide for the educational needs of a nonminor, illegitimate child in a parentage proceeding against respondent father.


OVERVIEW: After paternity and the child support obligation were established, the mother filed a petition for an order under § 513 requiring the father to pay their daughter's college expenses. The trial court dismissed the petition because the Parentage Act made no provision for the payment of such expenses. The mother argued that the failure to apply § 513 constituted an arbitrary differentiation between legitimate and illegitimate children in violation of the constitutional guarantees of equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. The court held that when read together the Parentage Act and Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act authorized a court making a child support award to include provisions for the payment of educational expenses for nonminor, illegitimate children. Despite the absence of a specific statutory provision, the legislature had manifested an intent to treat all children equally in matters of support in § 3 of the Parentage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2503 (1985).The court's construction gave effect to the legislative intent without the need to address the mother's equal protection challenge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order declining to apply the statute and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

702 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cregar


Nos. 4-87-0524, 4-87-0525 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


172 Ill. App. 3d 807; 526 N.E.2d 1376; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1181; 122 Ill. Dec. 613



August 4, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 1, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Livingston County; the Hon. Harold J. Frobish, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment from the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the addition of counts constituted an amendment to his indictment and violated his due process right to be convicted of the offense for which he was indicted. The court affirmed the judgment and remanded for entry of a sentence credit. The court held that additional counts brought by information were not an amendment of the indictment. Indictment on all state charges was not required if sufficient notice of the offense charged was given to the accused and he was afforded protection from invalid accusations. Double jeopardy concepts did not bar defendant's trial after the dismissal of three counts. The court found that the date of the offense was not an essential ingredient in child sex offenses. Because the date was not a material part of the offense charged, and defendant was not prejudiced by proof of a varying date, he was not denied a fair trial by the variance. The court held that evidence of the relationship between the victim and defendant was admissible to show familiarity of the parties and to corroborate the victim's testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse and remanded for entry of a sentence credit. The court held that additional counts were not an amendment to the indictment and that prosecution after the dismissal of certain counts did not bar the trial on double jeopardy grounds.

 

703 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kauffman


No. 4-88-0130


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


172 Ill. App. 3d 1040; 527 N.E.2d 645; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1144; 123 Ill. Dec. 182



August 4, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Moultrie County; the Hon. Arthur F. Powers, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Moultrie County (Illinois), which revoked his probation for driving with a revoked license and sentenced him to a two-year term of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had his probation revoked and was sentenced to imprisonment after admitted to the allegations contained in a petition to revoke probation. On appeal, defendant argued that (1) the two-year sentence of imprisonment was excessive; (2) the penalty provided in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 6-303(d) (1985) was disproportionate to the offense of driving with a revoked license and was, therefore, unconstitutional; and (3) the two-year sentence should have included a credit for time served while defendant was on probation. Upon review, the court found defendant's arguments without merit. The sentence of a term of imprisonment was not an abuse of discretion. Defendant's record showed an ongoing disrespect for the law. Twice defendant had been ordered to serve a period of time in the county jail. None of those punishments seemed to impress on him the importance of obeying the law. Challenging the constitutionality of a statute was not properly done for the first time on appeal. The trial court's failure to comment about defendant's probation means defendant was not supposed to receive credit for that time.


OUTCOME: The revocation of defendant's probation and the two-year term of imprisonment were affirmed.

People v. Glover


Nos. 85-2972, 85-3374, 86-0359 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


123 Ill. App. 330; 173 Ill. App. 3d 678; 527 N.E.2d 968; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1143; 123 Ill. Dec. 330



August 3, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Gino DiVito, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Five defendants sought review of judgments from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted them of armed robbery, home invasion, and aggravated battery. The grounds for appeal included errors in the admission of testimony and restrictions in cross-examination, and constitutional challenges to the Habitual Criminal Statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendants robbed the bar proprietor and the patrons, and injured some patrons with guns. A jury found defendants guilty of armed robbery, home invasion, and aggravated battery, and they challenged their convictions and sentences. The court held that: (1) the trial court's restriction of cross-examination of the proprietor, which prevented inquiry regarding the proprietor's charge of unlawful use of weapons, was harmless in view of the overwhelming evidence of guilt; (2) testimony that a defendant made a verbal reference to a gang affiliation was competent evidence as part of the res gestae; and (3) the Habitual Criminal Statute, § 33B-1 of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B-1 (1983), which mandated natural life imprisonment, did not violate Ill. Const. art I, § 11 (1970), or U.S. Const. amends. VIII, XIV, because it did not improperly prevent the trial court from consideration of mitigating circumstances, was not cruel and unusual punishment or a violation of due process, did not deny defendants adequate notice of the prosecutor's intention to seek a natural life sentence, did not place defendants in double jeopardy, and was not an ex post facto law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments that convicted defendants of armed robbery, home invasion, and aggravated battery.

 

705 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Penn


No. 5-87-0094


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


177 Ill. App. 3d 179; 533 N.E.2d 383; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1867; 127 Ill. Dec. 511



August 3, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County; the Hon. George Oros, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois) dismissing an information that charged defendant with perjury under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 32-2 (1985).


OVERVIEW: The State charged defendant with perjury on the basis that his testimony in two different criminal trials was contradictory. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the information for failure to state an offense. The trial court granted the motion finding that the information failed to allege defendant's mental state, which was an essential element of the offense. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that because defendant challenged the sufficiency of the information before the trial court, the more stringent standard of review applied, and the information had to comply with the requirements of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 111-3(a)(3) (1985) to withstand the attack. The court further held that defendant's mental state was an essential element of the offense regardless of whether defendant was charged under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 32-2(a) (1985) or § 32-2(b). Therefore, because the information failed to allege defendant's knowledge of the falsity of the perjured statements at the time he uttered them, it was fatally defective and was properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that dismissed the information that charged defendant with perjury.

State Farm Fire & Casualty Co. v. Ondracek


No. 87-3652


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


173 Ill. App. 3d 581; 527 N.E.2d 889; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1113; 123 Ill. Dec. 251



July 29, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas R. Rakowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant parents sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted judgment on the pleadings to plaintiff insurer in its declaratory judgment action seeking a determination concerning liability coverage under a homeowner's policy it issued to the parents.


OVERVIEW: The mother sued a driver for injuries to her daughter, which were the result of a collision between an automobile driven by the driver and a bicycle ridden by the mother with her daughter as a passenger. The driver later counterclaimed against the mother for contribution for bodily injuries sustained by the daughter. The parents asked the insurer to defend the counterclaim pursuant to their homeowner's policy, whereupon the insurance company filed the underlying declaratory judgment action. On appeal, the parents argued that a third-party claim for contribution was not a bodily injury to an insured and, further, that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, para. 755.01 (1985) and public policy prohibited enforcement of the household exclusion clause. Upon review, the court found the parents' arguments without merit. It was clear that the household exclusion clause in the parents' policy unambiguously excluded any liability for a counterclaim seeking contribution from them for bodily injuries to a family member. Such a counterclaim was an intangible loss not covered by the property damage provisions of the policy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the insurer in its declaratory judgment action against the parents.

 

707 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hightower


No. 5-86-0594


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


172 Ill. App. 3d 678; 526 N.E.2d 1129; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1120; 122 Ill. Dec. 590



July 26, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County; the Hon. Robert H. Howerton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of the murder of his wife. Defendant alleged that he was insane at the time of the offense. The jury was instructed, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 3-2 (1985), that defendant had the burden to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that he was not guilty by reason of insanity. The sole issue on appeal was whether § 3-2 violated defendant's due process rights.


OVERVIEW: The court held that § 3-2 did not offend the due process clause of the United States Constitution, which stated that no one could be deprived of life, liberty, or property without due process of law. The court found that the insanity defense did not negate mens rea and thus the legislature could properly classify it as an affirmative defense rather than an element of an offense. Section 3-2, which required defendant to prove his insanity by a preponderance of the evidence, did not violate the constitution of Illinois either. The Illinois courts and the Illinois legislature had distinguished between mens rea and sanity. Because a defendant could intend to commit an offense and yet be subject to a mental disease which rendered him or her incapable of appreciating the nature of or controlling his or her actions, sanity was not an element of a crime, such as murder. Moreover, although prior to the statute Illinois had always placed the burden of proof of sanity on the State, that was not enough by itself to render the statute unconstitutional. Therefore, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder by the trial court.

 

708 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sequoia Books, Inc.


No. 2-87-0675


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


172 Ill. App. 3d 627; 527 N.E.2d 50; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1059; 122 Ill. Dec. 678



July 21, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 22, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County; the Hon. Wilson D. Burnell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bookstore challenged the jury verdict entered in the Circuit Court of Kendall County (Illinois), which found the bookstore had violated a permanent injunction which enjoined it from, inter alia, violating § 11-20 of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20 (1985), which prohibited the distribution of obscene materials. The trial court imposed a fine of $ 10,000.


OVERVIEW: The bookstore was enjoined from distributing obscene material. It challenged the constitutionality of the injunction, and while that matter was pending was cited for contempt because it sold two pornographic magazines. A jury found the bookstore had violated the injunction and was in contempt. The trial court assessed a fine of $ 10,000. The bookstore filed an appeal, noting that the underlying injunction was found to be unconstitutional. It challenged the testimony of an expert witness and the imposition of the fine. The court affirmed the jury verdict and the fine. It held that in general a contempt charge could not be sustained if the underlying order engaged in prior restraint of pure speech. It held that paragraph one of the injunction enjoined the sale of obscene material as determined under the criminal code. It held that the finding of contempt could stand because paragraph one was still valid. It held that the expert's testimony about the relationship between the magazines and AIDS was not relevant, but its admission was not harmful error. It held that the imposition of punishment was in the province of the trial court, and the fine was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the jury verdict that found the bookstore had violated the permanent injunction against distributing obscene material and was in contempt of the trial court's order. It affirmed the fine as within the trial court's discretion for setting the appropriate punishment for contempt.

 

709 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brooks


Nos. 84-2358, 84-2359 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


173 Ill. App. 3d 153; 527 N.E.2d 436; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1009; 122 Ill. Dec. 938



July 13, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended December 27, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Gino L. DiVito, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions for armed robbery from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendants were convicted of armed robbery on a theory of accountability. Defendants appealed, and the court reversed the convictions. The trial court committed reversible error when it failed to question prospective jurors in accordance with a recent holding. Contrary to the state's position, the filing of a petition for rehearing did not alter the effective date of that holding. The trial court was required during its voir dire examination to have probed the venire's attitudes concerning (1) returning a guilty verdict if the state did not sustain its burden of proof; (2) the presumption of innocence; (3) the fact that defendants were not required to present any evidence; and (4) the fact that defendants' failure to testify could not be held against them. The subject matter of these questions was neither covered in the course of voir dire, nor set forth in the trial court's general comments to the venire. One defendant was not convicted in violation of the Juvenile Court Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 701-1 et seq. (1983), because the indictment clearly apprised him that he was charged with armed robbery with a firearm.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions for armed robbery and remanded the case for a new trial.

People v. Dail


No. 3-87-0461


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


171 Ill. App. 3d 308; 525 N.E.2d 588; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 925; 121 Ill. Dec. 530



June 29, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Robert R. Buchar, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order by the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of possession of a stolen motor vehicle, a Class 2 felony, and sentenced defendant to a seven-year term of imprisonment. The defendant appealed on grounds that the penalty provision of the statute under which he was convicted was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In support of defendant's assertion that the penalty provision for possession of a stolen vehicle was unconstitutional, he argued both that it punished the lesser included offense of possession more severely than the greater offense of theft, and that the penalty provision was not reasonably designed to remedy the evils which the legislature had determined to be a threat to the public. The court agreed with defendant stating that the sentencing scheme violated the constitutional assurances of proportionate penalties and due process since the penalty for theft of a motor vehicle was less than that for possession of a stolen motor vehicle even though additional elements were required to prove the greater offense of theft. The court concluded that although consideration of the problems associated with organized vehicle theft, "chop shops," and possible remedies were within the legislature's province, the court was compelled to intervene because the legislative scheme, which subjected defendants not engaged in those activities to a harsher penalty than those who were so engaged, was not reasonably designed to remedy the identified evils.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of possession of a stolen motor vehicle.

People v. Brown


No. 2-87-0060


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


171 Ill. App. 3d 391; 525 N.E.2d 576; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 913; 121 Ill. Dec. 518



June 27, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Jack Hoogasian, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) which convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual abuse in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-16(d) (1985) and sentenced defendant to 17 years imprisonment for defendant's activities with a 15-year-old girl. Defendant contended that he was improperly denied the opportunity to present an affirmative defense of reasonable belief of the victim's age.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 23-year-old male, was found in bed naked with a 15-year-old girl by the girl's mother. The couple had intercourse in the girl's bedroom at the mother's house. Defendant was charged with, and convicted of, aggravated criminal sexual abuse in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-16(d) (1985). Defendant appealed, contending that the refusal to instruct the jury as to the affirmative defense of reasonable belief of age was erroneous and that his counsel was ineffective. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. It held that the victim's testimony on cross-examination that defendant told the victim shortly after her 15th birthday that he thought she was 16 did not put defendant's affirmative defense of reasonable belief of age in issue. Defendant could not raise the defense on cross-examination, and therefore, defendant was not entitled to the defense instruction. The court held that defendant's counsel was not ineffective for deciding not to recall the victim in order to establish the reasonable belief defense because counsel's decision was a matter of trial strategy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual abuse and sentenced defendant to 17 years imprisonment.

In re J.M.


No. 2-87-0418


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


170 Ill. App. 3d 552; 524 N.E.2d 1241; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 847; 121 Ill. Dec. 193



June 13, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Kevin P. Connelly, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father of a minor appealed pro se a decision from the Circuit Court of DuPage County (Illinois), adjudicating the minor a minor requiring authoritative intervention (MRAI). The lower court also determined that it was in the best interests of the minor to be made a ward of the court, placed her under supervision for a one-year period, and released her to the continued care and custody of her foster parents.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the father contended (1) § 2 -- 3 of the Juvenile Court Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702 -- 3 (1985), (the MRAI statute) was unconstitutional; (2) he was deprived of due process at the dispositional hearing; (3) the adjudication of the minor as an MRAI was against the manifest weight of the evidence; and (4) the MRAI statute did not further the basic purpose of the Juvenile Court Act. The court rejected the father's contention that the statute was unconstitutional. In asserting that he was denied due process at the dispositional hearing, the father argued he did not receive the statutory notice required, he was not afforded a "fair opportunity to controvert" the contents of the social history report, and he was denied his right to have counsel present. He requested the court's dispositional order be set aside. The court concluded that lack of the required notice that the hearing was a dispositional one deprived the father of the opportunity to effectively controvert the report's conclusion and recommended disposition by presenting evidence relevant to the lower court's determination of wardship and proper disposition. This required reversal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment below which found the minor to be an MRAI. The court reversed the lower court's dispositional order, and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

Jordan v. Officer


No. 5-87-0421


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


170 Ill. App. 3d 776; 525 N.E.2d 1067; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 903; 121 Ill. Dec. 760



June 13, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. C. Glenn Stevens, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant successful nominees sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) that on remand found in favor of plaintiff defeated nominees by declaring that as to the city offices of mayor and treasurer a primary election was null and void. Plaintiffs had filed an action contesting the primary election results, alleging a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 7-43(c) (1987).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs and defendants, members of the same political party, sought nomination to run in a consolidated election for mayor and city treasurer. Plaintiffs were defeated in the primary election and they filed an action contesting the results. An injunction delaying the consolidated election was vacated on appeal. While the appeal was pending one plaintiff died. On remand, the trial court declared that the primary election was null and void as to the offices of mayor and treasurer. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court held that in the absence of evidence demonstrating fraud or an effort to undermine the nominating process, nullification was not warranted. The court determined that joinder of the candidates for an office that was not the subject of the action was unnecessary. The court held that § 7-43(c) was constitutional and it did not prohibit independents from voting in a party primary. The court held that the deceased plaintiff's cause of action abated. The court apportioned the illegal votes and concluded that plaintiff, who was seeking the nomination as treasurer, still won by a considerable margin.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

Bus. & Prof'l People for the Pub. Interest v. Ill. Commerce Comm'n


Nos. 87-3356, 87-3373, 87-3408, 87-3846 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


171 Ill. App. 3d 948; 525 N.E.2d 1053; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 835; 121 Ill. Dec. 746



June 10, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 14, 1988. As Amended December 27, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for review of order of Illinois Commerce Commission in 87 -- 3356, 87 -- 3373 and 87 -- 3408.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed in 87 -- 3408; affirmed as modified in 87 -- 3846; reversed in 87 -- 3356 and 87 -- 3373.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner electric company challenged respondent Illinois Commerce Commission's (commission) order, which directed the electric company to refund monies plus interest under the fuel adjustment rate of the Public Utilities Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 1 et seq., specifically Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 36 (1979). The electric company also challenged an injunction issued by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: The commission's order resulted from a reconciliation hearing during which the commission reviewed the electric company's costs of fuel and purchased power for 1983. The electric company argued that the commission exceeded its statutory authority in ordering a refund, the finding of the electric company's imprudence was not based on substantial evidence, it was denied due process of law, the commission's award of interest was erroneous, and the trial court abused its discretion in entering the injunction. The court affirmed the commission's order as to the refund and held that the commission was within its statutory authority under § 36 of the Act when it applied the prudence standard to the reasons for the purchases and not only to the actual purchases. However, the court reversed the finding that the electric company was liable for interest and held that the commission had no statutory authority to impose either pre- or post-order interest on the refund under §§ 36 or 72 of the Act, specifically Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, paras. 36, 76 (1979). The court affirmed the trial court's mandatory injunction, directing the commission to pay the refund, except for the interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the propriety of the commission's refund order, but reversed the interest provision. The court also affirmed the trial court's order of injunction, but directed that it be modified to eliminate the interest provision. The court further continued a stay of the injunction order until the time for filing a petition for rehearing in the court or a petition for leave to appeal expired.

Barbosa v. Committee on Accountancy


No. 87-1110


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


171 Ill. App. 3d 782; 525 N.E.2d 980; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 815; 121 Ill. Dec. 673



June 7, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accountant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant Committee on Accountancy of the Board of Trustees of the University of Illinois's motion for summary judgment against the accountant's action for declaratory judgment to compel the Committee to grant him a certificate as a certified public accountant (CPA) under the laws of the state of Illinois.


OVERVIEW: The accountant took three parts of the New York CPA examination. However, his application for a certificate was denied. The accountant moved to Illinois and applied to the Committee for an Illinois CPA certificate. He requested the Committee to accept the transfer of his New York examination credit. The Committee interpreted Committee Rule 16(d), 5 Ill. Reg. 8310 (1981), to require a person applying for a transfer of out-of-state credits to initially sit for all four sections of the examination at the same time. Because the accountant sat for only three sections when he first attempted the examination in New York, the Committee denied his application. The accountant filed an action for declaratory judgment and the trial court granted the Committee's motion for summary judgment. The court affirmed and held that the Committee correctly interpreted Rule 16 to mean that an applicant who wished to transfer examination credit from another state must have taken all four portions in one sitting, which was the same standard that was required of Illinois residents. Further, the State's interest in not discriminating against its own residents met the constitutional rational relationship test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of the Committee's motion for summary judgment.

 

716 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Continental Ins. Co. v. Walsh Constr. Co.


No. 86-0337


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


171 Ill. App. 3d 135; 524 N.E.2d 1131; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 744; 121 Ill. Dec. 83



May 26, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Alan E. Morrill, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held that the landowner's action against defendant contractor for negligence in the engineering and construction of an underground sewer system was barred by the two-year statute of limitations contained in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-214(a) (1983).


OVERVIEW: The landowner brought an action against the contractor for damages to the landowner's building resulting from negligent services provided by the contractor in the engineering and construction of an underground sewer system adjacent to the insurer's property. The trial court found that the complaint, filed almost five years after the damage occurred, was barred by a two-year statute of limitations set forth in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-214(a) (1983). On appeal, the landowner contended that its cause of action was governed by the five-year statute of limitations for recovery for an injury to property set forth in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-205 (1983). The court affirmed and held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-214(a) (1983) governed the landowner's cause of action and suffered no constitutional infirmity. There was nothing in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-214 (1983), to indicate that the Illinois General Assembly intended to create an exception for injured parties who owned property adjacent to construction or engineering services. Adjacent landowners acquired no rights in addition to those conferred upon owners of property that had been damaged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment holding that the landowner's negligence action against the contractor was not filed within the applicable two-year statute of limitations.

Mid-America Federal Sav. & Loan Asso. v. Kosiewicz


No. 2-87-0797


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


170 Ill. App. 3d 316; 524 N.E.2d 663; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 739; 120 Ill. Dec. 633



May 23, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. S. Bruce Scidmore, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor purchasers sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which granted the motion to vacate filed by defendant, mortgagor husband, vacated the judgment of foreclosure, and quashed the summons in plaintiff mortgagee's foreclosure action.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagee filed a foreclosure action and a deputy sheriff personally served the mortgagor wife with two copies of the summons and complaint. The return of service reflected that substituted service was made on the mortgagor husband by leaving the summons and complaint with the mortgagor wife. Default judgment was entered against the mortgagors, and the property was sold to the purchasers at a sheriff's sale. The purchasers went to the property to advise the mortgagors that they had obtained a writ of assistance against them. That day, the mortgagor wife died of a self inflicted gunshot wound. The mortgagor husband claimed that he never received notice of the foreclosure and filed a motion to vacate the default judgment. The trial court granted the motion and quashed the summons. The purchasers appealed. The court reversed the trial court's order and denied the motion. The return of service was not facially defective, and the substituted service pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2--203(a) (1985), was reasonably calculated to reach the mortgagor husband under the circumstances. Further, the statute as applied to the mortgagor husband was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that had granted the mortgagor husband's motion to vacate the judgment of foreclosure, vacated the judgment of foreclosure, and quashed the summons. The court remanded the foreclosure action for further proceedings.

 

718 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Glinka v. Flame of Countryside, Inc.


No. 87-3048


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


171 Ill. App. 3d 81; 524 N.E.2d 1102; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 721; 121 Ill. Dec. 54



May 23, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas P. Quinn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, widow of the deceased, appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted the motion to dismiss for failure to state a cause of action filed by defendants, the alcohol provider, a bank, and others, in plaintiff's complaint for loss of support for fatal injuries suffered by husband following his consumption of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff challenged the constitutionality of the Liquor Control Act of 1934, as amended, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 135(1985), claiming that it was an arbitrary classification that barred causes of action for loss of support by the relatives of intoxicated persons against the dramshop. The court reasoned that in the absence of a fundamental right or suspect classification, the legislature may differentiate between persons similarly situated if there was a reasonable basis for doing to. A court should not interfere with the legislature's judgment unless the classification was clearly unreasonable and palpably arbitrary. The court held that the challenged amendment was rationally related to the legitimate legislative purpose of increasing recovery for one class and denying it for another. Persons who claimed to be supported by the intoxicated person had a derivative claim. Since there was no common law cause of action against dramshops, the legislature had always denied recovery for the intoxicated person, and it was not arbitrary for the legislature to likewise withdraw recovery for those claiming through them. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Holveck


No. 85-1457


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


171 Ill. App. 3d 38; 524 N.E.2d 1073; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 717; 121 Ill. Dec. 25



May 20, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Nicholas Zagone, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) defendant was convicted of deviate sexual assault and unlawful restraint, receiving concurrent prison terms of 25 years and 3 years for those respective crimes. Defendant appealed, contending that his arrest should have been quashed and his initial statement suppressed.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was detained, he gave an incriminating statement. In reversing his conviction, the court found that the test to be applied was whether a reasonable innocent man would have concluded that he was not free to leave when confronted with the circumstances facing defendant. The test was not a subjective one, and therefore it was irrelevant whether defendant believed he was under arrest or whether the police intended to detain defendant against his will unless that intent was conveyed to the defendant. Officers had no probable cause to arrest defendant when he was stopped, and the stop of defendant in his car clearly was a seizure for purposes of the Fourth Amendment. The seizure of defendant was investigatory in nature, calculated to elicit information from him, and there were no intervening circumstances between this detention and defendant's initial confession to break the causal connection between those events. The trial court erred in failing to quash defendant's arrest and to suppress the statements he made during his interrogation. Based on that finding the convictions had to be reversed and the cause remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions for deviate sexual assault and unlawful restraint and remanded the cause for a new trial.

 

720 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Broeckl v. Chicago Park Dist.


Nos. 85-2995, 85-3062 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


170 Ill. App. 3d 1063; 524 N.E.2d 1045; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 702; 120 Ill. Dec. 863



May 18, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied June 30, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated proceedings from a declaratory judgment class action that alleged defendant, city park district, illegally levied and collected mooring fees in excess of the costs incurred in connection with related mooring activities and that the statute which permitted such actions was unconstitutional. Plaintiffs and the district sought review of the grant of the grant of partial summary judgment by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered a judgment allowing the district to levy and collect mooring fees in excess of the expenses and costs incurred in connection with related mooring activities. The trial court also entered a judgment that the statute which permitted the district to charge a higher fee to nonresidents of the city was unconstitutional and void, and that it was unconstitutional for the district to add a 25 percent surcharge on mooring fees to nonresidents of the city. On appeal, the court held that the district was entitled to conduct a profitable operation of its harbors and since mooring fees were the main source of revenue from the harbors, it could have only been accomplished through profits derived from mooring fees. The court further held that the practice of charging higher mooring fees to nonresidents of the city was constitutional because fees charged nonresidents of such district need not be the same as fees charged to resident of the district under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 105, para. 333.23n(g) (1987).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the judgment the allowed the district to levy and collect mooring fees in excess of the expenses and costs incurred in connection with related mooring activities. The court reversed and remanded the part of the judgment, which held the statute, which permitted such actions, was unconstitutional.
