Archer Daniels Midland Co. v. Department of Revenue


No. 87-2636


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


170 Ill. App. 3d 1014; 524 N.E.2d 1010; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 694; 120 Ill. Dec. 828



May 17, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the decision by defendant Department of Revenue to assess tax, penalty and interest against the company under the Illinois and municipal use taxes, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1985, ch. 120, para. 439.3 and ch. 24, para. 8-11-6, on three jet aircraft owned by the company.


OVERVIEW: The company operated in all states but was headquartered in Illinois. It owned three airplanes which were used for business purposes. The airplanes were purchased outside Illinois but were later hangered and maintained there. They were titled in Delaware, and no use, sale, or occupation tax of any kind had been paid at the time of purchase. The department conducted a tax audit and assessed tax, interest, and penalties due under the Illinois and municipal use taxes. The company filed an appeal, but a final assessment was made. The company appealed to the circuit court, which affirmed the department's decision. Upon further appeal, the court concluded that under an economic analysis, the company's airplanes were subject to taxation as there was a substantial nexus with Illinois and there was no discrimination against interstate commerce. The company received all the benefits of the protection of Illinois laws, access to its legal system, and innumerable other services. Thus, taxes should have been assessed. However, because the airplanes were titled in Delaware, the municipal use tax was improperly imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the imposition of the Illinois use tax but reversed on the municipal use tax.

 

722 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Young


No. 86-66


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


170 Ill. App. 3d 969; 524 N.E.2d 982; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 679; 120 Ill. Dec. 800



May 16, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Roger Kiley, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for murder, armed robbery, and unlawful restraint.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, armed robbery, and unlawful restraint based on his involvement in the robbery of a grocery store and the shooting death of the store owner. The court affirmed the conviction, finding that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10.1 (1985), which allowed the admission of his codefendant's prior inconsistent statements as substantive evidence, did not violate the separation of powers doctrine by encroaching upon an exclusive judicial function because the legislature was entitled to promulgate new or alter existing rules of evidence. Section 115-10.1 was not void where it complemented Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 238, which did not control the use of such statements as substantive evidence, but stated the rule with regard to their use for impeachment purposes. The trial court's decision to admit the codefendant's prior inconsistent statement as substantive evidence against defendant did not violate the Confrontation Clause because it allowed for full cross-examination, and the credibility of the signed statement was properly reserved for the trial court. The presumption of unreliability did not attach to the statement because it was extensively cross-examined.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder, armed robbery, and unlawful restraint.

 

723 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Adams


No. 4-87-0829


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


169 Ill. App. 3d 312; 523 N.E.2d 223; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 652; 119 Ill. Dec. 755



May 12, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 3, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. John L. Davis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentence imposed in the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), upon his conviction for voluntary manslaughter, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--2(b) (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant previously pleaded guilty to voluntary manslaughter and was sentenced to 10 years' imprisonment. However, the trial court permitted him to withdraw his guilty plea. After a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of manslaughter and sentenced to 12 years' imprisonment. Defendant argued that the increased sentence violated his due process rights. On appeal, the court affirmed the 12-year sentence. The court noted that, at the sentencing hearing, no evidence was presented in aggravation or mitigation. The court declined to follow People v. Pierce, 80 Ill. App. 3d 514, 400 N.E.2d 62 (1980). The court found that that the State pointed out a number of instances that came to light at trial and appeared in the record to support the increased sentence. The court also found that the trial court did not state its reasons for the increased sentence. The court reasoned that because defendant's second trial and later conviction were the result of his own decision to withdraw his guilty plea in the original proceeding, he could not claim the protection intended for those who attack their convictions on constitutional grounds by either direct review or collateral attack.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's 12-year sentence.

 

724 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bonilla


No. 86-2874


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


170 Ill. App. 3d 26; 523 N.E.2d 1258; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 640; 120 Ill. Dec. 347



May 11, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Themis N. Karnezis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his motion for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed violence and attempted murder, and did not file a direct appeal. Defendant filed a pro se appeal for post-conviction relief, which was dismissed without a hearing. The court reversed the lower court's order dismissing defendant's appeal. The court found that the lower court did not err in dismissing defendant's petition without appointing counsel, where the lower court found the petition to be frivolous or patently without merit. The court determined that defendant was not denied his equal protection or due process rights by the lower court's decision to not award defendant an attorney. The court found that there was a rational basis for treating defendants who filed a direct appeal differently than those who filed appeals for post-conviction relief. The court concluded that the lower court did not err in denying defendant a copy of his trial transcript. The court held that the lower court committed reversible error in failing to enter its order of dismissal within thirty days of the filing of the petition because the applicable statute was mandatory and not discretionary. The court found that the dismissal was void and remanded the matter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of defendant's motion for post-conviction relief because the lower court failed to enter its order of dismissal within the statutory requirements. The court remanded the matter for reinstatement of the cause.

 

725 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Department of Registration & Education


No. 87-2756


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


170 Ill. App. 3d 40; 523 N.E.2d 1271; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 639; 120 Ill. Dec. 360



May 11, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Anthony J. Scotillo, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff chiropractor brought an action against defendant Department of Registration and Education of the State of Illinois (state), seeking to enjoin administrative proceedings against him. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed the complaint. The chiropractor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state brought administrative proceedings against the chiropractor. The chiropractor allegedly forged the name of a doctor to obtain payment for services. The hearing officer denied the chiropractor's request for a subpoena to obtain the deposition of the doctor, whom the chiropractor claimed was the sole material witness. The chiropractor sought the injunction until the subpoena issued. The court held that the chiropractor had no due process right to a prehearing discovery deposition. Pursuant to Ill. Admin. Code tit. 68, § 110.130(h)(1985), the only depositions allowed in administrative hearings were evidence depositions agreed to by the parties for use at trial. The chiropractor had an adequate remedy at law. Denial of the deposition did not threaten to hamper the chiropractor's defense. The chiropractor was provided a list of all the state's witnesses and copies of all documents. The court noted that exhaustion of administrative remedies was a prerequisite to judicial review. Upon judicial review, the chiropractor could have alleged that the state had information that would have been helpful to him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Buhle v. Chicago Bd. Options Exchange, Inc.

Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that granted the Exchange's motion to dismiss.

People v. Gill


No. 86-1144


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


169 Ill. App. 3d 1049; 523 N.E.2d 1239; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 638; 120 Ill. Dec. 328



May 10, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Kenneth Gillis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery and attempted murder, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 378, para. 8-4, 9-1, 18-2(a) (1985), following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). The trial court sentenced defendant to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed on appeal that the state failed to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt, that a bullet found in his possession was improperly admitted into evidence, and that he was denied the effective assistance of counsel. Defendant also claimed the statute under which he was sentenced, the Habitual Criminal Act (Act) was unconstitutional, and that his previous felony convictions were not proved beyond a reasonable doubt for sentencing purposes. The court affirmed, holding (1) the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's convictions, (2) defendant waived his claim regarding the bullet by failing to object to its admission and, in any event, any error in its admission was harmless in light of the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt, (3) defendant's counsel did not render ineffective assistance by admitting during his closing that defendant was guilty of robbery because he was attempting to persuade the jury to convict defendant of a lesser-included offense in an effort to remove defendant from the ambit of a life sentence as a habitual offender, (4) the Act was constitutional, and (5) the state proved defendant's prior convictions beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence on charges of armed robbery and attempted murder.

People v. Fields


No. 85-3500


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


170 Ill. App. 3d 1; 523 N.E.2d 1196; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 635; 120 Ill. Dec. 285



May 10, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Vincent Bentivenga, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for attempt to commit murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8-4 (1983). Defendant was found guilty but mentally ill and sentenced to an extended term of 45 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a food service employee, attempted to kill his manager by stabbing her 13 times with a butcher knife. Defendant was charged with attempt to commit murder, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8-4 (1983), aggravated battery, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-4 (1983), and armed violence Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1983). The jury found him guilty but mentally ill on each count. Judgment of conviction was entered on the attempted-murder count only, with the other counts merging and defendant was sentenced to 45 years in prison. Defendant appealed. The court reversed and remanded. The court first rejected defendant's due process and equal protection challenges to the guilty but mentally ill statutory provisions. As to defendant's challenge to the jury instructions, the court held that the instructions as given were not so inaccurate and misleading as to deny defendant a fair jury determination of his defense. However, the court found that the state failed to instruct the jury on the three elements of guilty but mentally ill. The court found that it was not possible to say with confidence that the jury's verdict would have been the same with the omitted instruction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of attempt to commit murder and remanded for further proceedings.

Gadeikis v. Yourell


No. 87-2796


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


169 Ill. App. 3d 1033; 523 N.E.2d 1176; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 654; 120 Ill. Dec. 265



May 9, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. George M. Marovich, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant class sought review of an order from the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), which entered summary judgment in favor of appellee, the recorder of deeds, and dismissed that class's declaratory judgment action seeking a ruling that Public Act 83-1321, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 115, para. 9.07 (1985), and Public Act 84-1464, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 115, para. 9.07, and certain county ordinances were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Public Act 83-1321, Public Act 84-1464, and Cook County, Ill., Ordinances 126617, 141697, authorized the recorder to collect an additional fee to have been deposited into a special fund that was to be used solely for the installation and maintenance of a computerized document storage system in the recorder's office. The class filed a declaratory judgment action seeking to declare that the statutes violated Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(a) (1970). The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of the recorder and dismissed the action. On review, the court determined that because the payment of salaries and expenses from a general fund, which consisted in part of fees collected by the recorder, was constitutional, it could not have been said that payment of an office expense from a special fund consisting of money from the general fund was unconstitutional. The challenged statute provided revenue for a necessary expenditure while conforming to the constitutional intent that accounting, appropriation, and disbursement of funds for the recorder's office be separated from the collection of funds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court.

People v. Westefer


No. 2-86-0642


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


169 Ill. App. 3d 59; 522 N.E.2d 1381; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 604; 119 Ill. Dec. 522



May 2, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John J. Bowman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), for armed robbery under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18-2(a) (1985), and his sentence under the habitual criminal statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B-1 (1985). Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly held that a utility knife used in the robbery was a dangerous weapon and improperly admitted and excluded evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pointed a six-inch utility knife with a one-inch blade at a store clerk to facilitate a robbery. The clerk was able to identify defendant as the robber because a bag with two holes in it that defendant wore fell from his face during the robbery. A customer noted the license plate number of the car defendant drove away in after the robbery. Police arrested defendant finding the knife and a bag with two holes in the car used in the robbery. The trial court admitted a police officer's testimony that defendant was given Miranda warnings and did not allow defendant to elicit testimony as to his own post arrest statements. The trial court refused to instruct the jury on robbery as a lesser-included offense. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that admission of the officer's testimony was not subject to the plain error doctrine since there was overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt. Defendant was not entitled to elicit testimony of his post arrest statements, since they would have been hearsay statements of his alibi. Since the utility knife could cause serious injury however it was used, the court held that defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for armed robbery and his sentence under the habitual criminal statute.

Alford v. Phipps


No. 4-87-0766


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


169 Ill. App. 3d 845; 523 N.E.2d 563; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 559; 119 Ill. Dec. 807



April 28, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Edgar County; the Hon. Richard E. Scott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff estate administrator appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Edgar County (Illinois), which granted a motion to dismiss as to defendant hospital and two defendant doctors in the administrator's wrongful death action.


OVERVIEW: An estate administrator filed a wrongful death action against a hospital and doctors. The trial court dismissed with prejudice the count against the hospital and against two of the doctors, finding that the administrator's written reports were defective for failure to comply with Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622(b) (1985), which required a certificate and written report as to each defendant. The court found that the counts against the two doctors were properly dismissed because the administrator's reports did not mention them or their involvement in the case, and the reports did not indicate that there was a reasonable and meritorious cause for filing an action against them. The court affirmed the dismissal against the hospital for failure to state a cause of action because the administrator failed to allege a cognizable theory of liability and the allegations were conclusory and unsupported. The court found that the dismissals under § 2-622 did not have to be dismissed with prejudice, and the trial court had the discretion to allow the administrator to file an amended complaint, affidavit, or written report. Accordingly, the court vacated and remanded the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and remanded the order of the court below, which dismissed with prejudice the estate administrator's wrongful death action against the hospital and two doctors. The court found that the dismissal should have been without prejudice and that the trial court had the discretion to grant the administrator a motion to amend the defective pleadings to cure the defects.

Lily of the Valley Spiritual Church v. Sims


No. 87-0676


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


169 Ill. App. 3d 624; 523 N.E.2d 999; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 537; 120 Ill. Dec. 88



April 26, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant former minister appealed the grant of temporary and permanent injunctions against her by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) at the request of plaintiff church.


OVERVIEW: Following a dispute, the former minister was ousted from the church. Notwithstanding her ouster, the former minister still attempted to perform her previous duties at the church, and on a couple of occasions she refused to leave the church premises when requested to do so by the church's pastor. The church filed a petition for a temporary restraining order and a preliminary injunction, and the lower court granted the church a permanent injunction even though the church had not requested permanent relief. The lower court permanently enjoined the former minister from interfering with religious services, conducting meetings, and from contesting the right of the pastor to designate the method of religious service. The court reversed the lower court, holding that although there was adequate evidence to support a preliminary injunction, the former minister's due process rights were violated when the lower court issued a permanent injunction on its own initiative. The court ruled that the lower court on remand was required to particularize the restrictions it placed on the former minister so that her First Amendment rights were not violated by overly broad and vague restrictions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's grant of a permanent injunction against the minister and in favor of the church which restricted the minister's ability to take part in church activities. The matter was remanded to the lower court with directions to particularize the restrictions it placed on the minister in order to protect her First Amendment rights.

People v. Ambrose


No. 86-2829


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Ronald A. Himel, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment, after a bench trial, of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of burglary pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-1 (1985) and possession of a stolen motor vehicle in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-103 (1985).


OVERVIEW: The police officer who testified at trial stated that he saw defendant inside of a stolen car, attempting to pry the radio out of the car. The officer also testified that the stolen car had no tires and that he saw four tires in the backseat of defendant's car. The officer further stated that defendant confessed that he stole the car because he needed new tires for his car. The state, however, was unable to produce the tires at trial so that the owner of the stolen car could identify them. Defendant was convicted of burglary and possession of a stolen motor vehicle. The court also rejected defendant's claim that § 4-103, which was a lesser included offense of theft, was unconstitutional solely because it could possibly result in a longer sentence than the crime of theft.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of burglary and possession of a stolen motor vehicle.

736 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wade


No. 3-87-0576


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


167 Ill. App. 3d 921; 522 N.E.2d 285; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 475; 118 Ill. Dec. 830



April 12, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. Calvin R. Stone, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which convicted him of one count of armed violence in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1985) and of one count of attempted armed robbery in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8-4(a) (1985). The trial court sentenced defendant to a term of seven years' imprisonment for the armed violence only.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of armed violence and attempted armed robbery, he was sentenced to a term of seven years' imprisonment for the armed violence only. Defendant sought review, contending that the armed violence statute was unconstitutionally applied. Defendant also alleged that there was prosecutorial misconduct during closing arguments and that the trial judge erred in refusing to answer the deliberating jurors' questions. The court found that, although the two offenses were initially classified identically, when the gun was introduced, intimidation was elevated to a more serious crime than attempted armed robbery. The court ruled that this resulted in an unconstitutionally disproportionate sentencing scheme. The court examined the prosecutor's remarks and held that they did not diminish the presumption of innocence and the reasonable doubt standard. The court held that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion by submitting the answer that he did because the instructions to the jury were sufficient.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction for armed violence and vacated the sentence that was imposed for this offense. The court remanded the matter to the trial court for the entry of a judgment of conviction for attempted armed robbery and for sentencing to proceed accordingly.

 

737 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jones


No. 85-2154


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


168 Ill. App. 3d 925; 522 N.E.2d 1325; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 460; 119 Ill. Dec. 466



April 12, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Gino L. Di Vito, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to 100 to 300 years in prison. He filed a post-conviction petition alleging ineffective assistance of trial counsel and prosecutorial misconduct. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed the petition, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: When defendant's petition came before the trial court, he was not represented by counsel. The trial court determined that the petition was frivolous and insufficient to support any post-conviction relief. The court reversed and remanded because defendant's post-conviction petition was not ruled upon within 30 days of its filing. The 30-day rule of the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-2.1(a) (1985), was mandatory, and noncompliance rendered a dismissal void. Defendant sufficiently alleged meritorious constitutional claims. Defendant alleged that defense counsel prevented him from testifying, and he alleged prosecutorial misconduct and ineffective assistance of counsel. The allegations in defendant's petition could not have been raised on appeal because they were not found in the record. Therefore, he could not be deemed to have waived the issues.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing defendant's post-conviction petition was reversed, and the case was remanded with directions to proceed in accordance with the Post-Conviction Hearing Act.

 

738 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


City of Belleville v. Human Rights Com.


No. 5-86-0804


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


167 Ill. App. 3d 834; 522 N.E.2d 268; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 425; 118 Ill. Dec. 813



April 6, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for review of order of Human Rights Commission.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee applicant filed a complaint against appellant board of police and fire commissioners and alleged handicap discrimination in violation of the Illinois Human Rights Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 64, para. 1 - 101 et seq. (1985). Appellee Illinois Human Rights Commission found that the board unlawfully discriminated against the applicant and awarded the applicant the position he applied for. The board and applicant sought review.


OVERVIEW: The applicant applied for the position of probationary patrol officer. He passed the written test, but failed the vision test. The board denied him the position and the applicant brought this action. The court affirmed the commission's decision in favor of the applicant. The applicant was able to do his job and was qualified. Thus, he met his burden of establishing a prima facie case of discrimination. There was no evidence to indicate that the uncorrected vision requirement was the minimum degree of vision acuity necessary to perform the job. It was simply an arbitrary requirement. The board failed to articulate a legitimate, nondiscriminatory reason for its vision standard. Thus, the standard violated public policy. The court found that the commission properly awarded the applicant the position he applied for, rather than a position without probationary status that he requested. The commission did not have the power to grant the applicant anything more than the job he originally applied for.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commission's decision in favor of the applicant in his discrimination action against the board.

 

739 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Satellink of Chicago, Inc. v. Chicago


No. 86-2772


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


168 Ill. App. 3d 689; 523 N.E.2d 13; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 384; 119 Ill. Dec. 545



March 29, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the city of Chicago and the director of the department of revenue (city), sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment to plaintiff provider of subscription television service invalidating an amendment of the Chicago amusement tax, Chicago, Ill. Mun. Code ch. 104, § 104 -- 1 (1984-85). The provider cross-appealed the court's denial of attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The service provider installed and operated systems designed to provide television programming to subscribers in high-rise apartment buildings from a single satellite or microwave receiver. The city amended its amusement tax ordinance to cover cable and subscription television but provided an exception for any entity with whom the city had entered into a franchise agreement. The service provider brought suit seeking to have the amendment declared invalid and also seeking attorney fees. The trial court ruled in favor of the provider but denied its claim for attorney fees. On appeal, the court affirmed the declaration that the amendment was invalid but reversed the denial of attorney fees. The court held that, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, there were no special circumstances justifying a denial of fees. With respect to the amendment, the court found that no compelling governmental interest justified the tax exempt status granted to franchised cable television. The court held that the distinction the city tried to make between franchised cable television and subscription television was the kind of arbitrary legislative choice the equal protection clause forbids.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment finding that the amendment to the amusement tax was unconstitutional, vacated the circuit court's denial of attorney fees to plaintiff, and remanded for a determination of the appropriate fees.

Friendship Facilities, Inc. v. Region 1B Human Rights Authority

Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 701 et seq. (1985), was constitutional.

The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment and its holding that the Guardianship and Advocacy Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. Ch. 91 1/2, para. 701 et seq. (1985), was constitutional and constitutionally applied to the corporation. The court held that the legislature had sufficiently identified: (1) the eligible, disabled persons who were subject to regulation and the services to be regulated in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 1-102 et seq. (1985), which was within the guidelines of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 702(h) (1985).

Peoria v. Johnson


No. 3-87-0433


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


167 Ill. App. 3d 592; 521 N.E.2d 576; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 359; 118 Ill. Dec. 294



March 24, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 2, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. Charles A. Covey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bartender sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois) that found in favor of appellee city and fined the bartender for violating Peoria, Ill., Municipal Code § 3-24 because the bartender did not have a bartender's permit.


OVERVIEW: The bartender operated a bar for nearly two years without a bartender's permit. The owner was issued a complaint for violating § 3-24. Section 3-24 required that a bartender hold a bartender's permit. The parties stipulated to facts substantiating the ordinance violation, and a jury returned a directed verdict against the bartender and assessed a fine of $ 50. The bartender's two oral motions to dismiss the complaint on the grounds of vagueness and unconstitutionality of the subject ordinance were denied. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that the only power of the municipality to regulate the sale of alcoholic beverages was that conferred upon it by the State under the Liquor Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 115(d) (1985). The court noted that the Illinois Supreme Court made it clear that the subject ordinance requiring bartending permits was invalid in that it was beyond the ambit of the provisions of the Liquor Control Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the fine imposed upon the bartender for violation of the city ordinance regarding bartender permits.

People v. Robertson


No. 86-2227


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


168 Ill. App. 3d 132; 522 N.E.2d 239; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 332; 118 Ill. Dec. 784



March 16, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 29, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Frank W. Meekins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-13, 12-16 (1985). The trial court sentenced defendant to a term of 10 years for criminal sexual assault and a concurrent five-year term for aggravated criminal sexual abuse.


OVERVIEW: During an investigation of the use of the mail to distribute child pornography, a federal agent questioned defendant, who admitted fondling a child of one of his co-workers. He also admitted his conduct to the parents. The child, who was eight years old, testified with the help of an anatomically correct doll that defendant had put his finger in her vagina. Her mother was allowed to testify to the process of investigation and statements the child made at the time. Defendant was convicted and sentenced. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The hearsay testimony of the child's pretrial statements was admissible under the exception provided in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10 (1985). The child was competent and was available for cross-examination. Defendant did not show that claimed errors by his trial counsel resulted in substantial prejudice to him. Defendant's sentence was within statutory requirements, and there was no equal protection violation in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3(c)(2)(H), which allowed probation only if the criminal sexual assault defendant was a family member of the victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

People v. Edwards


No. 2-86-0341


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


167 Ill. App. 3d 324; 521 N.E.2d 185; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 306; 118 Ill. Dec. 117



March 11, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Fred A. Geiger, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) that convicted him of voluntary manslaughter, attempted murder, and armed violence. Defendant challenged Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115--10.1, and claimed that the trial court erred in excusing a juror for cause, in denying his motions for continuance, and in entering a judgment of conviction on both the armed violence and the attempted murder guilty verdicts.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant not guilty of murder but guilty of voluntary manslaughter, attempted murder, and armed violence. The trial court entered a judgment of conviction on all three verdicts but imposed concurrent eight-year terms on only two of the convictions, voluntary manslaughter and armed violence. Defendant appealed from his convictions. The court affirmed in part and vacated the armed violence conviction. The court found that the state acknowledged that it was improper for defendant to be convicted of both attempted murder and armed violence because both offenses arose from the same physical act. The court concluded that judgment should have been entered and sentenced imposed only on the more serious offense, but declined to serve as sentencing court and remanded the cause for sentencing on the attempted murder conviction. The court rejected defendant's claim of unconstitutionality as to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115--10.1, and found that the trial court properly excused the juror for cause because he was unwilling to accept and follow the law of the case. The court concluded that the denial of defendant's motion for continuance was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment in part and vacated defendant's armed violence conviction and remanded the cause for sentencing on the attempted murder conviction.

People v. Kerney


No. 85-1666


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


168 Ill. App. 3d 72; 522 N.E.2d 229; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 300; 118 Ill. Dec. 774



March 11, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert Sklodowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded, with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that dismissed his petition for postconviction relief, which was based on defendant's conviction for residential burglary in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-3 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of residential burglary and filed a petition for postconviction relief. The trial court denied the petition, and defendant sought review. The court reversed, finding that the trial court's dismissal occurred outside the 30-day period prescribed by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-2.1(a) (Supp. 1984). The court held that under § 122-2.1(a), all dismissals of postconviction relief petitions were to be made within 30 days of the date of the filing of the petition and that the requirements of § 122-2.1(a) were mandatory because the section stated that courts "shall" enter the order within 30 days. Because the petition was not properly dismissed under § 122-2.1(a), § 122-2.1(b) required the trial court to docket the petition for further consideration. Thus, remand to the trial court was necessary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of defendant's petition for postconviction relief and remanded to the trial court.

People v. Neither

Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of one count of armed robbery. 747 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Caldwell v. Nolan


No. 88-0583


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


167 Ill. App. 3d 1057; 522 N.E.2d 175; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 256; 118 Ill. Dec. 720



March 8, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Eugene L. Wachowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions; writ awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff candidate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion to dismiss filed by the defendants, a state senator and members of an election board, in the candidate's mandamus action, which sought to remove the state senator's name from an election ballot.


OVERVIEW: The candidate filed a mandamus action against the election board after they ruled that the state senator's name could not be on the election ballot because he was not a registered voter then subsequently amended their ruling to allow the state senator's name to appear on the ballot because his name was accidentally removed from the voter rolls. The candidate contended that the election board could not amend their initial ruling under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 10 -- 10 (1985). The trial court held defendant election board was authorized to rehear a decision as long as no new evidence is introduced and granted the candidate's motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision and remanded with instructions to issue a writ of mandamus and to stay proclamation of the election results until all issues are determined. The court held that para. 10 -- 10 did not give the election board the authority to rehear the case and that absent any clear statutory language, the election board lacked jurisdiction to rehear or modify its initial decisions. Further, a writ of mandamus would have expunged a void order of the election board.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of the candidate's motion to dismiss and remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to issue a writ of mandamus to expunge the election board's modification that allowed the state senator's name on the election ballot and to stay proclamation of any election results until the remaining issues were finally settled.

People v. Carrasquilla


No. 86-1292


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


167 Ill. App. 3d 1069; 522 N.E.2d 139; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 263; 118 Ill. Dec. 684



March 8, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended October 6, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas P. Durkin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver and imposed a large monetary fine.


OVERVIEW: After a search, the police found five bags of cocaine in different locations in defendant's apartment. Defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver and received a large fine. The court affirmed defendant's conviction but remanded the case for a hearing to determine the "street value" of the actual drug seized for imposition of a proper fine. The court instructed the trial court to determine whether it intended to sentence defendant solely under § 5--9--1.1 of the Unified Code of Corrections (Code), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005 -- 9 -- 1.1 (1985), which established a fine based on "street value" of drugs, or in conjunction with § 5-- 9--1 of the Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005--9--1 (1983). An officer's opinion, standing alone, was insufficient to establish the street value of the drugs in the absence of some evidence establishing the purity of the substance. The trial court did not err by seizing a bond posted by defendant's family members in order to satisfy the fine. Defendant had the requisite control over the apartment from which the trial court could have inferred knowledge and possession of the drugs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver but remanded the case for a hearing to determine the "street value" of the actual drug seized for imposition of a proper fine.

Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


166 Ill. App. 3d 881; 520 N.E.2d 1097; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 233; 117 Ill. Dec. 746

DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which dismissed its petition for administrative review of an opinion and direction of election issued by defendant, the Illinois State Labor Relations Board (board).


OVERVIEW: The board issued an opinion certifying a group of police officers and detectives employed by the city as an appropriate unit for collective-bargaining representation and directing that an election be held to determine representative status. The city filed a petition with the trial court seeking administrative review of the opinion and direction of election. The trial court dismissed the city's petition. Further, the court found that a unit-representation decision of the board was not directly reviewable in the courts by a writ of certiorari. Finally, the board's opinion was not an unlawful exercise of its delegated authority thereby subjecting the decision to direct review in the trial courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which dismissed the city's petition for administrative review of an opinion and direction of election issued by the board.

David E. Shelton Productions, Inc. v. Chicago


No. 87-1495


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


167 Ill. App. 3d 54; 520 N.E.2d 1073; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 223; 117 Ill. Dec. 722



March 1, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert L. Sklodowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff juice bar owner challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his suit against appellee city for a permanent injunction and a declaratory judgment that the amended ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code, ch. 104.1 -- 7 (1987), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city amended Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code, ch. 104.1 -- 7 (1987), which placed restrictions on the operation of the juice bar owner's establishment. The juice bar owner sought an injunction, and the trial court dismissed his complaint with prejudice. The court affirmed and held that the amended ordinance was not unconstitutional. Accordingly, there was the requisite relationship between the ordinance and the city council's legitimate objectives. Community approval was a proper requirement mandated by the ordinance because the public interest was affected. The municipality had the authority to alter the benefits and responsibilities that the juice bar owner, as a license holder, received from his license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that dismissed with prejudice the juice bar owner's action against the city.

Beeding v. Miller


No. 2-87-0899


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


167 Ill. App. 3d 128; 520 N.E.2d 1058; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 237; 117 Ill. Dec. 707



March 1, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 7, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. Paul A. Logli, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlord and defendant tenant both appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which entered a judgment in favor of the tenant in the landlord's eviction action and a judgment in favor of the landlord and his wife on the tenant's counterclaim. The landlord challenged the trial court's interpretation of § 8 of the Mobile Home Landlord and Tenant Rights Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 80, para. 208 (1985).


OVERVIEW: The landlord notified the tenant that his lease would not be renewed at the end of the term because his yard was not maintained and the disposal of garbage created a health hazard. The tenant refused to move, and the landlord instituted an eviction action. The tenant counterclaimed, alleging that the landlord and his wife violated various statutes and ordinances. The trial court found that the Act required proof of cause for nonrenewal, that the Act was constitutional, that the landlord was not entitled to a judgment of eviction, and that the tenant failed to provide sufficient evidence to support relief on his counterclaim. The court affirmed, holding that: 1) the trial court properly found that proof of cause was required by § 8 of the Act; 2) the Act did not violate due process, equal protection, the special legislation provision of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 (1970), or the right to contract; 3) it was not against the manifest weight of the evidence for the trial court to determine that the landlord failed to prove cause for nonrenewal; and 4) the evidence supported the trial court's finding that the tenant did not offer sufficient proof to prevail on his counterclaim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the tenant on the landlord's eviction complaint. The court also affirmed the judgment in favor of the landlord and his wife on the tenant's counterclaim.

People v. Poole


No. 84-197


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


167 Ill. App. 3d 7; 520 N.E.2d 1017; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 230; 117 Ill. Dec. 666



February 23, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert L. Sklodowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that denied his motions to suppress evidence and identification testimony, convicted him of armed robbery, and sentenced him to life in prison as a habitual offender, as provided in § 33B-1 of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B-1 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that, because the police officer that arrested him did not have probable cause to believe he had committed a crime, the evidence seized during a search of his vehicle after his arrest should have been suppressed. Defendant also argued that the victim's show-up identification testimony should have been suppressed. The court affirmed the conviction. The court found that the officer had probable cause to arrest defendant based on an accurate, detailed description of the suspect, defendant's nearness in time and place to the scene of the crime, the fact that defendant did not live in the neighborhood, and defendant's attempted flight when the officer approached him. The court similarly found that the search incident to the lawful arrest was based on probable cause reasoning that the crime defendant was suspected of committing involved a weapon and defendant bent down as if to reach beneath the seat of the vehicle when the officer approached. The court opined that an immediate show-up identification near the scene of a crime was a proper police procedure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders denying defendant's motions to suppress evidence and identification testimony and affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of armed robbery.

 

753 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Petitioners Seeking to Incorporate Frankfort Square v. Vill. of Frankfort (In re Proposed Incorporation)


No. 3-87-0607


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


166 Ill. App. 3d 146; 519 N.E.2d 721; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 191; 116 Ill. Dec. 653



February 22, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Herman S. Haase, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner residents sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which sustained intervenor villages' objections to the residents' proposed incorporation of a new village, dismissed the application, and denied a motion for stay pending appeal. The issue was whether the residents had complied with the Illinois Municipal Code.


OVERVIEW: The residents filed a petition to incorporate a village pursuant to the Illinois Municipal Code (Code), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 2-3-5a (1985), that consisted of at least four square miles, no part of which lies within any existing city or village; that approximately 7,900 residents lived in the area; and that the proposed name had not been adopted by another municipality. The villages, both of which were within 1 1/2 miles of the proposed incorporation area, one of whom annexed part of the territory during the pendency of the action, claimed that their consent was a precondition to approval. The trial court dismissed the petition to incorporate and denied a stay pending appeal, and the residents sought review. The court affirmed the judgment and held that: (1) the annexation could not be accomplished while the action was pending; (2) the villages' intervention was proper pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 1-106 (1985); (3) by the 1980 census, the area contained less than the required number of residents and approval of the villages was a prerequisite; and (4) under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 1-7-2 (1985), the most recent federal census was conclusive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that upheld the villages' objections to the residents' petition to incorporate a village.

 

754 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Application of Walgenbach


Nos. 2-87-0503, 2-87-0504 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


166 Ill. App. 3d 629; 520 N.E.2d 78; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 180; 117 Ill. Dec. 88



February 19, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County; the Hon. James C. Franz, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent tax objectors appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) denying their objections to taxes levied by appellant county collector on behalf of a school district.


OVERVIEW: The Board of Education for the school district adopted a resolution abolishing its working case fund and directing that the balance in the fund be transferred to the educational fund at the end of the school year. The Board also created a new working cash fund and authorized the issuance of working cash fund bonds. Additional taxes were levied against the district's taxpayers as a result of the bond issue and the objectors challenged the levy of new taxes. The objectors, contrary to their original position, argued that the school district could have increased the working fund by issuing bonds, but it could not abolish and re-create the fund to achieve the same result. The district claims that its procedure was not prejudicial to the objectors because it did not result in issuance of bonds in excess of the amount statutorily allowed. The court found that the procedure followed by the district, permissible under the School Code, did not permit it to circumvent the statutory tax limits or levy an illegal tax against the objectors, thus, it was not improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

755 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Semersky v. West


No. 2-87-0567


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


166 Ill. App. 3d 637; 520 N.E.2d 71; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 184; 117 Ill. Dec. 81



February 19, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Fredrick Henzi, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) dismissed plaintiff patient's medical malpractice complaint against defendant doctors pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 103(b), 107 Ill. 2d R. 103(b), for her failure to exercise reasonable diligence in obtaining service after expiration of the statute of limitations. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient filed a medical malpractice action against the doctors on the day the applicable statute of limitations was to expire. The patient served only one of the doctors nine months later. The patient then voluntarily dismissed her complaint without prejudice, refiled her complaint, and served both doctors within two months. The doctors then filed their motion to dismiss under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 103(b), 107 Ill. 2d 103(b), for the patient's failure to exercise reasonable diligence in serving the original complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the trial court did not err in considering the patient's diligence in obtaining service of the original complaint and that the doctors did not waive their rights under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 103(b), 107 Ill. 2d 103(b), by filing motions and participating in the lawsuit. The court held given that the doctors' business addresses were listed in the telephone book and that there were no special circumstance preventing the patient from serving them, the patient failed to exercise reasonable diligence in serving the doctors after the expiration of the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that dismissed the patient's medical malpractice action against the doctors for the patient's failure to exercise reasonable diligence in serving the doctors after the expiration of the applicable statute of limitations.

 

756 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Ballin Drugs, Inc. v. Department of Registration & Education


No. 87-0128


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


166 Ill. App. 3d 520; 519 N.E.2d 1151; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 193; 116 Ill. Dec. 936



February 16, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph M. Wosik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants Illinois Department of Registration and Education (department) sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which reversed an order of the department revoking the licenses of appellees, pharmacy and pharmacists, and held that the "good faith" provision of Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1981, ch. 56 1/2, para. 1102(v), was unconstitutionally vague and uncertain.


OVERVIEW: The pharmacy was licensed by the department to dispense controlled substances. The department filed an action against the pharmacy and two pharmacists, seeking revocation or suspension of licenses. After a hearing before the state board of pharmacy, the department revoked the licenses, asserting that the pharmacy and pharmacists lacked good faith in dispensing schedule II controlled substances, in violation of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. 1981, ch. 56 1/2, para. 1102(v). The circuit court reversed the decision. On review, the court reversed judgment of the circuit court and held that the "good faith" provision of the act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1981, ch. 56 1/2, para. 1102(v), was not unconstitutionally vague and uncertain. The court held that the "good faith" provision of the act contained six specific guidelines to place pharmacists on notice of prohibited practices. Further, the department could utilize its experience and knowledge in determining whether there was substantial evidence to support a finding of lack of good faith, and a reviewing court would not interfere with an agency's decision to impose sanctions absent an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment in favor of the department and upheld the order of the department to revoke the licenses of the pharmacy and the pharmacists for violating the "good faith" provisions of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act.

 

757 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Little v. East Lake Fork Special Drainage Dist.


No. 4-87-0527


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


166 Ill. App. 3d 209; 519 N.E.2d 1113; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 140; 116 Ill. Dec. 898



February 11, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Creed D. Tucker, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant district appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which determined that plaintiff treasurer was entitled to reimbursement for the actual cost of his services pursuant to the Illinois Drainage Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 42, para. 4-36, 4-37 (1985). The treasurer cross-appealed the denial of its motion for judgment on the pleadings and the findings that his method of computing costs was erroneous.


OVERVIEW: After the legislature amended the Illinois Drainage Code (Code) to require reimbursement by districts to the county treasurer for his services as ex officio treasurer and collector, the district refused to pay its treasurer, and the treasurer filed an action for reimbursement. The trial court granted judgment to the treasurer, but found that his method of accounting was erroneous. Both parties cross-appealed. The court affirmed, holding that §§ 4-36, 4-37 did not violate Ill. Const. of 1970 art. VII, § 9(a) because the constitutional provision did not limit or restrict the counties and local taxing districts from contracting among themselves. The statutes were not unconstitutionally vague because their terms were not so ill defined that their meaning would be determined on the opinions and whims of the trier of fact. The statutes did not violate the equal protection clauses of the Illinois and United States Constitutions and they were not special or local laws because they did not contain unreasonable or arbitrary classifications and they operated alike upon all persons in like situations. Further, the treasurer's method of accounting was not erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that the treasurer was entitled to reimbursement for the actual cost of his services, but it reversed the judgment that the treasurer's method of computing costs was erroneous, and it entered judgment in favor of the treasurer and against the district in the amount claimed by the treasurer, plus costs.

People v. Martin


No. 85-0951


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


166 Ill. App. 3d 428; 519 N.E.2d 1085; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 162; 116 Ill. Dec. 870



February 11, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas Fitzgerald, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found him guilty but mentally ill of murder, aggravated arson, and arson, and convicted and sentenced him for murder and aggravated arson.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder, arson, and aggravated arson arising out of a fire he set at his mother's house. The trial court found him guilty but mentally ill on all charges and convicted him of murder and aggravated arson. Defendant sought review of the trial court's decision. On appeal, the court reversed defendant's aggravated arson conviction on the basis of that statute's unconstitutionality and remanded the matter for sentencing on the arson charge. The court otherwise affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that defendant's ability to rent gas cans, flight from the crime scene, and unfulfilled threats to his mother was sufficient evidence to support the trial court's conclusion that defendant was not insane and could appreciate the criminality of his conduct and control his behavior. The court also ruled that the guilty but mentally ill statute was not unconstitutional and that the burden imposed upon defendant by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 6-2(e) (1985) to prove his insanity did not violate his constitutional right to due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the trial court's decision that had convicted and sentenced defendant for aggravated arson, affirmed that part of the trial court's decision that had convicted and sentenced him for murder, and remanded the matter to the trial court for sentencing on the arson charge.

People v. Brent


No. 85-1003


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


175 Ill. App. 3d 459; 530 N.E.2d 43; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 1610; 125 Ill. Dec. 125



February 10, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing November 2, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James M. Schreier, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted him of three counts of murder, four counts of aggravated arson, and one count of arson for setting an apartment building fire that resulted in the death of one person and injuries to four others.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10.1, which allowed substantive use of prior inconsistent statements in criminal trials, was an unconstitutional legislative infringement on judicial power because it changed a rule of evidence developed by prior case law and that the aggravated arson statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para 20-1.1, was unconstitutional. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the case, finding that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10.1 did not unduly infringe on judicial power and was, therefore, a proper exercise of legislative authority. The court noted that the aggravated arson statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para 20-1.1, was unconstitutional because it did not require an unlawful purpose in setting a fire. The court further concluded that because the aggravated arson charges filed against defendant did not require proof of injury to any person, there was no multiple-victim basis for allowing defendant's single act to support a conviction for arson as well as murder.


OUTCOME: The vacated defendant's convictions and sentences for aggravated arson and felony murder, affirmed defendant's convictions on all of the other counts, and remanded the case for sentencing on the intentional murder count.

People v. Rosario


No. 86-0438


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


166 Ill. App. 3d 383; 519 N.E.2d 1020; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 116; 116 Ill. Dec. 805



February 4, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Vincent Bentivenga, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for arson and aggravated arson.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to pouring gasoline over the porch of a residence in the early morning hours and lighting it. A child died as a result of his actions, even though he did not intend to kill her. Defendant was acquitted of murder; convicted of arson and aggravated arson. He appealed. The court affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded. The court vacated the aggravated arson conviction because the statute was declared unconstitutional. The court affirmed defendant's arson conviction because there was no evidence that his confession was rendered involuntary by threats of a long prison term or death; there was sufficient evidence that defendant was familiar with the criminal justice system. The court also stated that the acquittal on the murder and the mistrial on the arson charges based on the deadlocked jury did not bar retrial of the arson charges based on double jeopardy grounds even though the arson charge was a lesser included offense of the felony murder charge.


OUTCOME: Defendant's arson conviction was affirmed; his aggravated arson conviction was vacated; and, the case was remanded for resentencing on the arson conviction.

 

761 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Application of County Collector of McHenry County


Nos. 2-87-0403, 2-87-0404, 2-87-0405 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


166 Ill. App. 3d 11; 518 N.E.2d 1253; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 115; 116 Ill. Dec. 273



February 3, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County; the Hon. James C. Franz, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a dispute over taxes due, petitioner county tax collector sought review of an order by the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) granting tax refunds to respondent tax objectors.


OVERVIEW: The Board of Education for a school district adopted a resolution abolishing its working case fund and directing that the balance in the fund be transferred to an educational fund. The Board also created a new working cash fund and authorized the issuance of working cash fund bonds. Additional taxes were levied against the district's taxpayers as a result of the bond issue and the objectors challenged the levy of new taxes. The trial court denied their objections to taxes levied by the county tax collector on behalf of a school district. The court stated that the most important criterion in the area of procedural due process was "reasonableness." The State had to act reasonably before depriving a person of a liberty or property interest. The court found that the situation involved a statutory equalization procedure in apportioning the burden of taxation for counties within an overlapping taxing district and a provision to implement that procedure when there was not a timely valuation or rate certification. The failure to provide prior notice of the extension of a deficiency tax levy or tax credit to an individual taxpayer did not present a denial of due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

People v. Bryant


No. 86-1919


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


165 Ill. App. 3d 996; 520 N.E.2d 890; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 28; 117 Ill. Dec. 539



January 20, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended July 26, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. William Cousins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of possession of a stolen motor vehicle, a class 2 felony. Defendant was sentenced three and one-half years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The conviction was defendant's first for possession of a stolen motor vehicle and there was no evidence that defendant was involved in organized vehicle theft as a profession. The court determined that it was in the interests of justice to consider the constitutionality of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95, para. 4-103(b) despite defendant's failure to preserve the issue below. The legislative scheme of increasing the penalty imposed on all defendants convicted for the first time of possession of a stolen motor vehicle was not reasonably designed to attack the evils of organized vehicle theft and chop shops. Paragraph 4-103(b) imposed a greater penalty on all such defendants than it did on those convicted of theft of a motor vehicle under the general theft statute. The amendment to para. 4-103(b) was unconstitutional because it violated the due process clause of the Illinois Constitution. It punished the lesser included offense of possession of a stolen vehicle more severely than the greater, more serious offense of theft of a motor vehicle.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was vacated and remanded.

People v. Sequoia Books, Inc.


Nos. 2-87-0074, 2-87-0157 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


165 Ill. App. 3d 143; 518 N.E.2d 775; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 33; 116 Ill. Dec. 153



January 19, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County; the Hon. Wilson D. Burnell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Orders reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, operators of an adult bookstore, appealed from a permanent injunction issued by the Circuit Court of Kendall County (Illinois), which restrained them from using a building for one year.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 37-1 et seq. (1985) the state obtained an injunction prohibiting the operators of an adult bookstore from operating at a specified location for one year. In reversing the injunctive orders, the court held there was little question that the order enjoining the operators from selling or exhibiting explicit material was a prior restraint on First Amendment rights. On the basis of past violations, the court enjoined future sales of sexually explicit materials whether or not they were actually obscene. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 37-1 et seq. (1985) was unconstitutional in its application to adult bookstores that sell sexually explicit materials.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the injunctive orders prohibiting the sale of sexually explicit materials by bookstore operators.

 

764 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jihan


No. 5-86-0582


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


165 Ill. App. 3d 507; 519 N.E.2d 22; 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 22; 116 Ill. Dec. 432



January 12, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County; the Hon. Bill F. Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of her conviction for practicing midwifery without a license in the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois). The trial court dismissed the charge of voluntary manslaughter. Defendant was sentenced to one year of probation and ordered to serve six months of "electronic home confinement."


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the statute under which she was convicted, the Medical Practice Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 4401 et seq. (1985), was unconstitutionally vague because the term midwifery was not defined. The prosecution argued that the term midwifery had a common and popularly understood meaning, that of assisting in childbirth. The court held that: (1) in the context of a criminal prosecution, the offense was not defined with sufficient definiteness that a person of ordinary intelligence could understand what conduct was prohibited in a manner that would prevent arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement; (2) while many other types of professions and activities were defined by the legislature, the term midwifery had not been defined; (3) the lack of a scienter requirement lent vagueness to the Act; (4) due process was offended because the Act was so incomplete, vague, indefinite, and uncertain that people of ordinary intelligence had to guess at its meaning and could differ as to its application; and (5) the provisions of the Act making it a crime to practice midwifery without a license were unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

People v. McGee


No. 86-0468


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


165 Ill. App. 3d 833; 520 N.E.2d 836; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3648; 117 Ill. Dec. 485



December 31, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended November 7, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Michael B. Getty, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted the defendant of possession of a weapon as a convicted felon in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1.1 (1985) and sentenced the defendant to a term of five years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted the defendant of possession of a weapon as a convicted felon in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1.1 (1985) and sentenced the defendant to a term of five years' imprisonment. The defendant appealed, contending that the trial court erred in its denial of his motion to quash his arrest and suppress the evidence obtained from an allegedly illegal detention, that the prosecution was allowed to present the prejudicial evidence of his prior rape conviction to the jury even though it was an element of the crime with which he was charged, and that para. 24-1.1 was unconstitutional on equal protection and due process grounds. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the trial court's denial of the defendant's motion to quash and suppress was not against the weight of the evidence because police officers had the minimum articulable suspicion required to stop the defendant, that there was no denial of due process in either the prosecutor's statements or the instructions given to the jury by the trial court, and that para. 24-1.1 was constitutional. There was no improper delegation of legislative power to the prosecutor in para. 24-1.1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted the defendant of possession of a weapon as a convicted felon.
