People v. Daniels


No. 2-86-0470


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


164 Ill. App. 3d 1055; 518 N.E.2d 669; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3686; 116 Ill. Dec. 47



December 31, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 2, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. John E. Sype, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which convicted her of aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentenced her to a six-year term of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with committing sexual assault upon her minor son. The evidence overwhelmingly established that defendant and her husband engaged in various acts of sexual misconduct with her son, as well as with her other minor children. Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to support her conviction. The court held that: (1) defendant was proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt based on testimony from her son, which was corroborated by his sister's eyewitness testimony; (2) the trial court did not deprive defendant of her rights to a fair trial and due process when her attorney was barred from interviewing her son and 10-year-old daughter; (3) the failure to raise the issue of her son's competency and object to the admission of physical evidence at trial waived those issues on appeal; (4) the prosecutor's introduction of sexually explicit material seized from defendant did not prejudice the trial court's judgment warranting a new trial; (5) defendant received effective assistance of counsel; and (6) defendant's argument as to the unconstitutionality of the sexual assault law lacked a constitutional basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault.

In re Call an Election on the Question of Incorporating the Vill. of Forest Knoll


No. 2-87-0202


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


164 Ill. App. 3d 392; 517 N.E.2d 1188; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3576; 115 Ill. Dec. 502



December 31, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Charles F. Scott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, city, village, and residents, appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which dismissed their petition for incorporation on motion of appellee amici curiae.


OVERVIEW: The petition for incorporation of a village was dismissed. The court vacated and remanded for proceedings in accordance with § 2-3-18 of the Illinois Municipal Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 2-3-18 (1983), which required a showing that the county board had made certain determinations before proceeding on the petition. On remand, the petition was dismissed on motion of the amici curiae, two cities. The village, the city, and the residents argued that § 2-3-5a of the Illinois Municipal Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 2-3-5a (1983) violated due process and equal protection by requiring the consent of nearby municipalities for incorporation of a village containing fewer than 7,500 residents. The court vacated the order allowing the amici curiae to file pleadings and dismissing the petition, struck the amici curiae's briefs, and remanded the case. The amici curiae lacked standing to seek dismissal of the petition. The court previously had rejected the constitutional challenges to § 2-3-5a of the Illinois Municipal Code. The trial court must resolve whether the requirements of §§ 2-3-5a, 2-3-18 of the Illinois Municipal Code had been met before proceeding with the petition.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order permitting the amici curiae to file pleadings in the case and dismissing the petition for incorporation filed by the city, village, and residents. The court remanded the case to the trial court to determine whether certain statutory requirements necessary for incorporation had been met. The court also struck the briefs of the amici curiae.

 

768 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Bloom v. Guth


No. 2-87-0267


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


164 Ill. App. 3d 475; 517 N.E.2d 1154; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3587; 115 Ill. Dec. 468



December 30, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing February 4, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Bernard E. Drew, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed from the dismissal of her five-count medical malpractice complaint against defendant doctor by the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) for her failure to provide the affidavit required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2 (1985).


OVERVIEW: The patient filed a five-count medical malpractice complaint against the doctor, seeking damages and attorneys fees. The doctor filed a motion to dismiss the complaint for failure to file an affidavit stating that, based on consultation with a health professional, there was a reasonable and meritorious cause for filing the action, as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2 (1985). The trial court dismissed the action for failure to meet the statutory requirement. The patient appealed, arguing that the statute was unconstitutional. She contended that the statute violated her rights to equal protection and due process and authorized a health professional to exercise a judicial function. On appeal, the court ruled that the statute was constitutional because it met the rational-basis test and therefore did not infringe the patient's rights to equal protection and due process. The court also concluded that the statute did not require the health professional to exercise a judicial function because the affidavit was required to contain only statements of fact, not conclusions of law. Accordingly, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the patient's complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that granted the doctor's motion for involuntary dismissal of the patient's medical malpractice complaint.

 

769 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Dunne v. County of Cook


No. 87-252


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


164 Ill. App. 3d 929; 518 N.E.2d 380; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3670; 115 Ill. Dec. 855



December 16, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. David J. Shields, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, several members of a county board of commissioners, appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) declaring unconstitutional two ordinances pertaining to the power of the board members to appoint or remove members of their staffs. Plaintiffs, the board president and two commissioners, filed the action to declare the ordinances unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The board members contended that by finding the ordinances unconstitutional, the constitutional mandate of separation of powers between the legislative and executive branches of the county government was violated. They also maintained that Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6, empowered the county board, under its home rule powers, to pass the ordinances despite the conflicting statute empowering the county president to appoint members of the commissioners' staffs. The court disagreed and affirmed the circuit court. The board members attempted to take power given by statute to the chief executive officer and improperly transfer it to the legislative body of the government. Absent submission for approval by referendum, enactment of these ordinances was improper. The court's finding regarding an improper attempt to alter the form of government applied with equal force to all positions enumerated in the employee resolution and was not based on the confidential status or duties of the employees. The fact that the action constituted a change in the form of government, requiring referendum approval, also limited the home rule powers invoked by the board members.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Mitsuuchi v. Chicago


No. 84-2886


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


164 Ill. App. 3d 815; 518 N.E.2d 313; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3620; 115 Ill. Dec. 788



December 11, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Lester D. Foreman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed her complaint against defendants, city and fellow police officer, for personal injuries sustained in the course of her employment. Defendants' motions to strike and dismiss was based on the Illinois Pension Code, Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 22-306 and 307 (1985).


OVERVIEW: The police officer was injured when her fellow officer wrecked the squad car in which they were driving. The court held that under the Illinois Pension Code the trial court properly dismissed the police officer's cause of action against the city, but reversed the trial court as to the claim against her fellow officer. The court held that although the police officer was prohibited from receiving a double recovery, she was entitled to continue her claim against her fellow officer for the alleged negligence The court held that there would be no double recovery because the city had a subrogation right to receive the amount of benefits paid to the police officer from any recovery that she obtained by reason of her action against her fellow officer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the police officer's negligence claim against her fellow officer for personal injuries sustained during the course of her employment.

 

771 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Quincy v. Carlson


No. 4-87-0320


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


163 Ill. App. 3d 1049; 517 N.E.2d 33; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3739; 115 Ill. Dec. 68



December 10, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Adams County; the Hon. Robert L. Welch, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois), which upheld the constitutionality of the § 4(q) notice provision under the Illinois Environmental Protection Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1004(q) (1985). The trial court dismissed the remaining counts against the Illinois Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) for failure to state a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: After the EPA had certified the city's landfill closed and covered, it issued a § 4(q) notice under the act to the city. The notice informed the city that there was an actual or threatened release of a hazardous substance from the site, which presented an imminent and substantial endangerment to public safety. The notice outlined the specific steps the city had to take to comply with the act. It also informed the city that there was potential liability for punitive damages if the city did not comply "without sufficient cause" pursuant to § 22.2 of the act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1022.2 (1985). The city challenged the constitutionality of the notice provision. Upon review, the court found that the notice provision of the act was constitutional because the protection of the public health and safety was a paramount governmental interest that justified the summary administrative action. The court determined that the lack of a pre-enforcement hearing did not offend due process principles because the act gave the city the opportunity to assert a good-faith defense to the validity of the order prior to the imposition of a penalty. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the constitutionality of the notice provision under the act and affirmed the dismissal of the remaining counts against the EPA for failure to state a cause of action.

People v. Manley


No. 2-86-0940


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


163 Ill. App. 3d 950; 516 N.E.2d 1343; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3727; 114 Ill. Dec. 949



December 8, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Bernard E. Drew, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction of two counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-16(b) (1985), by the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois). Defendant claimed that the trial court erroneously admitted evidence of his prior sexual acts with the victims and that the statute violated his equal protection rights when compared with Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para 12-15(a) (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of sexually abusing the victims, his adopted daughters. The trial court admitted the victims' testimony as to defendant's prior sexual misconduct with them after defendant had questioned the victims as to their failure to report the earlier conduct. The court instructed the jury that the testimony was admitted to explain the victims' previous silence and not as evidence of the crimes charged. Defendant claimed that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para 12-16(b) (1985) denied him equal protection of laws because it punished non-violent sexual acts more severely than sexual abuse by force, more egregious conduct criminalized by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-15(a) (1985). On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the victims' testimony about defendant's prior sexual misconduct with them was properly admitted to explain their earlier silence, given the limiting instruction and the fact that defendant had raised the issue. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para 12-16(b) (1985) did not violate the equal protection clause since it was reasonable for the legislature to have found that sexual misconduct with a family member was more egregious than that by force.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of aggravated sexual abuse.

People v. Sims


Nos. 84-2337; 84-2717


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


166 Ill. App. 3d 289; 519 N.E.2d 921; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3795; 116 Ill. Dec. 706



December 7, 1987

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert Sklodowski, Judge, presiding



DISPOSITION: 84 -- 2337, Affirmed.

84 -- 2717, Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants both appealed from decisions of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, in separate jury trials, convicted one defendant of rape and convicted the other defendant of rape and deviate sexual assault. Both defendants were sentenced to natural life terms.


OVERVIEW: After defendants abducted a woman and raped her, they were charged with rape and deviate sexual assault. One defendant was convicted of both charges, and the other defendant was convicted on only the rape charge. Both were sentenced to natural life terms. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and the sentences given defendants. The court held, inter alia, that: (1) complainant's testimony that she had been raped was sufficient to prove penetration; (2) the acquittal of one defendant on the deviate sexual assault charge did not cast doubt on his conviction for rape, as deviate sexual assault required completely different acts; (3) there was no Brady violation, because the state tendered everything it had in its possession; (4) the acquittal of one defendant on the deviate sexual assault charge did not raise any doubt as to other defendant's guilt, as each was tried separately with somewhat different evidence; (5) the complainant's testimony sufficiently proved venue; (6) the search of the car in which the crimes occurred was reasonable under the circumstances; and (6) the Habitual Criminal Statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B -- 1 (1981), was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and the sentences of both defendants and ruled that defendants were properly found guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.

OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal and the complaint for retaliatory discharge underlying it based on a federal court decision.

In re Application of Anderson


No. 2-86-0574


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


162 Ill. App. 3d 815; 516 N.E.2d 860; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3445; 114 Ill. Dec. 705



November 24, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. William F. Homer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent landowners appealed the final order from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) that denied their motion to vacate and set aside the order that found petitioner county fully complied with the Revenue Act of 1939 (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 482 et seq., was entitled to tax deeds after it struck their redemptions under protest, and that found the Act constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the tax deeds issued to the county. The court held that the penalty provisions of § 253 of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 734 (1983), did not contravene due process or any usury laws. The court determined that use of permanent real estate index numbers in advertisements and notices of sale were proper legal descriptions of the properties pursuant to §§ 228, 30, and 1 of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 709, 511, and 482(19) (1983). The county satisfied the requirement of § 239 of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 720 (1983), because the county clerk did certify a tax judgment, its entry upon the record, and issued certificates of purchase to the county against the delinquent properties prior to their sale. The county could make non-cash bids as specifically authorized by § 216d of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 697d (1983). Finally, the petitions for tax sale could be filed separately for each delinquent property, and need not have been combined under on notice, pursuant to § 263 of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 744 (1983). Further, the county's approach was reasonable based upon advice given it by a title company.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the final order that found the county was entitled to tax deeds after determining that the penalty provisions of the Act were neither unconstitutional, nor violated the state's usury laws, the advertisements of notices for tax sale were adequate, the county fully complied with the Act, and the county was authorized to made non-cash bids.

First Federal Sav. & Loan Asso. v. Sadnick


Nos. 3-87-0065, 3-87-0203 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mortgagor challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of La Salle County (Illinois), which entered a decree for foreclosure in favor of plaintiff mortgagee.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagor defaulted on a mortgage obtained from mortgagee. The mortgagee filed a complaint for foreclosure against the mortgagor. The mortgagor filed a motion to dismiss the complaint and contended that the mortgage was invalid because an attorney did not prepare it. The trial court denied the motion and the mortgagor filed a motion to vacate the decree for foreclosure. The trial court also denied the motion to vacate and the county sheriff sold the property. The mortgagor appealed and contended that the trial court erred when it failed to dismiss the mortgagee's complain because the mortgage was not prepared by an attorney and that the fee collected by the sheriff for selling the property was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the mortgagee was not practicing law when it prepared the mortgages. The mortgagee prepared the mortgages for its purposes, did not provide legal advice to the mortgagor, and did not prohibit the mortgagor from retaining an attorney. The court also held that the sheriff's collection of a fee for selling the property was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the mortgagee.

People v. Gulley


No. 2-86-0758


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


162 Ill. App. 3d 545; 515 N.E.2d 1309; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3404; 114 Ill. Dec. 38



November 18, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. John C. Layng, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action filed by the People of the State of Illinois, defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which convicted her of arson and that imposed a sentence. Defendant contended that arson was not a lesser included offense of aggravated arson, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1(a)(1) (1983), when the offense was committed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated arson under para. 20-1.1(a)(1). After defendant committed the offense, this provision was found unconstitutional because the fact that mental state for arson was greater than that for aggravated arson. Arson was not a lesser included offense of aggravated arson. The trial court, finding that arson was a lesser included offense of aggravated arson, convicted defendant of arson. The court vacated the judgment. Though the issue of whether arson was a lesser included offense when the crime was committed had not been raised by defendant, substantial justice required the court to overlook the waiver rule. The judgment required vacatur because arson was not a lesser included offense of aggravated arson when the crime was committed.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment that convicted defendant of, and that sentenced her for, arson.

People v. Newman


No. 3-87-0287


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


163 Ill. App. 3d 865; 516 N.E.2d 667; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3716; 114 Ill. Dec. 512



November 6, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified Opinion Filed December 2, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Edwin B. Grabiec, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), where a jury found him guilty of driving with a breath-alcohol concentration of .10 or more and failure to dim headlights. The trial court denied his motions for a new trial, for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, and in arrest of judgment. Defendant was fined $ 300 and ordered to successfully complete a remedial driving course. He then filed this appeal.


OVERVIEW: At the hearing on defendant's pretrial petition to rescind the statutory summary suspension of his driver's license, the officer who administered the breathalyzer did not testify, and the State failed to establish that the defendant was observed continuously for 20 minutes before the test was given. Based on the lack of foundation, the trial court refused to admit the test results, and rescinded the summary suspension. Defendant argued that the trial court's ruling at the suspension hearing collaterally estopped the State from introducing the results at trial. The court found that collateral estoppel did not apply because the question of whether the State laid a proper foundation at the suspension hearing was a question of law, and collateral estoppel applied only to issues of fact. Additionally, the trial court's ruling on the foundation objection was not a final judgment on the merits of an ultimate issue. The court also found that the evidence was sufficient for the jury to have found beyond a reasonable doubt that the defendant had at least a .10 concentration of alcohol in his breath at the time of his driving.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for driving with a breath-alcohol concentration of .10 or more and failure to dim headlights.

People v. Hinton

The court rejected defendant's arguments just as it had rejected similar and like arguments in prior cases.

People v. Warren

Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District

November 4, 1987, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Henry County (Illinois) that convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12 -- 14(b)(1) (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated sexual assault after molesting his six-year old nephew. Jojan Corp. v. Kusper


No. 86-0287


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


173 Ill. App. 3d 622; 528 N.E.2d 989; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3811; 124 Ill. Dec. 98



November 2, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing September 19, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Benjamin S. Mackoff, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer brought a mandamus and declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of § 235a of the Revenue Act of 1939, as amended, known as the Scavenger Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 716a (1983). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted defendant county clerk's motion to dismiss, finding that the taxpayer had an adequate remedy at law and that the amendment was constitutional. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The challenged amendment to the Act provided that except for single family residential units being owner-occupied condominium units, cooperative units, or dwellings, the amount required to be paid for redemption shall include an amount equal to all delinquent taxes on such property which taxes were delinquent at the time of sale. To protect its security interest in real estate sold at a scavenger sale, the taxpayer sought redemption under the Act. The county clerk rejected the taxpayer's tender for redemption because it did not include an amount equal to all the delinquent taxes due as of the time of sale as required by the Act. The taxpayer sought mandamus and declaratory relief. The trial court dismissed the taxpayer's action. The taxpayer sought review. The court held that, because the Act provided an adequate remedy at law to adjudicate the sufficiency of the redemption by paying the required amount under protest, the taxpayer was not entitled to equitable relief where there was no showing that the tax was unauthorized by law, that the property was exempt from taxation, or that the tax was fraudulent. As such, it was unnecessary to reach the constitutional question.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's judgment that found declaratory relief was improper because there was an adequate remedy at law. However, the court vacated and set aside the portion of the trial court's judgment regarding the constitutionality of the amendment to the Act.

Bruce v. Halterman-Flynn


No. 3-86-0834


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


162 Ill. App. 3d 248; 515 N.E.2d 410; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3367; 113 Ill. Dec. 601



October 30, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County; the Hon. John Donald O'Shea, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administrator sought review by certified question of an order entered in the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois) denying appellant's motion to dismiss appellee administrator 's counterclaim filed under the Wrongful Death Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 70, paras. 1,2 (1985).


OVERVIEW: Two motorboats collided on the Mississippi River resulting in the death of two occupants of one of the motorboats. More than two years after the accident, appellee filed a wrongful death counterclaim against appellant in the wrongful death action previously filed by appellant against appellee. Appellant filed a motion to dismiss on grounds that the counterclaim was untimely. On appeal of the trial court's denial of the motion, the court reversed and held that the counterclaim should have been dismissed as untimely filed. The court determined that the trial court erred in failing to follow the rule that a counterclaim for wrongful death based upon the same facts as the original claim required dismissal as untimely filed if not filed within the two-year time period set forth in the Wrongful Death Act. The court further determined that the rule denying wrongful death victims the right to file counterclaims when personal injury victims were allowed to pursue otherwise time-barred claims under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-207 (1985) did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order denying appellant's motion to dismiss appellee's counterclaim filed under the Wrongful Death Act.

People v. Williams

788 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Morrison


Nos. 2-84-0623, 2-84-1067 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


162 Ill. App. 3d 299; 515 N.E.2d 356; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3373; 113 Ill. Dec. 547



October 26, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. Robert J. French, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted of obscenity based on the alleged sale of obscene magazines. After the convictions were upheld, defendants appealed to the United States Supreme Court, which reversed the judgments and remanded the cases for a determination of whether the constitutional violation of the jury having been instructed to apply the contemporary community standards in deciding the value question was harmless error.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed defendants' convictions of obscenity, but vacated one defendant's sentence and remanded his case for resentencing. The court held that no rational juror, if properly instructed, could have found value in the magazines in question because the obscenity of the magazines is obvious from the materials themselves, and, therefore, the trial court's improper jury instruction constituted harmless error. The court noted that defendants' guilt of the offense of selling obscene materials was "blatantly evident" from the materials themselves. The court rejected defendants' contention that the error in the instruction could not have been harmless unless the court reconstrued the Illinois obscenity statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20 (1983), as constitutional. The court concluded that analysis of the statute was not necessary because the United States Supreme Court did not find the statute to be unconstitutional and the statute did not require the social value of allegedly obscene material to be adjudged on community standards. The court also concluded that although one defendant may have failed to preserve the error, interests of justice required review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions of obscenity, but vacated one defendant's sentence and remanded his case for resentencing.

 

789 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Federated Distribs., Inc. v. Johnson


No. 86-2572


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


163 Ill. App. 3d 27; 516 N.E.2d 471; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3477; 114 Ill. Dec. 316



October 22, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended April 7, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff beverage manufacturer appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that upheld the constitutionality of a ruling by defendant Illinois Department of Revenue, which imposed a $ 2-per-gallon tax on a product produced by the manufacturer. The tax was imposed pursuant to the Liquor Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 94 et seq. (1985) (the Act).


OVERVIEW: Under the Act, manufacturers of wine coolers that contained less than 14 percent alcohol had to pay a $ .23-per-gallon tax, while manufacturers of spirits paid a $ 2-per-gallon tax. The manufacturer sold a spirit-based, fruit-flavored drink similar to a wine cooler. Although the product contained less than 14 percent alcohol, the Department determined that, because the alcohol in the product was obtained from distillation rather than fermentation, the Act required Federated to pay the $ 2-per-gallon tax. The manufacturer contended that, even though the alcohol was produced by distillation, the total alcoholic percentage in the product was less than 14 percent and the product was a type of wine cooler. The court held that it was the alcohol, not the process from which it was derived, that the Act was meant to regulate. Since the ingredients in the product were nearly identical to that of wine coolers, and since the percentage of alcohol in both was precisely the same, there existed no substantial difference between the two types of beverages. To be consistent with the overall theme of the Act, the product was taxed at the lowest rate, as it posed the least danger of abuse.


OUTCOME: The judgment for the Department was reversed.

Outdoor Media, Inc. v. Bellwood


No. 86-1912


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


162 Ill. App. 3d 1041; 516 N.E.2d 419; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3468; 114 Ill. Dec. 264



October 16, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 18, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Albert Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant village appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment to plaintiff media company in the media company's action concerning village land use restrictions and denied the media company's post-trial motion for rehearing and modification or, alternatively, remand.


OVERVIEW: The media company obtained a state permit, pursuant to the Illinois Highway Advertising Control Act of 1971 (HACA), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121, para. 501 et seq. (1985), to erect a billboard on certain property but was denied a village construction permit. The media company filed a declaratory judgment complaint challenging the ordinance that prohibited the sign. The trial court initially granted the media company summary judgment on the ground that the ordinance was unconstitutional but, upon reconsideration, entered summary judgment on the ground that HACA preempted the ordinance. The trial court then denied the village's motion for rehearing and modification. On appeal, the court held that it was able to sustain the judgment on any grounds warranted by the record and affirmed on the ground that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The court found that the it was not able to say that the village's legislative body would have passed the ordinance in question with an admittedly unconstitutional portion eliminated entirely, and thus it was unable to sever the unconstitutional portion and the entire ordinance was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

791 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Walcher


No. 4-87-0235


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


162 Ill. App. 3d 455; 515 N.E.2d 319; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3391; 113 Ill. Dec. 510



October 15, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. Rodney A. Scott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) for three counts of child pornography, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20.1(a)(1)(vii) (1985), and one count of unlawful possession of cannabis, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 704(d) (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty after he stipulated to the facts. Defendant contended that there was no rational basis for classifying the pornographic photography of a child as a Class 1 felony while punishing intercourse with a child as a Class A misdemeanor, and therefore, the child pornography statute violated due process of law. After a review of the law, the court held that the classification did not constitute a due process violation because there was a rational basis for it. The legislature fashioned the two statutes in question to remedy entirely separate and distinct conduct. Defendant's second argument was that he was not proved guilty of child pornography beyond a reasonable doubt because the photographs depicted mere nudity rather than lewd exhibition of the genitals, as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20.1(a)(1)(vii) (1985). Examination of the photographs refuted any suggestion that mere nudity was depicted. The photographs were obviously intended to excite sexual desire.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed. However, the case was remanded for the issuance of an amended mittimus.

 

792 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Jim M'Lady Olds, Inc. v. Secretary of State


No. 86-1483


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


162 Ill. App. 3d 959; 516 N.E.2d 346; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3459; 114 Ill. Dec. 191



October 13, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner auto dealership appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed a 30-day suspension of its dealership license by respondent, the Secretary of State of Illinois.


OVERVIEW: Based on evidence that the dealer rolled back a car's odometer, the Secretary revoked its dealership license for 30 days. The circuit court affirmed the decision. On appeal, the court concluded that while it was error for the Secretary to base its decision on a provision that had not been charged, the error was harmless in view of the ample evidence of violations of other provisions that were charged. A criminal conviction was not required as a predicate for an offense under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 5--501(a)(3) (1983), and the provision was not unconstitutionally vague. The Secretary 's findings of fact clearly supported the conclusion that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 3--112.1 was violated. The auto had 96,000 miles on the odometer when the dealer received it. The previous owners did not put the odometer reading on the title assignment form. The form submitted by the dealer indicated an odometer reading of 42,095 miles. The false statement was obviously intended to defraud a later purchaser. Thus, the dealer made an untruthful odometer statement with intent to defraud, satisfying the elements for a para. 3--112.1 violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

People v. Galvin


No. 3-87-0011


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


161 Ill. App. 3d 190; 514 N.E.2d 260; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3229; 112 Ill. Dec. 794



October 9, 1987  
October 9, 1987, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to suppress all items seized pursuant to a search.


OVERVIEW: A police officer patrolling an area saw defendant, who was suspected of being involved in criminal activity and had been in the area on the night of a prior burglary, visit a dark house and a closed business. Four police cars surrounded defendant and armed officers ordered him out of his vehicle. An officer then frisked defendant and, upon finding ammunition in his pocket, searched his vehicle and seized a screwdriver and a flashlight. Defendant was charged with theft and possession of burglary tools. The trial court granted his motion to suppress the seized evidence and, on appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the initial stop of defendant for questioning was proper pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 107-14 (1985) of the Illinois Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, which was predicated upon Terry, because the officer reasonably suspected that defendant's conduct may have been indicative of past or prospective criminal activity. The court further held, however, that the frisk was improper pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 108-1.01 (1985) and Terry because the officers admittedly did not feel threatened or believe that defendant was armed and dangerous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, an insurer under an automobile policy, sought a declaration that it had no duty to defend or indemnify its insureds who had been injured while their granddaughter was driving. People v. Du Pree


No. 2-86-0105


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


161 Ill. App. 3d 951; 514 N.E.2d 583; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3322; 112 Ill. Dec. 920



October 7, 1987  
October 7, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. John E. Sype, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) entered upon a jury verdict convicting defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated battery, in part on the ground that he was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. In support of this argument, defendant asserted that the complainant's testimony was disjointed and inconsistent. Affirming, the court stated that the inconsistencies did not detract from the reasonableness of complainant's story. The majority of the inconsistencies relied on by defendant were minor and collateral. Furthermore, the remaining inconsistencies regarding when a knife was produced by defendant and where and how the complainant was injured involved collateral matters relating to how the incident occurred. They did not call into question the identity of the attacker or whether the complainant was in fact sexually assaulted and hit on the head with a deadly weapon. In this regard, the complainant's statements immediately after the incident and her testimony at trial were consistent. While the inconsistencies that developed at trial affected the complainant's credibility, they did not sufficiently detract from the reasonableness of her testimony to render it unclear and unconvincing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Olsen


No. 2-86-0250


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


161 Ill. App. 3d 945; 514 N.E.2d 233; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3321; 112 Ill. Dec. 767



October 2, 1987  
October 2, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Lawrence D. Inglis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) wherein he was convicted of two counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault, two counts of aggravated battery, and one count of armed violence and was sentenced to concurrent extended terms of imprisonment of 50 years for each aggravated sexual assault conviction, 10 years for each aggravated battery conviction, and 14 years for the armed violence conviction.


OVERVIEW: The victim testified that after she refused defendant's request to have sexual intercourse, he struck her eight or nine times with a pair of numchucks, and that she then consented to intercourse because she feared that he would kill her, and that afterward, when she refused to help him find the numchucks, he kicked her repeatedly in the head. The court rejected defendant's arguments that the criminal sexual assault statutes, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 12-14(a)(1), (a)(2) (1985), were vague and overbroad and that a demonstration of the use of numchucks was irrelevant and prejudicial. The court agreed that defendant's multiple convictions arising from a single act of sexual penetration by use of force could not stand because of the one-act-one-crime rule. The court vacated the convictions and sentences imposed for committing a criminal sexual assault by the display of a dangerous weapon, aggravated battery, and armed violence. Because the court could not determine whether the other convictions influenced the trial judge in imposing sentence for the remaining conviction of aggravated criminal sexual assault, the court found that the sentence should be reconsidered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault imposed under count III of the indictment, vacated the sentence, and remanded for a new sentencing hearing as to that offense. The court vacated the convictions and sentences imposed for the offenses charged in counts II, IV, V and VI of the indictment.

 

797 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Porter v. Klein Constr. Co.


No. 84-0448


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


162 Ill. App. 3d 1; 515 N.E.2d 821; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3331; 113 Ill. Dec. 836



September 30, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Charles Freeman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administrator appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion of appellees, wife and children of the deceased, to strike the administrator's petition to vacate a settlement. The administrator contended that she was a next of kin under the Wrongful Death Act (Act) (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 70, para. 2 (1985), even though her son was also survived by a wife and child.


OVERVIEW: The administrator and mother of the deceased claimed that she was a next of kin of the deceased within the meaning of the Wrongful Death Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 70, para. 2 (1985), even though her son was also survived by a wife and child. Her son had died as a result of injuries sustained. Legal proceedings were instituted and during trial the opposing parties settled the claims. When the administrator filed a motion alleging that she was the next of kin, the wife and children of the deceased filed a motion to strike on the ground that the administrator lacked standing. The opposing parties asserted the same ground for affirmance. The trial court granted the motion to strike. Upon appeal, the court affirmed and stated that recovery under the Act was limited to those beneficiaries clearly described in the statute. The beneficiaries as defined by the Act were the surviving spouse and next of kin. Parents were not the next of kin when a decedent left children. The reason was so that the distribution was based on the actual dependency of the spouse and next of kin. The court held that the trial court properly dismissed the administrator's petition to vacate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of a motion filed by the wife and children of the deceased, to strike the administrator's petition to vacate the settlement. The court held that the petition was properly dismissed because the administrator, the mother of the deceased, lacked standing and was not a next of kin and was not a beneficiary to the distributions of the settlement.

 

798 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Outlaw v. O'Leary


No. 3-86-0854


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


161 Ill. App. 3d 218; 514 N.E.2d 208; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3234; 112 Ill. Dec. 742



September 28, 1987  
September 28, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Herman S. Haase, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus after the Illinois Prisoner Review Board (board) denied him parole. Respondents, warden and chairman of the board, filed a motion to dismiss the petition pursuant to Ill. Code Civ. P. § 2-619, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-619 (1985) for failure to state a claim, which was granted by the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois). The inmate sought review.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's habeas corpus petition was dismissed. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that a motion to dismiss and an answer were distinct actions, and the filing of a motion to dismiss did not preclude later filing an answer. Nor did, filing an answer did not preclude later filing a motion to dismiss. This was clear from Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-610, 2-619(d) (1985). The mere fact that the motion to dismiss did not deny the allegations of the inmate's complaint did not automatically constitute admission of the allegations in the complaint, thereby entitling him to the relief he requested. Further, the court rejected the inmate's claim that the parole provisions of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1003-3-5(c)(2) (1985) were unconstitutional because they established a deterrent criterion, while Ill. Const. of 1970, art. I, § 11 mandated a rehabilitative criterion. There was also no showing that the inmate was unconstitutionally disadvantaged by the fact that good conduct credit under § 3-6-3(a)(3) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1003-6-3(a), was limited to 90 days by statutory amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

799 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Raymond W. Wineblad, P.A. v. Department of Registration & Education


No. 85-123


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


161 Ill. App. 3d 827; 515 N.E.2d 705; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3309; 113 Ill. Dec. 720



September 28, 1987  
September 28, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur C. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff physician's assistants sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant Department of Registration and Education's (department) motion for summary judgment in the physician's assistants' action for declaratory and injunctive relief against the department that alleged that an amendment to the statutory licensing requirements was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The legislature amended the Physician's Assistants Practice Act to require physician's assistants to hold a valid certificate issued by the National Commission on Certification of Physician's Assistants. The trial court had determined that there had been no violation of the physician's assistants' constitutional rights where retroactive application of the rule requiring the certification was reasonably related to the public health, safety, and welfare. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the state could have changed the requirements for the issuance or retention of an occupational license so long as the requirement bore some reasonable relationship to the legitimate interest of securing the public health, safety, and welfare. The state had a compelling interest in the practice of professions within its boundaries. The court decided that the classification of the physician's assistants was rationally related to the state's objectives and therefore there was no equal protection violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment granted in favor of the department in the physician's assistants' action for declaratory and injunctive relief that alleged that an amendment to the licensing requirement was unconstitutional.

 

800 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tomlianovich


No. 3-87-0032


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


161 Ill. App. 3d 241; 514 N.E.2d 203; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3239; 112 Ill. Dec. 737



September 25, 1987  
September 25, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Fulton County; the Hon. Charles H. Wilhelm, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Fulton County (Illinois), which convicted her of cruelty to children under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 2368 (1985) and sentenced her to two years of probation, with the conditions that she pay a fine and costs, continue mental health counseling, and cooperate with the Department of Children and Family Services.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's trial for abuse of her son, a physician testified that defendant's 11-year-old son' buttocks were severely bruised to the point of hematoma and that he had never seen a condition so severe. Defendant's son testified that his stepfather, a co-defendant, had hit him approximately 20 times with a wooden paddle. Defendant claimed that the stepfather had not spanked her son, but that she had done it with a wooden paddle only five or six times. The stepfather was acquitted, but defendant was convicted of cruelty to children, and sentenced to probation, with conditions. On appeal, defendant contended that she was denied equal protection and due process rights because had she committed the more serious offense of aggravated battery to a child and been charged under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-4..3(a) (1985), she would have been eligible to have her felony conviction erased, but by her cruelty to child conviction she had to suffer the stigma of a felony conviction. The court affirmed, concluding that equal protection and due process were not denied by the fact that the same conduct could be the basis for charging different offenses carrying different penalties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for cruelty to children and her sentence.
